Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
5 min
The Obligation to Study Usul al-Fiqh: Communal Duty
States the legal obligation of studying usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on studying Usul al-Fiqh and explain the difference between fard 'ayn and fard kifayah.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is a communal shield, not an individual burden.

This lesson addresses a foundational question: is every Muslim personally required to study the methodology of fiqh? The Hanafi tradition provides a clear answer that balances collective responsibility with individual capacity. Understanding this ruling helps us appreciate the role of specialized scholars in preserving Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the ruling
The passage states: 'Acquiring Usul al-Fiqh is fard kifayah.' Identify the key term 'fard kifayah'.
2
Define fard kifayah
Fard kifayah means a communal obligation: if sufficient members of the community fulfill it, the rest are absolved. If no one undertakes it, the entire community sins.
Contrast with fard 'ayn, which every individual must perform personally.
3
Apply to Usul al-Fiqh
Mastering the principles of jurisprudence is necessary for deriving rulings. Not everyone needs to become a mujtahid, but the community must ensure that some scholars attain this knowledge.
This ruling underscores the importance of specialized Islamic scholarship.
4
Reflect on consequences
If all Muslims abandoned the study of Usul al-Fiqh, the entire community would be sinful. If a qualified group exists, the obligation is fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵) اصول فقہ کا حکم: اصول فقہ کا حاصل کرنا فرض علی الکفایہ ہے۔
(5) The ruling on Usul al-Fiqh: Acquiring Usul al-Fiqh is a communal obligation (fard kifayah).
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage states a short but fundamental ruling: studying Usul al-Fiqh is fard kifayah (communal obligation). This means that as long as a sufficient number of scholars master it, the obligation is lifted from the rest of the community. It is not fard 'ayn (individual obligation) on every Muslim, but the community as a whole must ensure the methodology of fiqh is preserved. This ruling underscores the importance of Usul al-Fiqh as the theoretical foundation for deriving Islamic law.

Key Terms
فرض علی الکفایہ (fard 'ala al-kifayah): A communal obligation; if some members of the community fulfill it, the rest are absolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of obligation is studying Usul al-Fiqh according to the text?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Fard kifayah
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Studying Usul al-Fiqh is a communal duty (fard kifayah), ensuring the preservation of Islamic legal methodology.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

The Rule: Haqiqah and Majaz Cannot Combine
States the rule and provides a case from Imam Muhammad's Jami' al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that haqiqah and majaz cannot be intended simultaneously from a single word, and derive the correct interpretation of bequests involving the word mawla.

Core Idea
Haqiqah and majaz cannot coexist in one utterance: when the literal meaning is intended, the figurative is automatically void.

This usul rule clarifies a fundamental principle of Hanafi legal interpretation: a single word cannot carry both its literal and figurative intended meanings at the same time. The passage presents the rule, illustrates it with the analogy of ownership vs. borrowing, and then applies it to a concrete case from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Kabir involving the word mawla. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly interpreting ambiguous terms in legal documents.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the core principle: haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined in a single utterance intended at the same time.
The author compares it to a garment that cannot be both owned and borrowed.
2
Understand the word mawla
Recognize that mawla has multiple literal meanings (manumitter and freed slave) and a figurative meaning (mawla of a mawla).
Context determines which literal meaning applies.
3
Analyze the case context
The testator is an Arab, so he cannot have a manumitter. Therefore, the literal meaning of 'mawali' here is his own freed slave, not his manumitters.
This eliminates one literal possibility.
4
Apply the rule to the case
Since the literal meaning (his freed slave) is intended by context, the figurative meaning (freed slave of his freed slave) becomes void. Thus only the one freed slave inherits.
The bequest to 'mawali' is interpreted as singular due to inheritance rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: حقیقت اور مجاز کا حکم ان دونوں کے اجتماع کا محال ہونا ہے، مراد بن کر ایک ہی لفظ سے ، جیسا کہ محال ہے کہ ایک ہی کپڑا پہننے والے پر ملکیت کا اور عاریت کا ہوا ایک ہی وقت میں ۔
شریح:- مصنف حقیقت اور مجاز کا حکم بیان فرما ر ہے کہ ایک لفظ بول کر ایک ہی وقت میں اس کے حقیقی معنی بھی مراد لئے جائے اور اس کے مجازی معنی بھی مراد لئے جائے یہ محال ہے، بلکہ ایک وقت میں یا تو لفظ کے حقیقی معنی مراد ہوں گے یا مجازی معنی ، دونوں معنی ایک وقت میں مراد لینا صحیح نہیں ہے، جیسے ایک آدمی کے بدن پر کپڑا ہو تو وہ یا تو ملکیت کا ہوگا یا عاریت کا ، ایک ہی وقت میں ملکیت کا بھی ہو اور عاریت کا بھی ہو، ایسا نہیں ہوسکتا ہے، پس حقیقی معنی مملوک کے مانند ہے اور مجازی معنی عاریت کے درجہ میں ہے۔
وَلِهَذَا قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي الْجَامِعِ لَوْاَنَّ عَرَبِيَا لَا وَلَاءَ عَلَيْهِ أَوْصَى بِثُلُثِ مَالِهِ لِمَوَالِيْهِ وَلَهُ مُعْتَقٌ وَاحِدٌ فَاسْتَحَقَّ النِّصْفَ كَانَ النِّصْفُ الْبَاقِي مَرْدُودًا إِلَى الْوَرَثَةِ وَلَا يَكُونُ لِمَوَالِي مَوْلَاهُ لِاَنَّ الْحَقِيقَة أريدَتْ بِهَذَا اللَّفْظِ فَبَطَلَ الْمَجَاز
ترجمہ:۔ اسی وجہ سے امام محمد نے جامع کبیر میں فرمایا کہ اگر کسی عربی نے جس پر ولاء نہ ہو اپنے موالی کے لئے اپنے تہائی مال کی وصیت کی اور اس کا ایک ہی معتق ( آزاد کیا ہوا غلام ) ہے، تو تہائی کے آدھے کا وہ مستحق ہوگا، اور تہائی کا باقی آدھا اس عربی کے وارثوں کی طرف لوٹا دیا جائے گا، اور اس کے مولی کے موالی کے لئے نہیں ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ اس لفظ سے جب حقیقت مراد لے لی گئی تو مجاز باطل ہو گیا۔
تشریح :۔ جب حقیقت اور مجاز کا حکم معلوم ہو گیا کہ دونوں ایک ساتھ جمع نہیں ہو سکتے تو مصنف اس پر ایک مسئلہ متفرع کر رہے ہیں ۔ پہلے یہ سمجھ لیں کہ مولی کا لفظ معتق ( آزاد کرنے والا ) اور معتق ( آزادشدہ ) دونوں کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے، اس لفظ کے حقیقی معنی ہے اس کا معتق اور معتق یعنی وہ شخص جس نے اس کو آزاد کیا ہے یا جس کو خود اس نے آزاد کیا ہے، یہ تو حقیقی معنی ہوئے اور معتق کا معتق یا معتق کا معتق مجازی معنی ہوئے۔ دوسری بات یہ سمجھ لیں کہ غلام کے مال میں آزاد کرنے والے کا جو حق ہوتا ہے، غلام کے مرنے کے بعد وہ ولاء کہلاتا ہے۔ اور یہ بھی سمجھ لیں کہ عربی حر الاصل ہوتا ہے، عربوں میں رقیت نہیں ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ عربوں میں دوہی باتیں تھیں یا اسلام یا قتل، پس عرب میں غلامی نہیں ہوتی ہے، تو ولاء بھی نہیں ہوگی، لہذا مصنف کی عبارت میں عربیا کے بعد لا ولا علیہ تاکید کے لئے ہے۔
اب عبارت سمجھیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی عربی نے اپنے موالی کے لئے تہائی مال کی وصیت کی ، تو یہاں موالی کے معنی معتق ( آزاد کردہ غلام) ہے، یہاں معتق مراد نہیں ہو سکتا ہے، کیوں کہ عربوں میں غلامی نہیں ہوسکتی ہے، لہذا اس کا کوئی معتق نہیں ہوگا، تو یہاں مولی کا معنی معتق معین ہو گئے ، اب حقیقی معنی اس کا خود کا آزاد کردہ غلام، اور مجازی معنی غلاموں کے غلام ، اور اس کا ایک ہی معتق ہے اور اس کے معتق کے معتق بہت ہیں ، لہذا اس کے حقیقی معنی اس کا خود کا معتق جب مراد لے لیا تو غلاموں کے غلام کے لئے وصیت نہیں ہوگی ، لہذا اس کے معتق کو ثلث کا آدھا دیکر باقی موصی کے وارثوں کو دے دیا جائے گا۔
سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ اس نے موالی جمع کا صیغہ استعمال کیا ہے اور اس کے کم سے کم تین فرد ہیں ، تو اس کو ثلث کا تیسرا حصہ دینا چاہیے نہ کہ آدھا فما الجواب
جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ کی بات بالکل صحیح ہے مگر میراث اور وصیت میں دو کوجمع کا حکم دیا جاتا ہے ،لہذا ایک جمع کا نصف شمار ہوگا ، اس لئے اس کو ثلث کا آدھا ملے گا۔
Translation: The ruling of haqiqah (literal meaning) and majaz (figurative meaning) is that it is impossible to intend both simultaneously from a single word, just as it is impossible for a single garment on a wearer to be both owned and borrowed at the same time. Explanation: The author states the ruling of haqiqah and majaz: when one utters a single word and intends both its literal meaning and its figurative meaning at the same time, this is impossible. Rather, at one time, either the literal meaning or the figurative meaning will be intended; intending both meanings at the same time is not valid. For example, if a man has a garment on his body, it is either owned or borrowed; it cannot be both owned and borrowed at the same time. So the literal meaning is like owned property, and the figurative meaning is like a borrowed item. And for this reason, Muhammad said in al-Jami‘: If an Arab who has no wala’ over him bequeaths one-third of his property to his mawali, and he has only one freed slave, then that slave is entitled to half of that third; the remaining half of the third is returned to the testator's heirs, and it is not given to the mawali of his mawla, because when the literal meaning was intended by this word, the figurative meaning becomes void. Translation: For this reason, Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami‘ al-Kabir: If an Arab who has no wala’ over him bequeaths one-third of his property to his mawali, and he has only one freed slave (mu‘tiq/an), then that freed slave is entitled to half of that third, and the remaining half of that third is returned to the Arab's heirs, and it will not go to the mawali of his mawla, because when the literal meaning was intended by this word, the figurative meaning became void. Elaboration: When the ruling of haqiqah and majaz is known – that they cannot be combined – the author derives a subsidiary case. First, understand that the word mawla is used for both the manumitter (mu‘tiq) and the freed slave (mu‘taq). Its literal meaning is one's own manumitter or freed slave – that is, the person who freed him or the person he freed. These are the literal meanings. And the mawla of one's mawla (i.e., the mawla of one's freed slave) is the figurative meaning. Second, understand that the right that the manumitter has over the slave's property after the slave's death is called wala’. Also understand that an Arab is free-born; among Arabs slavery does not occur, because among the Arabs there were only two outcomes: Islam or death. So among Arabs slavery does not exist, so wala’ also does not exist. Hence, in the author's phrase 'an Arab who has no wala’ over him' is for emphasis. Now understand the text: He says that an Arab bequeathed one-third of his property to his mawali. Here mawali means his freed slaves (mu‘taq). It cannot mean his manumitters (mu‘tiqun) because among Arabs slavery does not occur, so he has no manumitter. Thus here the meaning of mawla is determined to be the freed slave. Now, the literal meaning is his own freed slave, and the figurative meaning is the freed slaves of his freed slave. He has one freed slave, but that freed slave has many freed slaves. So when the literal meaning – his own freed slave – is intended, the bequest does not go to the freed slaves of his freed slave. Therefore, his freed slave is given half of the third, and the remaining half is given to the testator's heirs. A question arises: He used the plural form mawali, which requires at least three individuals, so he should be given one-third of the third, not half. What is the answer? The answer is that what you say is correct, but in inheritance and bequest, two is given the ruling of a plural (jam‘), so one (i.e., the single freed slave) is counted as half of a plural. Therefore, he receives half of the third.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule followed by its application. The author states the fundamental principle: haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined in a single utterance intended at the same time. He illustrates with the analogy of a garment: it cannot be owned and borrowed simultaneously. The commentary then quotes a case from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami‘ al-Kabir to demonstrate the principle. In the case, an Arab (whose status means he cannot have a manumitter because slavery among Arabs is impossible) bequeaths one-third of his property to his mawali (plural of mawla). The word mawla can mean either manumitter or freed slave literally, and also can refer figuratively to the mawla of one's mawla. Since the testator is an Arab, he has no manumitter; thus the literal meaning here is his own freed slave. Therefore, only his one freed slave benefits, receiving half the one-third (because in inheritance law, two is considered a plural, so one counts as half). The figurative meaning – the freed slaves of his freed slave – is invalid because the literal meaning precludes it. This case clearly shows that when a word is used in its literal sense, any figurative application is void.

Key Terms
حقیقت (haqiqah): The literal, original meaning of a word with which it was coined.
مجاز (majaz): The figurative meaning of a word, used for something other than its original meaning due to a relationship and a contextual indicator (qarinah).
مولی (mawla): A word used for both the manumitter (mu'tiq) and the freed slave (mu'taq), literally; also figuratively for other relationships like the mawla of a mawla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Arab testator's bequest to 'mawali' only go to his one freed slave and not to that freed slave's freed slaves?
A) Because the Arab has no wala' over him, so the term 'mawali' cannot refer to freed slaves.
B) Because the literal meaning of 'mawali' is his own freed slave, and once literal is intended, figurative is void.
C) Because the Arab only has one freed slave, so he cannot bequeath to more than one.
D) Because in inheritance, the plural 'mawali' is understood as two, so only half is given.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when the literal meaning of a word is determined by context, the figurative meaning becomes void; the two cannot coexist.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Deriving Talaq Raj'i from Kinayah Words: Usul Analysis
Analyzing three kinayah words for talaq raj'i using usul principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul principles (intention, implication, metaphor) to kinayah words and derive the ruling of talaq raj'i for the three specific words.

Core Idea
Three kinayah words produce talaq raj'i because their effect (iddah) is uniquely linked to divorce, allowing reverse metaphor and implication.

In Hanafi fiqh, most kinayah words for divorce produce talaq bain (irrevocable divorce). However, three words—i'taddi, istabri'i, and anti wahidah—are exceptions, yielding talaq raj'i (revocable divorce) when intention is present. This lesson unpacks the usul reasoning behind this exception, focusing on how intention removes ambiguity and how the exclusive cause-effect relationship between divorce and iddah permits a unique metaphorical usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exceptions
Recall that most kinayah words produce talaq bain. The passage lists three exceptions: i'taddi, istabri'i, anti wahidah. Understand that these words require intention and produce talaq raj'i.
This is the starting point: knowing the default rule helps highlight the exceptional case.
2
Analyze 'i'taddi' linguistically and contextually
Examine its literal meaning (counting) and why it has no direct effect on marriage. Then consider two contexts: if the wife is consummated (the command implies divorce due to iddah requirements) and if not consummated (the word is used metaphorically).
The literal meaning is irrelevant to divorce, so intention is needed. The contextual clue (consummation) triggers different usul mechanisms.
3
Understand the usul principle of implication (iqtiḍāʾ)
For a consummated wife, the command to observe iddah only makes sense if divorce has occurred. Thus, the word implies divorce by necessity (iqtiḍāʾ). This is a type of dalalah (indication) that yields a revocable divorce.
Implication is not explicit wording but a logical necessity derived from the command.
4
Understand the usul principle of metaphor (istiʿārah)
For a non-consummated wife, there is no iddah. The word 'i'taddi' is then taken as a metaphor from effect (iddah) to cause (divorce). This is valid only because iddah is exclusively caused by divorce—a unique link that strengthens the metaphor.
This reverses the usual direction (cause→effect) but is allowed due to exclusivity.
5
Apply the same analysis to 'istabri'i'
Analyze 'istabri'i' (purity your womb) similarly: intention for divorce, then check if the wife is consummated or not. The same implication/metaphor mechanisms apply, supported by the hadith of Sawdah where the Prophet said 'i'taddi' and then revoked the divorce.
The hadith directly supports that these words can initiate a revocable divorce.
6
Analyze 'anti wahidah'
This phrase is ambiguous: it could mean 'you are divorced once' or 'you are one woman'. Intention resolves the ambiguity, making it a clear indication of a single revocable divorce.
No implication or metaphor needed; intention alone makes it explicit.
7
Synthesize the usul framework
Summarize: Intention removes ambiguity; for consummated wives, implication (iqtiḍāʾ) operates; for non-consummated, reverse metaphor (istiʿārah) operates due to exclusivity. The result is always talaq raj'i.
This shows how Hanafi usul integrates linguistic analysis with contextual factors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
اِلَّافِى قَوْلِ الرَّجُلِ اِعْتَدِى لِاَنَّ حَقِيْقَتَهُ لِلْحِسَابِ وَلَا أَثَرَ لِذْلِكَ فِي النِّكَاح وَالْإِعْتَدَادُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يُرَادَ بِهِ مَايُعَدُّ مِنْ غَيْرِ الْأَقْرَاءِ فَإِذَانَوَى الْأَقْرَاءَ وَزَالَ الْإِبْهَامُ بِالنِّيَّةِ وَجَبَ بِهِ الطَّلَاقُ بَعْدَ الدُّخُولِ  ِاقْتِضَاء وَقَبْلَ الدُّخُولِ جُعِلَ مُسْتَعَارًا مَحْضَّاعَنِ الطَّلَاقِ لِأَنَّهُ سَبَبُهُ فَاسْتُعِيْرَ الْحُكْمْ لِسَبَبِهِ
ترجمہ :۔ مگر مرد کے قول اعقدی میں اس لئے کہ اس قول کی حقیقت حساب کے لئے ہے اور حساب کا کوئی اثر (دخل ) نہیں ہے نکاح ختم کرنے میں اور اعتداد احتمال رکھتا ہے کہ اس سے مراد لی جائے وہ چیز جو شمار کی جاتی ہے حیض کے علاوہ ، پس جب اس نے حیض کی نیت کی اور ابہام زائل ہو گیا نیت سے، تو ثابت ہو جا ئیگی اس سے طلاق دخول کے بعد اقتضاء اور دخول سے پہلے، اس قول کو بنایا جائے گا مستعار محض طلاق سے ، اس لئے کہ طلاق اعتداد کا سبب ہے ، پس حکم ( مسبب ) کا استعارہ کیا گیا اس کے سبب کے لئے ۔
تشریح:- مصنف اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تمام الفاظ کنایات سے طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی ہے ، مگر تین الفاظ ایسے ہیں کہ ان کے کنایہ ہونے کے باوجود اور ان میں نیت کی حاجت ہونے کے باوجود ان سے ایک طلاق رجعی پڑتی ہے، وہ تین لفظ یہ ہیں، اعتدى، استبرئي، انت واحدة -
پہلا لفظ اعتدی ہے ،اس کے معنی ہیں شمار کرنا، اور اس حقیقی معنی کو قطع نکاح میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے جیسے پہلے الفاظ بائن حرام وغیرہ کے معانی کو دخل تھا، بہر حال اعتدی سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی ، اس لئے کہ اعتدی کے معنی ہیں شمار کرنا، تو اس میں احتمال اور ابہام ہے کہ کیا شمار کرے؟ پیسے شمار کرے، اللہ کی نعمتیں شمار کرے، یا حیض شمار کرے ، جب شوہر نے نیت کی کہ حیض شمار کرے تو ابہام دور ہو گیا، اب دیکھیں گے کہ عورت مدخول بھا ہے یا غیر مدخول بھا؟ اگر مدخول بھا ہے یعنی شوہر اس سے دخول کر چکا ہے اور اس کو کہ رہا ہے کہ عدت گزارنے کے لئے حیض شمار کر ، تو اس سے پہلے اقتضاء طلاق کو مقدر مانا جائے گا، کیونکہ بغیر طلاق کے عدت گزارنا نہیں ہوتا ہے، تو گویا شوہر نے یوں کہا میں نے طلاق دی تو عدت گزار، اور جب طلاق کو مقدر مانا ، جو صریح لفظ ہے، تو اس سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔ اور اگر عورت غیر مدخول بھا ہے ، تو اس پر عدت نہیں ہے، لہذا غیر مدخول بھا میں اعتدی سے مجاز اطلاق مراد لینگے، کیونکہ عدت گزارنا اور طلاق دونوں میں سبیت کا علاقہ ہے ، طلاق سبب ہے اور عدت گزارنا مسبب ہے تو یہاں مسبب بولکر سبب مراد لیا، لہذا اس سے بھی طلاق رجعی پڑے گی۔ مگر اس پر یہ سوال پیدا ہو گا کہ پہلے تو آپ نے بتایا تھا کہ سبب اور مسبب میں اتصال کمزور ہوتا ہے، تو استعارہ جانبین سے درست نہیں ہے، بلکہ ایک طرف سے استعارہ درست ہے، سبب بولکر مسبب مراد لینا درست ہے مگر مسبب بولکر سبب مراد لینا درست نہیں ہے تو یہاں آپ نے کیسے مسبب بولکر سبب مراد لیا ؟
،،
جواب یہ ہے کہ وہ بات عام حالات میں تھی لیکن اگر مسبب ایسا ہے جو سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہے تو استعارہ ت ہے اور یہاں مسبب یعنی عدت گزارنا سبب یعنی طلاق کے ساتھ خاص ہے بغیر طلاق کے عدت گزارنا نہیں ہوتا ہے، لہذا استعارہ درست ہے جیسے انی ارانی اعصر خمرا یہاں خمر سے مراد انگور ہے، انگور سبب ہے اور خمر مسبب ہے، یہاں بھی مسبب بولکر سبب مراد لیا کیونکہ مسبب سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہے،شراب بغیر انگور کے نہیں بنتی ہے۔
وَكَذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ إِسْتَبْرِئِيْ رَحِمَكِ وَقَدْ جَاءَتْ بِهِ السُّنَّةُ أَن النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ لِسَوْدَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا إِعْتَدِئُ ثُمَّ رَاجَعَهَا وَكَذَلِكَ أَنْتِ وَاحِدَةٌ يَحْتَمِلُ نَعْنَّا لِلطَّلَقَةِ وَيَحْتَمِلُ صِفَةً لِلْمَرْأَةِ فَإِذَازَالَ الْإِبْهَامُ بِالنِّيَةِ كَانَ دَلَالَةً عَلَى الصَّرِيحَ لَا عَامِلًا بِمُوْجَبِهِ
ترجمہ :۔ اور ایسے ہی شوہر کا قول " استبرئی رحمک ، اور تحقیق کہ اس کے بارے میں حدیث وارد ہوئی ہے کہ نبی کریم صلی یا پیام نے حضرت سودہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے فرمایا اعتدی پھر آپ صلی اینم نے ان سے رجوع فرما لیا ،اور ایسے ہی انت واحدة “ ہے ، یہ لفظ احتمال رکھتا ہے طلقہ کی صفت کا ، اور احتمال رکھتا ہے عورت کی صفت کا ، پس جب نیت سے ابہام دور ہو گیا تو یہ لفظ دلیل ہو گا طلاق صریح پر نہ کہ عمل کرنے والا اپنے منہ
تشریح :۔ دوسرا کنائی لفظ جس سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہوتی ہے، استبرئی رحمک ہے،اس کے معنی ہیں تو اپنے رحم کو پاک کر لے ، اس میں دو احتمال ہے (۱) تو بچہ کے لئے رحم پاک کر یعنی حیض سے رحم پاک کر ، تا کہ میں وطی کروں اور بچہ کی امید ہو، (۲) دوسرے شوہر کے لئے رحم پاک کرے تو اس میں ابہام آگیا، اب نیت کی ضرورت پڑے گی ، جب شوہر نے نیت کر لی کہ دوسرے شوہر کے لئے رحم پاک کرنا میری مراد ہے، تو یہاں بھی وہی دو صورتیں ہوں گی، مدخول بھا اور غیر مدخول بھا جو اعتدی میں تھی بالکل وہی تقریر یہاں بھی ہے کہ اگر عورت مدخول بھا ہے تو استبرکی سے پہلی طلاق کو مقدر مانا جائے گا، تو گو یا شوہر نے یوں کہا کہ میں نے تجھے طلاق دی تو دوسرے شوہر کے لیے رحم پاک کر ، اور جب طلاق کو مقدر مانا جو صریح لفظ ہے تو طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی اور اگر عورت غیر مدخول بھا ہے تو استبرائی سے مجاز اطلاق مراد لیں گے ، تو یہاں بھی طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔ مصنف سے ” اعتدی“ سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہونے پر دلیل میں ایک حدیث لائے کہ ایک مرتبہ
مقتضی پر۔
Al-Faiz al-Hijazi: Urdu commentary on Al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Except in the man's saying 'i'taddi' because its literal meaning is for counting, and that has no effect in ending marriage. And 'i'tidad' could mean what is counted besides menstruation. So if he intends menstruation, the ambiguity is removed by intention, then divorce becomes obligatory after intercourse by implication, and before intercourse it is considered a pure metaphor for divorce because it is its cause, so the ruling (effect) is lent to its cause. The author states: All kinayah words produce irrevocable divorce, but three words, despite being kinayah and requiring intention, produce one revocable divorce: i'taddi, istabri'i, anti wahidah. First word: i'taddi (count). Its literal meaning has no impact on dissolving marriage. It produces talaq raj'i because it implies counting, and there is ambiguity. When the husband intends menstruation, ambiguity is removed. If the wife is consummated, divorce is implied (she cannot observe iddah without divorce); he is deemed to have said 'I divorce you, so observe iddah.' Since divorce is a explicit word, talaq raj'i occurs. If not consummated, since she has no iddah, the word is used metaphorically meaning divorce (cause) from the effect (iddah). This is valid because iddah is specific to divorce. Similarly, the hadith of Sawdah. The word 'anti wahidah' can describe the divorce or the woman. When ambiguity is removed by intention, it indicates explicit divorce, not acting on its literal meaning. The second kinayah word is 'istabri'i rahimaki' (purify your womb). It has two possibilities: purify for pregnancy or for another husband. With intention, it also produces talaq raj'i by implication or metaphor. The author cites a hadith for i'taddi... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage from Al-Faiz al-Hijazi, a commentary on Al-Husami, analyzes three kinayah words that, unlike other kinayah words which produce talaq bain, yield talaq raj'i when intention is present. The author explains each word's linguistic properties and how the legal ruling is derived. For i'taddi (count), its literal meaning (counting numbers) has no connection to divorce, so it requires intention. If the wife is consummated, the command to count 'iddah implies that divorce has already occurred; thus the word is treated as a declaration of divorce by implication (qarinah). If not consummated, the word is used metaphorically (isti'arah) from effect to cause: 'iddah (the effect) is mentioned but divorce (the cause) is intended. This is valid because 'iddah is specific to divorce, unlike general cause-effect relationships where such reverse metaphor is weak. The author then discusses istabri'i (purify your womb), which similarly requires intention and can imply divorce by implication or metaphor. Finally, anti wahidah (you are one) is ambiguous—it could mean 'you are divorced once' or 'you are one woman.' With intention, it indicates the explicit meaning of divorce. The passage also cites the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told Sawdah 'i'taddi' and then took her back, supporting that i'taddi produces revocable divorce. The discussion demonstrates the Hanafi usul principle that kinayah can produce explicit legal effects through intention and contextual reading, especially when a metaphorical relationship (cause-effect) is exclusive.

Key Terms
اعتدي (i'taddi): A kinayah word meaning 'count' (your 'iddah), which with intention produces talaq raj'i.
استبرئي (istabri'i): A kinayah word meaning 'purify your womb', which with intention produces talaq raj'i.
انت واحدة (anti wahidah): A kinayah phrase meaning 'you are one', ambiguous between one divorce and describing the woman; intention clarifies.
كناية (kinayah): A word that implies divorce indirectly, requiring intention for legal effect.
استعارة (isti'arah): Metaphorical use of a word, here from effect (iddah) to cause (divorce), valid when cause and effect are uniquely linked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following words, when intended for divorce, produces talaq raj'i rather than talaq bain according to the Hanafi school?
A) i'taddi
B) anti wahidah
C) istabri'i
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school derives talaq raj'i from three specific kinayah words by applying intention and either implication or reverse metaphor, the latter valid only when the effect is uniquely linked to the cause.

Nafs al-Wujub vs Wujub al-Ada: Application to Kaffarah
Explaining Hanafi distinction between inherent obligation and obligation to pay for mali vs badani and its effect on kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada to determine the timing of obligation for bodily vs wealth expiation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
For bodily obligations, nafs al-wujub is identical to wujub al-ada; for wealth, they separate — but in kaffarah, both bind only after hanth.

This passage tackles a subtle but critical distinction in Hanafi usul: the difference between the essence of an obligation (nafs al-wujub) and the obligation to perform it at a specific time (wujub al-ada). For wealth-based duties, these can diverge, but for bodily acts they are inseparable. The author applies this to the expiation (kaffarah) for breaking an oath, a point of contention with the Shafi'i school. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping Hanafi reasoning on timing of obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two concepts
From the passage, define nafs al-wujub (the essence of obligation) and wujub al-ada (the obligation to pay/perform at a specific time). Note how they relate to the timing of the duty.
These terms are central to Hanafi usul analysis.
2
Analyze separation in wealth obligations
The passage gives examples (zakat before the year ends, deferred payment before term) where nafs al-wujub is established but wujub al-ada is delayed. Verify that the essence of obligation exists before payment becomes due.
This shows that for wealth, 'absence of wujub al-ada does not indicate absence of nafs al-wujub'.
3
Contrast with bodily obligations
The passage states that for bodily acts, the two are identical: wujub al-ada is nafs al-wujub. There can be no gap. Explain why this is: bodily actions require immediate performance; you cannot owe a bodily duty without it being due now.
This is a key usul principle in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to the kaffarah dispute
The author applies the distinction to kaffarah. Since the cause of expiation is hanth (breaking the oath) — not the oath itself — both wealth and bodily expiation share the same cause. For bodily kaffarah, the obligation arises only after hanth because nafs al-wujub = wujub al-ada. For wealth kaffarah, even if nafs al-wujub could precede wujub al-ada in other contexts, here the cause (hanth) is the same, so the Hanafis reject giving it before hanth. Contrast with the Shafi'i view that allows wealth expiation beforehand.
The practical result: according to Hanafis, any expiation given before hanth is invalid and must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہو گیا لیکن وجوب ادا ایک مہینہ کے بعد ہوگا، تو یہاں وجوب ادا اور نفس وجوب میں فصل ہوا، اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ مال میں عدم وجوب ادا عدم نفس وجوب پر دلالت نہیں کرتا ہے، یعنی ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ مال کا نفس وجوب تو ثابت ہو جائے اور وجوب ادا ابھی نہ ثابت ہو، اور نفس وجوب ثابت ہو جانے کے بعد واجب کو وجوب ادا کے ثابت ہونے سے پہلے ادا کرنا جائز ہے، جیسے کہ مالک نصاب کے لئے حولان حول سے پہلے زکوۃ ادا کرنا جائز ہے، اور مشتری کے لئے شمن مؤجل کو میعاد پوری ہونے سے پہلے ادا کرنا جائز ہے، لیکن جو بدنی واجب ہے اس میں نفس وجوب اور وجوب ادا میں فصل نہیں ہوسکتا ہے، بلکہ وجوب ادا ہی کا نام نفس وجوب ہے، لہذا کفارہ بدنی میں وجوب ادا حانث ہونے کے بعد ہے تو نفس وجوب بھی حانث ہونے کے بعد ہی ہوگا کیونکہ واجب بدنی میں وجوب ادا ہی نفس وجوب ہے، فلما تاخر الاداء سے مصنف یہی سمجھا رہے ہیں، کہ جب وجوب ادا مؤخر ہو گیا تو نفس وجوب بھی پہلے باقی نہیں رہا بلکہ وہ بھی مؤخر ہو گیا، اور جب مؤخر ہو گیا تو حانث ہونے سے پہلے بدنی کفارہ ادا نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک حانث ہونے سے پہلے کفارہ کالی دے سکتا ہے، کفارہ بدنی نہیں ادا کر سکتا ہے، اور احناف کے نزدیک چونکہ کفارہ کا سبب یمین نہیں ہے بلکہ حانث ہونا ہے تو کفارہ حانث ہونے کے بعد ہی واجب ہوگا ، چاہے کفارہ مالی ہو یا بدنی، اگر کوئی پہلے ادا کر دے تو اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا حانث ہونے کے بعد اعادہ ضروری ہے۔
But the obligation to pay will be after one month. Here there is a separation between the obligation to pay and the essence of obligation. From this it is understood that in wealth, the absence of obligation to pay does not indicate the absence of the essence of obligation. That is, it is possible that the essence of obligation for wealth is established but the obligation to pay is not yet established, and after the essence of obligation is established, it is permissible to pay the obligated before the obligation to pay is established, just as it is permissible for the owner of the nisab to pay zakat before the passage of a year, and for the buyer to pay the deferred price before the term is complete. But in a bodily obligation, there cannot be a separation between the essence of obligation and the obligation to pay; rather, the obligation to pay is itself the essence of obligation. Hence, in bodily expiation, since the obligation to pay is after becoming a traitor, the essence of obligation will also be after becoming a traitor, because in bodily obligations, the obligation to pay is the essence of obligation. Therefore, when the obligation to pay is delayed, the essence of obligation also does not remain before; rather, it is also delayed. And when it is delayed, one cannot give bodily expiation before becoming a traitor. In any case, according to Imam Shafi'i, one can give wealth expiation before becoming a traitor, but not bodily expiation. According to the Hanafis, since the cause of expiation is not the oath but the act of treachery, expiation becomes obligatory only after treachery, whether wealth or bodily. If anyone gives it before, it will not be considered; after treachery, repetition is necessary.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage explains a key usul principle regarding the timing of obligation. The text distinguishes between the essence of obligation (nafs al-wujub) and the obligation to pay (wujub al-ada). For wealth obligations, these two can be separated: the essence of obligation can be established before its payment becomes due, as in zakat before the year's end or deferred payment before the term. However, for bodily obligations, they are identical; the essence of obligation is the obligation to pay. The author applies this to the case of kaffarah (expiation) for breaking an oath. According to the Hanafi school, the cause of kaffarah is the act of breaking the oath (hanth), not the oath itself. Therefore, expiation is only obligatory after hanth. If one gives expiation before hanth, it is invalid and must be repeated. This differs from Imam Shafi'i, who distinguishes between wealth and bodily expiation, allowing wealth expiation before hanth. The passage reaffirms the Hanafi position using rational arguments.

Key Terms
نفس الوجوب (nafs al-wujub): The essence of legal obligation, the existence of the duty itself regardless of when it is due.
وجوب ادا (wujub al-ada): The obligation to pay or perform at a specific time.
حانث (hanth): The act of breaking an oath or failing to fulfill a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view explained in the passage, when does bodily expiation (kaffarah badani) become obligatory?
A) Immediately upon taking the oath.
B) After the passage of one month from the oath.
C) Only after actually breaking the oath (hanth).
D) At the same time as wealth expiation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the cause of kaffarah is the act of breaking the oath, so expiation is only due after hanth, regardless of wealth or bodily nature.

Refuting the Shafi'i Distinction: Financial and Bodily Kaffarah
Refuting a Shafi'i premise on financial vs. bodily obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain and apply the Hanafi position that financial and bodily expiations (kaffarah) cannot be given before their cause, using the analogy (qiyas) based on the nature of rights of Allah.

Core Idea
In rights of Allah, financial obligations are inseparable from their cause, just like bodily ones.

This passage addresses a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the timing of expiations (kaffarah). The Shafi'i school distinguishes between financial and bodily obligations, allowing early payment for financial kaffarah before the triggering act (e.g., breaking an oath). The Hanafi response refutes this, arguing that both types are alike because the right of Allah resides in the act of payment, not the property itself. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping how rights of Allah govern devotional obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Identify the Shafi'i claim that in financial obligations, the essence of obligation (nafs al-wujūb) separates from the obligation of performance (wujūb al-adā'), allowing early payment.
Shafi'i uses this to permit financial kaffarah before breaking the oath (ḥanth).
2
Identify the Hanafi response
Recognize that the Hanafi school denies this separation because in rights of Allāh, the right is the servant's act of giving, not the property itself.
Property is merely a tool (ālah).
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyās)
Understand how the Hanafi position uses an analogy: financial obligations are like bodily obligations because the effective cause (ʿillah) is that both are rights of Allāh where the object is the act of payment.
The ʿillah is shared, so the ruling is the same.
4
Note the exception for rights of people
Recognize that in rights of people (ḥuqūq al-ʿibād), separation is possible because specific property is intended. Since kaffārah is a right of Allāh, the exception does not apply.
This confirms the Hanafi rule for devotional obligations.
5
Conclude the practical effect
Derive that both financial and bodily kaffārah must be delayed until the cause (e.g., breaking the oath) occurs. Neither can be given beforehand.
This is the thamarah al-khilāf (practical consequence).

And the distinction between financial and bodily [expiation] – this is a refutation of the fifth premise. Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, made a distinction between financial and bodily expiation and said that in a financial obligation, the essence of obligation separates from the obligation of performance, so financial expiation can be given before the act of breaking the oath, and in a bodily obligation, the essence of obligation and the obligation of performance are not separated, but both occur together after the act of breaking the oath, therefore bodily expiation before breaking the oath is not permissible. This is false, because in financial obligations, the right of Allah Almighty is not the property itself but the servant's act of payment, since property is merely a tool. So when the right of Allah becomes the servant's act of payment, the financial obligation becomes like the bodily obligation. Just as in bodily obligation the essence of obligation does not separate from the obligation of performance, similarly in financial obligation it also becomes so. Therefore, in both bodily and financial [obligations], the essence of obligation and the obligation of performance will both occur together after the act of breaking the oath, so before breaking the oath neither financial nor bodily expiation can be given. Yes, in rights of people you can separate the essence of obligation from the obligation of performance, because in the rights of people specific property is intended, but in rights of Allah this separation cannot be made. And expiation is from the rights of Allah, so this distinction cannot be made in it.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Shafi'i argument. The author explains that the Shafi'i view distinguishes between financial and bodily expiations, claiming that in financial obligations the obligation and its performance can be separated (so expiation may be given before the triggering act), while in bodily obligations they are inseparable (so expiation must come after). The Hanafi response argues that in both cases, the right of Allah is the servant's act of giving, not the property itself, making both obligations alike. Therefore, expiation (whether financial or bodily) cannot be given before the act that necessitates it (like breaking an oath). The exception is for rights of people, where property is the actual object, so separation is possible. Since expiation is a right of Allah, no such distinction applies.

Key Terms
واجب مالی (wajib mali): An obligation involving property, e.g., paying kaffarah in money or kind.
واجب بدنی (wajib badani): A physical obligation, e.g., fasting or freeing a slave as kaffarah.
حقوق اللہ (huquq Allah): Rights of Allah; obligations that are purely devotional and not tied to specific individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because property is involved.
B) Yes, because it is a financial obligation.
C) No, because financial kaffarah is like bodily kaffarah in rights of Allah.
D) No, only bodily kaffarah cannot be given before.

Key Takeaway
In the rights of Allah, both financial and bodily expiations are due only after the triggering act; the financial nature does not allow early payment.

Definition of 'Amr and Its Default Ruling
Defining 'amr and establishing its default ruling of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of amr, identify its default ruling of obligation, and apply the rule to distinguish between a command before and after prohibition.

Core Idea
A command defaults to obligation — proof is needed to shift it.

This lesson establishes the foundational usul concept of 'amr (command). You will learn its definition, its default ruling according to the Hanafi school, and how the school handles commands that appear after a prohibition. The passage also contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, providing a key point of ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of amr
Amr is a specific verbal form (صيغة) placed to demand an action from a lower authority. Note that it is classified as 'specific' (خاص) in the division of words.
The definition excludes nouns and other verb forms.
2
State the default ruling (mujib)
According to the majority (جمهور), including Hanafis, the required implication (موجب) of amr is obligation (إلزام/وجوب). This is the default unless a proof (دليل) indicates otherwise.
The author notes that amr can have up to 21 meanings, but obligation is primary.
3
Note the exception
A contextual proof or extraneous evidence can shift the meaning from obligation to another ruling (e.g., permissibility, recommendation).
The shift requires a separate dalil, not mere sequence.
4
Apply to the dispute with al-Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i held that a command after a prohibition indicates permissibility. The Hanafi response is that the default remains obligation; temporal sequence alone does not change it.
Example: Quran 5:2 'then hunt' after the prohibition of hunting in ihram.

Chapter on the Command. And it belongs to the first category of the first division of the divisions we have mentioned. For the command form is a specific word from the conjugations of the verb, placed for a specific meaning, which is the demand of an action. Its required implication according to the majority is obligation, except if there is a proof. And the command after prohibition and before it is equal.
Translation: This is a chapter on command. And command is from the type of the first category of the first division from the divisions we have mentioned. Because the command form is such a specific word from the conjugations of the verb that has been placed for a specific meaning, and that is the demand of action. And the required implication of command according to the majority is obligation, except due to some proof. And the command after prohibition and before it is equal.
Elaboration: This is a chapter about command. The author says that in the previous section, under the four divisions that we have mentioned, in the first division (i.e., specific, general, common with interpretation), command is the first type, i.e., it is specific. Because the command form from the conjugations of the verb is such a specific word placed for a specific meaning, i.e., the demand of action. By the qualification 'conjugations of the verb', specific nouns and specific letters are excluded. And by 'specific word', other types of verbs besides command are excluded. There are many types of specific words, but the author will only explain two types in detail, i.e., command and prohibition, because command and prohibition are frequently used in the Shariah. Moreover, since the meaning of command is existential and the meaning of prohibition is non-existential, he prioritized command. Its remaining details you have already read in Nur al-Anwar. And its required implication: He is stating the ruling of command that according to the majority, the required implication of command is obligation. However, if a proof or context indicates a meaning other than obligation, then command is used in that meaning. Command is used for approximately sixteen meanings, and the author of al-Ta'liq al-Hami has mentioned five additional meanings, i.e., total twenty-one meanings. But the real and original meaning of command is obligation. And command after prohibition: The author, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, says that the requirement of command is obligation, whether the command comes after prohibition or before it. By this, he refutes the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. Imam al-Shafi'i says that if command comes before prohibition, it is for obligation, but if it comes after prohibition, it is for permissibility, like 'and when you have completed [the pilgrimage]' (Quran 5:2).

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of 'amr (command) in usul al-fiqh. It defines the command form (صيغة الأمر) as a specific verbal form placed to indicate a demand for an action. This form falls under the category of 'specific' (خاص) in the broader classification of words. The passage then discusses the default ruling of a command: according to the majority of scholars (جمهور), a command implies obligation (إلزام/وجوب). However, if there is a contextual proof (دليل or قرينة) indicating a different meaning (like recommendation or permissibility), then the command is interpreted accordingly. The commentator notes that command can be used for up to 21 different meanings, but the primary meaning is obligation. The passage also addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether a command after a prohibition (like 'hunt after the prohibition of ihram' in the Quran) indicates obligation or permissibility. The Hanafi position is that it still indicates obligation unless there is a specific proof to the contrary, while al-Shafi'i holds that it indicates permissibility. The passage begins with the matn (original Arabic) by the author, followed by an Urdu translation and commentary.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): A verbal form (صيغة) used to demand an action from a lower authority.
صيغة الأمر (ṣīghat al-amr): The specific morphological form (e.g., 'if'al') used for command.
موجبه (mūjibuhu): The required implication or necessary consequence of the command.
الجمهور (al-jumhūr): The majority of scholars, excluding those with differing views.
بعد الحظر (ba‘da al-ḥaẓr): After a prohibition.

Definition of Amr and Its Default Ruling
Defines amr and its default obligation, with a ruling on amr after prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the command (amr) and apply the Hanafi default rule that it indicates obligation (wujub) unless a contrary evidence exists.

Core Idea
A command form defaults to obligation unless proven otherwise — even after a prohibition.

In this passage, Al-Husami defines the concept of 'amr' — the command form — and establishes its foundational default ruling in Hanafi usul. Understanding this definition is crucial because the entire edifice of deriving obligations from Quran and Sunnah rests on how we interpret command forms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of amr
Locate the precise definition in the Arabic text: amr is a specific word form from the conjugations of the verb, coined to mean a request for an action.
The definition emphasizes that amr is a linguistic sigha, not just any imperative.
2
Understand the default ruling
The text states that the implication (mujab) of amr according to the majority is obligation (ilzam), unless there is evidence to the contrary.
This is a key usul principle: the default for commands is wujub.
3
Note the exception
The ruling of obligation can be overridden if a dalil (evidence) indicates a different meaning such as permissibility or recommendation.
The burden of proof lies on the one claiming the default does not apply.
4
Recognize the key dispute
The text asserts that amr after a prohibition and before a prohibition are equal in default obligation. This directly opposes the Shafi'i view that amr after prohibition indicates permissibility.
This dispute has significant practical consequences in fiqh.
5
Apply to a sample command
Take a Quranic command like 'Establish prayer' (aqimu al-salah). Apply the default rule: it is wajib unless evidence shows otherwise. Even if it came after a prohibition, it remains wajib.
Practice this mental step with any command in the Quran or Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْل فِي الْأَمْرِوَهُوَ مِنْ قَبِيْلِ الْوَجْهِ الْاَوَّلِ مِنَ الْقِسْمِ الْأَوَّلِ مِمَّا ذَكَرْنَا مِنَ الْأَقْسَامِ فَإِنَّ صِيغَةَ الْأَمْرِ لَفْظٌ خَاصٌ مِنْ تَصَارِيفِ الْفِعْلِ وُضِعَ لِمَعْنًى خَاصَ وَهُوَ طَلَبَ الْفِعْلِ وَمُوْجَبْهُ عِنْدَ الْجَمْهُورِ الْإِلْزَامُ إِلَّا بِدَلِيْلِ وَالْأَمْرُ بَعْدَ الْحَظُر وَقَبْلَهُ سَوَاءٌ
A section on the command. It is from the category of the first aspect of the first division of the divisions we mentioned. For the command form is a specific word from the conjugations of the verb, coined for a specific meaning, which is the request of the action. Its implication according to the majority is obligation unless there is a (contrary) evidence. And the command after a prohibition and before it are equal.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage defines the legal command (amr). It states that the command form is a specific verbal form from the verb's conjugations, coined for the meaning of demanding an action. According to the majority of scholars (jumhur), the default ruling of a command is obligation (wujub), except if there is evidence indicating otherwise. Importantly, it states that whether the command comes after a prior prohibition or not, it still implies obligation. This is a direct refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's view that a command after prohibition indicates permissibility (ibaha). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that such a command is for permissibility, but the Hanafi position holds that the default is always obligation unless a specific evidence changes it.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): A specific verbal form (sigha) from the conjugations of the verb, coined for the meaning of requesting an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The command form in Arabic linguistics is coined for requesting an action, and its default legal effect in Hanafi usul is obligation (wujub) unless a contrary evidence (dalil) overrides it.

Amr Does Not Imply Repetition
States amr does not require repetition, with divorce example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that amr does not imply repetition to determine the number of performances required by a command.

Core Idea
A single command requires a single performance — repetition is not inherent in the form.

The command form (amr) in Arabic is linguistically coined to seek an action, but the action itself is expressed as a singular masdar. This means a command like 'pray' obligates only a single prayer, not multiple repetitions unless context indicates otherwise. This passage establishes that principle and illustrates it with a divorce case, showing that intention of multiple divorces does not override the singular form, except in the specific case of a slave woman due to her unique legal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the first line: 'And there is no implication for it of repetition, nor does it bear it.' This is the central ruling — amr does not imply takrar (repetition).
The ruling is absolute – the command form itself does not indicate multiple performances.
2
Understand the Linguistic Proof
The passage explains that the command form is coined for seeking the action (talab al-fi'l), but the word for the action (the masdar) is singular (fard), so it cannot bear number (la yahtamil al-adad). This is the dalil: the singular nature of the infinitive.
The proof is linguistic, not textual. It relies on the structure of Arabic.
3
Apply to the Divorce Example
The passage applies the rule: if a man tells his wife 'Divorce yourself' (tallaqi nafsaki), it effects only one divorce, even if he intended two. Intention of number is not operative because the command form does not bear number.
Note that intention (niyyah) cannot change the singular to plural.
4
Note the Exception for a Slave Woman
If the woman is a slave (amah), the command effects two divorces because two is the kind (jins) of her divorce. This is an exception based on the legal category of the slave woman, not on the command form itself.
The exception shows that context (the legal capacity of the addressee) can affect the outcome, but the core rule remains unchanged.
5
Recognize the Cross-Madhhab Relevance
Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with the Hanafi position on this point, while some Asha'ira (like Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini) argued that amr implies repetition. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference is that in the Shafi'i school, a single command is still generally interpreted as one performance, but the disagreement affects how certain commands are construed.
This ikhtilaf is methodological rather than fiqh-practical in most cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا مُوجَبَ لَهُ فِي التَّكْرَارِ وَلَا يَحْتَمِلُهُ لاَنَ لَفْظَ الْأَمْرِ صِيْغَةٌ أُخْتُصِرَتْ لِمَعْنَاهَا مِنْ طَلَب الْفِعْلِ لكِنَّ لَفْظَ الْفِعْلِ فَرْدْ فَلَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْعَدَدَ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا فِي قَوْلِ الرَّجُلِ لِاِمْرَأَتِهِ طَلَقِىٰ نَفْسَكِ إِنَّهُ يَقَعُ عَلَى الْوَاحِدَةِ وَلَا تُعْمَلُ نِيَةُ الثَّنْتَيْنِ فِيْهِ لأَنَّهُ لا تَصِعُ نِيَةُ الْعَدَدِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ الْمَرْأَةُ آمَةً لِاَنَ ذَلِكَ جِئْسُ طَلَاقِهَا فَصَارَ مِنْ طَرِيقِ الْجِنْسِ وَاحِدًا
And there is no implication for it (the command) of repetition, nor does it bear it, because the word of command is a form that is coined for its meaning of seeking the action, but the word of the action (the infinitive) is a single instance, so it does not bear number. And for this reason we said concerning a man's statement to his wife 'Divorce yourself' that it occurs as one divorce, and the intention of two does not take effect in it, because it is an intention of number, unless the woman is a slave, because that (two) is the kind of her divorce, so it becomes one by way of the genus.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage addresses whether a command implies repetition. The Hanafi position is that a command does not require repetition (takrar) and does not even bear the implication of repetition. The reason is that the command form is coined for the meaning of seeking an action, but the action itself (the masdar) is a single instance. Therefore, a command like 'pray' obligates only a single performance. The text illustrates this principle with a practical example from divorce: if a man says to his wife 'Tallaqi nafsaki' (Divorce yourself), this command effects only a single divorce, even if the man intended two divorces. This is because the command form indicates a single instance. However, an exception is made if the woman is a slave, because the kind of divorce for a slave woman is two (i.e., the maximum number of divorces for a slave is two), so in that context, the command might be interpreted as two because the genus (jins) of her divorce is two. This shows that the command does not inherently imply repetition, but context can affect it.

Key Terms
التكرار (al-takrar): Repetition: the command does not require or imply multiple performances of the action.
الأمر (al-amr): The command form in Arabic, which indicates a request for action. In Hanafi usul, it signifies obligation but not repetition.
الفعل (al-fi'l): The action expressed by the masdar (infinitive). In this context, it is singular and thus cannot indicate number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, if a man tells his wife 'Tallaqi nafsaki' (divorce yourself), how many divorces occur if he intended two divorces and she is a free woman?
A) Two divorces because of his intention
B) One divorce because the command does not bear number
C) Zero because the intention is not valid
D) Three divorces because it is a command

Key Takeaway
The command form (amr) in Arabic does not inherently indicate repetition; a single performance fulfills it.

Time as Cause: The Hanafi Rule of Sababiyyah in Time-Bound Acts
Explains how only part of time is cause, not whole

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the part of time that serves as the cause (sabab) for obligation in time-bound acts and explain the Hanafi reasoning for its transfer upon delay.

Core Idea
Only the part of time immediately before performance is the cause—not the whole duration.

Time plays a dual role in Islamic law for obligatory acts: it is both the container (zarf) in which the act must be performed and the cause (sabab) that triggers the obligation. This lesson explores a subtle logical problem: if the entire time span were the cause, the act would either precede its cause or be delayed beyond the container. The Hanafi solution designates only the part of time immediately connected to performance as the cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dual role of time
Recognize that time is both a container (zarf) for the act and a cause (sabab) for its obligation. The act must occur within the time, and the time makes the act obligatory.
This is a foundational usul al-fiqh principle for muwaqqat acts.
2
Understand the logical contradiction
If the entire time were the cause, then performing at the start would mean the act precedes its cause (impossible), and performing at the end would mean the act is delayed beyond the container (invalid).
The text says: 'that would necessitate delaying the performance from its time or advancing it before its cause.'
3
Apply the solution: partial cause
Only a part of time—the part immediately connected to the performance—is made the cause. This resolves the paradox because the cause now truly precedes or coincides with the act without contradiction.
The cause is the juz' alladhi yattasilu bi'l-ada'.
4
Trace the causality transfer process
If the act is performed later, causality transfers to the next part. This continues until the end of the time, ensuring the cause always just precedes the act.
The text explains transfer 'until the time becomes narrow' (Zufar) or 'until the last part' (our view).
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Zufar holds that causality becomes fixed when the time narrows, while the majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that it continues to transfer until the final moment.
The practical difference: for an act performed just before the end, the cause is the last part (majority) or the part at which narrowing began (Zufar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْأَصْلُ فِي هَذَا النَّوْعِ أَنَّهُ لَمَا جُعِلَ الْوَقْتُ ظَرْفًا لِلْمُؤدَّى وَسَبَبًا لِلْوُجُوْبِ لَمْ يَسْتَقِمْ أَنْ يَكُونَ كُلَّ الْوَقْتِ سَبَبًا لِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ يُوجِبُ تَأْخِيرَ الْأَدَاءِ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ أَوْ تَقْدِيمَهُ عَلَى سَبَبِهِ فَوَجَبَ أَنْ يُجْعَلَ بَعْضُهُ سَبَبًا وَهُوَ الْجُزْءُ الَّذِى يَتَّصِلُ بِالْأَدَاءِ فَإِنِ اتَّصَلَ الْأَدَاءُ بِالْجُزْءِ الْأَوَّلِ كَانَ هُوَ السَّبَبَ وَإِلَّا يَنْتَقِلُ السَّبَبِيَّةُ إِلَى الْجُزْءِ الَّذِي يَلِيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَا وَجَبَ نَقْلُ السَّبَبِيَّةِ عَنِ الْجُمْلَةِ وَلَيْسَ بَعْدَ الْجُمْلَةِ جُزْءٌ مُقَدَّرٌ وَجَبَ الْاِقْتِصَارُ عَلَى الْأَدْنَى وَلَمْ يَجُزْ تَقْدِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا سَبَقَ قُبَيْلَ الْأَدَاءِ لِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ يُؤَدِّي إِلَى التَّخَطِّي عَنِ الْقَلِيلِ بِلَا دَلِيلٍ ثُمَّ كَذَلِكَ يَنْتَقِلُ إِلَى أَنْ يَتَضَيَّقَ الْوَقْتُ عِنْدَ زُفَرَ وَإِلَى آخِرِ جُزْءٍ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ الْوَقْتِ عِنْدَنَا فَيَتَعَيَّنُ السَّبَبِيَّةُ فِيهِ لِمَا يَلِي الشُّرُوْعَ فِي الْأَدَاءِ إِذْ لَمْ يَبْقَ بَعْدَهُ مَا يَحْتَمِلُ انْتِقَالَ السَّبَبِيَّةِ إِلَيْهِ
The principle in this type is that when time is made a container for the performed act and a cause for obligation, it is not correct for the entire time to be the cause, because that would necessitate delaying the performance from its time or advancing it before its cause. So it is necessary that some part of it be made the cause, and that is the part that is connected to the performance. If the performance is connected to the first part, then that is the cause; otherwise, the causality transfers to the part that follows it. Because when it became necessary to transfer causality from the whole, and there is no estimated part after the whole, it became necessary to restrict to the least, and it is not permissible to fix it on what preceded just before the performance, because that would lead to passing over the small without evidence. Then similarly it transfers until the time becomes narrow according to Zufar, and until the last part of the parts of the time according to us, so causality becomes fixed in it for what follows the commencement of the performance, since after it there remains no part to which causality could transfer.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage discusses a foundational usul rule regarding time-bound obligations (muwaqqat bi'l-waqt) where time serves both as the container (zarf) for the act and the cause (sabab) for its obligation. The author explains the logical problem: if the entire time span were the cause, then performing the act at any point would either delay the act beyond its time (if performed after) or precede the cause (if performed before), contradicting the roles. Hence, only a part of the time—specifically the part immediately preceding the performance—is designated as the cause. If one prays at the beginning of the time, that first part is the cause; if later, causality shifts to the later part just before the act. This transfer continues until the end, where in the Hanafi view (unlike Zufar's view that it becomes fixed when time narrows) causality settles in the final part. The reasoning is based on avoiding contradiction and adhering to the minimal necessary designation without arbitrary leaps.

Key Terms
سَبَب (sabab): The part of time that is immediately connected to the performance of the act, making the act obligatory.
ظَرْف (zarf): The container or time within which the act must be performed.
أَدَاء (ada'): Performance of the obligatory act within its designated time.
وُجُوب (wujub): Obligation—the legal quality that makes an act required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule discussed, if a person delays performing a time-bound act until near the end of its time, what happens to causality?
A) Causality transfers to the first part of the time
B) Causality transfers to the part immediately before performance
C) Causality becomes fixed at the beginning of the time
D) Causality disappears if the act is delayed

Key Takeaway
In time-bound obligations, the cause (sabab) is the part of time immediately connected to the performance, not the entire duration, and causality transfers with delay until the final moment.

The Last Part of Time as Sabab for Obligation
Hanafi usul rule on the sabab of prayer obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the last part of prayer time is the cause (sabab) for obligation, and derive rulings for changes in personal status at that moment.

Core Idea
The last part of time determines obligation: personal status and prayer completeness depend on that moment.

In Hanafi usul, the cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer is not the entire time but the last part sufficient only for the opening takbir (tahrima). This lesson unpacks that rule, showing how changes in Islam, puberty, sanity, travel, and menstruation at that final moment trigger new obligations or exemptions. It also distinguishes between sound (Fajr) and deficient (Asr) last parts, affecting whether the prayer must be performed fully or may be deficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State clearly that the last part of the prayer time (juz') is the sabab for obligation, not the entire time.
This is Imam Abu Hanifa's position.
2
Examine personal status conditions
List the personal statuses considered at that last part: Islam, puberty, sanity, travel/residence, menstruation/purity. Explain how changes at that moment affect obligation.
E.g., if a kafir becomes Muslim at that moment, prayer becomes wajib.
3
Distinguish sound vs. deficient last parts
Define sound (complete quality) last part (like Fajr) vs. deficient (like Asr at redness). Explain how this affects whether the prayer is obligatory as complete or deficient.
If the last part is sound, prayer must be performed fully; if deficient, performance with deficiency is valid.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a change in status at the last part, determine the ruling on obligation and completeness.
Use the examples from the text: sunrise during Fajr voids the prayer; starting Asr at redness obligates a deficient prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي نہیں ہے ، مگر تو ہم قدرت ضرور ہے اس طریقہ پر کہ اللہ تعالی وقت کو لمبا کر دے اور بندہ ادا پر قادر ہو جائے تو خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ادا و ا جب ہونے کے لئے تو ہم کافی ہے لہذا آخری جز ء سبب ہو جائے گا۔ فَيُعْتَبَرُ حَالُهُ فِي الْإِسْلَامِ وَالْبُلُوغِ وَالْعَقْلِ وَالْجُنُونِ وَالسَّفَرِ وَالْا قَامَةِ وَالْحَيْضِ وَالطُّهُرِ عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْءِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ صِفَةُ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْءِ فَإِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْءُ صَحِيحًا كَمَافِى الْفَجْرِ وَجَبَ كَامِلاً فَإِذَا اعْتَرَضَ الْفَسَادُ بِطُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ بَطَلَ الْفَرْضُ وَإِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْهُ فَاسِدًا كَمَا فِي الْعَصْرِ يَسْتَانِفُ فِي وَقْتِ الْإِحْمِرَارِ وَ جَبَ نَاقِصَّافَيَتَأْذَى بِصِفَةِ النُّقْصَانِ ترجمہ: پس اعتبار کیا جائے گا مکلف کے حال کا اس جزء کے وقت ، مسلمان ہونے میں ، بالغ ہونے میں ، عاقل ہونے میں، مجنون ہونے میں ، مسافر اور مقیم ہونے میں، حائضہ ہونے میں اور حیض سے پاک ہونے میں، اور اعتبار کیا جائے گا اس جزء کی صفت کا پس اگر وہ جزء صیح ہے جیسا کہ فجر میں تو نماز کامل واجب ہوگی پس اگر فساد پیش آ گیا طلوع شمس کی وجہ سے تو فرض باطل ہو جائے گا، اور اگر وہ جزء فاسد ( ناقص ) ہو جیسا کہ عصر میں درانحالیکہ وہ عصر کی نماز شروع کرے احمرار کے وقت تو عصر کی نماز ناقص واجب ہوگی پس ادا ہو جائے گی وہ نقصان کی صفت کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح:- جب امام صاحب کے نزدیک آخری جزء سبب بنا جو تحریمہ کی مقدار ہے تو اسی جزء میں مکلف کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا، لہذا اتنا وقت باقی رہ گیا جس میں صرف تحریمہ کی گنجائش ہے اور اس وقت میں کا فر مسلمان ہو گیا یا بچہ بالغ ہو گیا یا مجنون کا جنون ختم ہو گیا، یا مقیم مسافر ہو گیا، یا مسافر مقیم ہو گیا، یا عورت حیض سے پاک ہوگئی تو ان سب پر نماز فرض ہو جائے گی ، اگر اس وقت عاقل مجنون ہو گیا یا عورت کو حیض آگیا تو نماز ساقط ہو جائے گی، اس وقت میں مقیم مسافر ہو گیا تو قصر کرے گا اور مسافر مقیم ہو گیا تو پوری نماز پڑھے گا۔ اور مامور بہ کے کامل اور ناقص ہونے میں بھی اس جزء کا دخل ہوگا ، اگر یہ آخری جزء کامل ہے تو نماز کامل واجب ہوگی جیسے فجر کا پورا وقت کامل ہے، کسی نے آخری جزء میں نماز شروع کی اور دورانِ نماز سورج طلوع ہو گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ آخری جزء کے کامل ہونے کی وجہ سے کامل واجب ہوئی ، اور صفت نقصان کے ساتھ ادا ئیگی درست نہیں۔۔ اور اگر آخری جزء ناقص ہے تو واجب بھی ناقص ہوگا، جیسے عصر ناقص واجب ہوئی اور ادائیگی بھی ناقص ہو رہی ہے پس ناقص واجب کی صفت نقصان کے ساتھ ادا ئیگی درست ہے۔
This is not sufficient, but power is definitely necessary in this way that Allah lengthens the time and the servant becomes able to perform, so the summary is that according to Imam Sahib, for performance and obligation, capacity is sufficient, hence the last part becomes the cause. So consideration is given to the state of the person in Islam, puberty, sanity, insanity, travel, residence, menstruation, and purity at that part. And consideration is given to the quality of that part: if that part is sound like in Fajr, then the prayer becomes obligatory in full; so if corruption occurs due to sunrise, the obligation becomes void. And if that part is corrupt (deficient) like in Asr when one starts at the time of redness, then the prayer becomes obligatory in a deficient manner, so it is performed with the quality of deficiency. Translation: So consideration is given to the state of the obligated person at the time of that part, regarding being Muslim, being adult, being sane, being insane, being traveler or resident, being menstruating or pure from menses, and consideration is given to the quality of that part. So if that part is sound as in Fajr, then the prayer becomes obligatory in full; so if corruption occurs due to sunrise, the obligation becomes void. And if that part is corrupt (deficient) as in Asr while he starts Asr prayer at the time of redness, then Asr prayer becomes obligatory as deficient, so it is performed with the quality of deficiency. Explanation: When according to Imam Sahib, the last part becomes the cause, which is the measure of the opening takbir, then in that part the state of the obligated is considered. So if only enough time remains in which only the opening takbir can be done, and at that time an infidel becomes Muslim, or a child reaches puberty, or an insane person becomes sane, or a resident becomes a traveler, or a traveler becomes a resident, or a woman becomes pure from menses, then prayer becomes obligatory upon all of them. If at that time a sane person becomes insane, or a woman begins menstruation, then prayer is dropped. If a resident becomes a traveler, he will shorten; if a traveler becomes a resident, he will pray in full. And the completeness or deficiency of the commanded act also depends on this part. If this last part is complete, then the prayer is obligatory as complete, like the entire time of Fajr is complete. If someone starts prayer in the last part and during prayer the sun rises, then the prayer becomes invalid, because due to the completeness of the last part, it was obligatory as complete, and performing it with the quality of deficiency is not valid. And if the last part is deficient, then the obligation is also deficient, like Asr becomes obligatory as deficient, and the performance is also deficient, so performing a deficient obligation with the quality of deficiency is valid.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This lesson expounds the Hanafi ruling that the last part of the prayer time (the portion just sufficient for the opening takbir) is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if only that last part remains, the obligation becomes due, and the state of the person at that moment determines whether the prayer is obligatory or not, and whether it is complete or deficient. The passage first considers personal conditions (Islam, puberty, sanity, etc.) and then the quality of the time part itself. It explains that if the last part is sound (e.g., Fajr time is entirely sound), the prayer must be performed fully; if corruption like sunrise occurs, the prayer is void. If the last part is deficient (e.g., Asr at the time of redness), the prayer is obligatory but in a deficient form, and performing it with that deficiency is valid. The commentary also clarifies that the last part is defined by the length needed for the opening takbir.

Key Terms
جزء (juz'): The last part of the prayer time, sufficient only for the opening takbir (tahrima).
سبب (sabab): The cause for the obligation of prayer; here specifically the last part of time.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer, used here as a measure of minimal time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule in this passage, if a resident becomes a traveler at the last moment of Zuhr time, what is the ruling on his Zuhr prayer?
A) He must pray full Zuhr (4 rak'ahs) because he was a resident at the beginning of time.
B) He must pray shortened Zuhr (2 rak'ahs) because the last part determines his status.
C) Zuhr is not obligatory because he missed the most of the time.
D) He may choose either full or shortened prayer.

Key Takeaway
The last part of prayer time, sufficient only for takbir, is the sabab for obligation and determines both the duty and its completeness.

Qada Prayer in Makruh Times: The Rule of Perfect Performance
Concluding the first type: when time passes without performance, obligation attaches to whole time requiring perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a time-bound obligation is missed, the obligation attaches to the whole time and requires perfect performance, and identify the three makruh times where qada is invalid.

Core Idea
When time expires, obligation binds the whole time, requiring perfect qada free from deficiency.

This passage from the sharh of Al-Husami examines the fourth scenario in the classification of time-bound obligations: when the entire time for a prayer passes without performance. The author explains how the causality of obligation shifts back to the whole time, necessitating perfect performance, and thus qada in certain makruh times is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the condition 'khalā al-waqt 'an al-ādā' — the entire time passes without the obligatory act being performed.
This is the trigger for the rule.
2
Understand the shift of causality
The necessity that had transferred causality from the whole time to a part (to allow performance) is removed, so causality returns to the whole time.
The obstacle was the impossibility of combining container and cause.
3
Determine the consequence
Since the whole time is perfect, the obligation now requires perfect performance (with all conditions).
4
Apply to qada in makruh times
Perfect performance cannot be achieved in the three makruh times (sunrise, sunset, zenith) because those times are inherently deficient. Therefore, qada is invalid in those times.
This applies to any missed fard prayer, even if it was from a previous day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا إِذَا خَلَا الْوَقْتُ عَنِ الْآدَاءِ فَالْوُجُوبُ يُضَاف إلى كُلِ الْوَقْتِ لِزَوَالِ الضَّرُورَةِ الدَّاعِيَةِ لِانْتِقَالِ السَّبَبِيَّةِ عَنِ الْكُلِّ إِلَى الْجُزْءِ فَوَجَبَ بِصِفَةِ الْكَمَال فَلَايَتَأَذَى بِصِفَةِ النُّقْصَانِ فِي الْأَوْقَاتِ الثَّلْثَةِ الْمَكْرُوهَةِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ سَائِرِ الْفَرَائِضِ

ترجمہ: اور بہر حال جب وقت خالی ہو جائے ادا سے تو وجوب منسوب کیا جائے گا پورے وقت کی طرف اس ضرورت کے زائل ہو جانے کی وجہ سے جو تقاضا کر رہی تھی سبیت کو منتقل کرنے کا کل سے جزء کی طرف ، پس واجب ہوگا وہ واجب صفت کمال کے ساتھ تو نہیں ادا ہو گا وہ واجب صفت نقصان کے ساتھ ان تین مکروہ اوقات میں ، بمنزلہ دیگر فرائض کے۔

تشریح : ۔ مصنف اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب پورا وقت گذر گیا اور نماز ادا نہیں کی ( یہ چوتھی صورت ہے ) تو اب پورے وقت کو سبب قرار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ اب پورے وقت کو سبب قرار دینے میں جو مانع تھا وہ ختم ہو گیا ، وہ یہ کہ ظرفیت اور سبیت دونوں چیزوں کو جمع کرنا ممکن نہ تھا، اس مجبوری اور مانع کی وجہ سے کل وقت سے جزء کی طرف سبیت کو منتقل کیا تھا، لیکن اب یہ مانع نہ رہا، کیونکہ اب وقت ظرف نہ رہا تو اب پورے وقت کو سبب قرار دیں گے ، اور کل وقت چونکہ کامل ہے لہذا نماز کامل واجب ہوگی تو یہ کامل واجب تین مکروہ اوقات یعنی بوقت طلوع ، غروب اور استواء میں ادا نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ مکروہ اوقات میں ادا ئیگی ناقص ہوتی ہے، لہذا جیسے اور نمازوں کو مکروہ اوقات میں پڑھنا درست نہیں ہے، ایسے ہی یہ قضا نماز بھی چاہے وہ گذشتہ کل کی عصر کی ہی کیوں نہ ہو، درست نہیں ہے۔
And as for when the time becomes empty of performance, then the obligation is attributed to the whole time due to the removal of the necessitating need that caused the transfer of causality from the whole to the part. So it becomes obligatory with the attribute of perfection, so it will not be performed with the attribute of deficiency in the three disliked times, like the rest of the obligatory prayers. Translation: And in any case, when the time becomes empty of performance, the obligation is attributed to the whole time due to the removal of the need that was demanding the transfer of causality from the whole to the part. So it becomes obligatory with the attribute of perfection, so that obligation will not be performed with the attribute of deficiency in those three disliked times, like other obligations. Elucidation: The author says: When the entire time has passed and the prayer was not performed (this is the fourth case), then now the whole time will be made the cause, because the obstacle that prevented making the whole time the cause has been removed, namely that it was not possible to combine both being a container and being a cause. Due to this compulsion and obstacle, causality was transferred from the whole to the part. But now this obstacle is gone, because time is no longer a container, so we will make the whole time the cause. And since the whole time is perfect, the prayer becomes obligatory with perfection, so this perfect obligation will not be performed in the three disliked times, i.e., at sunrise, sunset, and zenith, because performance in disliked times is deficient. Therefore, just as other prayers are not valid in disliked times, similarly this make-up prayer, even if it be the previous day's Asr, is not valid.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a legal rule from the commentary on the first type of time-bound obligations. It addresses the scenario when the entire time for a prayer (e.g., Asr) passes without performance, so it becomes qada. The author explains that in this case, the obligation attaches to the whole time (causality returns to the whole) because the necessity that had transferred causality to a part (to allow performance) is removed. Consequently, the obligation now requires perfect performance (i.e., with full conditions). Therefore, performing this qada prayer in the three makruh times (sunrise, sunset, zenith) is not valid, because performance in those times is inherently deficient. This is analogous to other obligatory prayers which are also invalid in those times. The commentary clarifies that this is the fourth scenario in the classification of time-bound obligations.

Key Terms
خلو الوقت عن الأداء (khalā al-waqt 'an al-ādā'): The state when the entire designated time period passes without the obligatory act being performed within it.
سببية (sababiyya): Causality; the legal cause that triggers the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the entire time for Asr prayer passes without performance, in which of the following times is its qada prayer valid according to this text?
A) At sunrise
B) At sunset
C) At zenith
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
When a time-bound obligation is missed, its qada requires perfect performance and cannot be offered in the three makruh times.
