Defining the Second Type: Time as Measure and Cause for Fasting
Defining the second type where time is both measure and cause for fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the second type of time-bound obligation in Hanafi usul and explain why the absolute name of fasting suffices even with error in description.

Core Idea
Time is both the measure and the cause for fasting; therefore, only fasting is valid in this time.

In this passage, al-Husami distinguishes the second type of time-bound obligations from the first. Here, time is not just a container but the very reason the act is obligated and the measure that defines it. This has direct implications for the validity of intentions: any general intention of 'fasting' fulfills the obligation, even if the specific type is mistaken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type
Compare this second type (fasting) to the first (prayer). In prayer, time is only a container (zarf); in fasting, time is both measure (miyar) and cause (sabab).
The text says 'time is made the measure for the commanded and the cause for its obligation.'
2
Understand the core ruling
The ruling: no other act remains valid in this time. This means you cannot substitute another act for the obligatory fast in this time slot.
Other acts like nafl fasts are still valid but do not replace the obligation.
3
Apply the consequence
If someone intends fasting with the absolute name (e.g., 'I am fasting') and errs in describing the type (e.g., thought it was a voluntary fast), it still counts for the obligatory fast.
This is because the time itself designates the act, so the absolute intention is sufficient.
4
Note the exception signaled
The text then introduces exceptions (travelers and sick) which will be detailed in the following lesson.
The phrase 'except in the case of travelers' indicates that the core ruling does not apply to them under certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالنّوع الثّانِئ مَاجُعِلَ الْوَقْتُ مِعْيَارَ اله وَسَبَبًا لِوُجُوْبِهِ وَهُوَ وَقْتُ الصَّوْمِ الا تَرى أَنَّهُ قَدِرَبِهِ وَأَضِيْفَ إِلَيْهِ وَمِنْ حُكْمِهِ أَنْ لَا يَبْقَى غَيْرُهُ مَشْرُوعًا فِيهِ فَيْصَابَ بِمُطْلَقِ الْاِسْمِ وَمَعَ الْخَطَاءِ فِي الْوَصْفِ إِلَّا فِي الْمُسَافِرِينَ يَنْوِيءُ وَاجِبًا أَخَرَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَلَوَنَوَى النَّفْلَ فَفِيهِ رِوَايَتَانِ وَأَمَّا الْمَرِيضُ فَالصَّحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ صَوْمُهُ عَنِ الْفَرْضِ بِكُلِ حَالٍ لِاَنَ رُخْصَتَهُ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِحَقِيْقَةِ الْعَجْزِ فَيَظْهَرُ بِنَفْسِ الصَّوْم فَوَاتُ شَرْطِ الرُّخْصَةِ فَيُلْحَقُ بِالصَّحِيحِ وَأَمَّا الْمُسَافِرُ فَيَسْتَوْجِبْ الرَّخْصَةَ بِعَجْزِ مُقَدَر لِقِيَام سَبَبِهِ وَهُوَ السَّفَرُ فَلَا يَظْهَرُ بِنَفْسِ الصَّوْمِ فَوَاتُ شَرْطِ الرُّخْصَةِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ التَّرَخُصُ فَيَتَعَدَّى حِينَئِذٍ بِطَرِيقِ التَّنْبِيْهِ إِلَى حَاجَتِهِ الدِّينِيَةِ

ترجمہ:۔ اور مقید بالوقت کی دوسری قسم وہ ہے جس میں وقت کو معیار بنایا جائے مامور بہ کے لئے اور سبب بنایا جائے اس کے وجوب کے لئے اور وہ روزہ کا وقت ہے کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ روزہ کو مقدر کیا گیا ہے وقت کے ساتھ اور روزہ کی اضافت کی گئی ہے وقت کی جانب ، اور اس قسم کے حکم میں سے یہ ہے کہ اس کے علاوہ وقت میں مشروع باقی نہیں رہے گا پس واجب کو درست قرار دیا جائے گا مطلق اسم صوم کے ساتھ اور وصف میں خطا کے ساتھ مگر مسافر کے حق میں کہ وہ نیت کرے دوسرے واجب کی امام ابو حنیفہ اللہ کے نزدیک ، اور اگر مسافر نے نفل روزے کی نیت کی تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ اور بہرحال بیمار کے بارے میں صحیح یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک اس کا روزہ ہر حال میں فرض کی طرف واقع ہو گا کیونکہ اس کی رخصت عجز کی حقیقت سے متعلق ہے پس روزہ کے ذریعہ رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے لہذا وہ صحیح کے حکم میں ملحق ہوگا اور بہرحال مسافر رخصت کا مستحق ہے ایک مقدر عجز کی وجہ سے اس لئے کہ اس کا سبب یعنی سفر قائم ہے پس روزہ کے ذریعہ رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا ظاہر نہیں ہوتا لہذا رخصت باطل نہیں ہوگی پس اس وقت وہ رخصت تعدی کرے گی تنبیہ کے طریقہ سے اس کی دینی حاجت کی طرف۔
And the second type is that in which time is made the measure for the commanded [act] and the cause for its obligation, and it is the time of fasting. Do you not see that it is measured by it and attributed to it. And from its ruling is that no other [act] remains valid in it, so it is attained with the absolute name [of fasting] and with error in description, except in the case of travelers who intend another obligatory [fast] according to Abu Hanifah. And if he intends voluntary, then there are two narrations. As for the sick person, the correct [opinion] with us is that his fast falls for the obligation in any case, because his concession is attached to the reality of incapacity, so by the fast itself the absence of the condition for the concession becomes apparent, so he is joined to the healthy. And as for the traveler, he deserves the concession due to a presumed incapacity because its cause, travel, remains. So by the fast itself, the absence of the condition for the concession does not become apparent, so the concession is not invalidated. Then at that time it extends by way of indication to his religious need. Translation: And the second type of time-bound [obligation] is that in which time is made the measure for the commanded [act] and the cause for its obligation, and that is the time of fasting. Do you not see that fasting is measured with time and attributed to time. And from the rulings of this type is that no other act remains valid in that time, so the obligation is considered valid with the absolute name of fasting and with error in description, except regarding the traveler that he intends another obligatory [fast] according to Imam Abu Hanifah. And if the traveler intends a voluntary fast, then there are two narrations. And as for the sick person, the correct opinion with us is that his fast falls for the obligation in any case, because his concession is attached to the reality of incapacity, so by the fast itself the absence of the condition for the concession becomes apparent, so he is joined to the ruling of the healthy. And as for the traveler, he deserves the concession due to a presumed incapacity because its cause, travel, remains. So by the fast itself, the absence of the condition for the concession does not become apparent, so the concession is not invalidated. So at that time, the concession extends by way of indication to his religious need.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage defines the second type of time-bound obligations in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Here, time serves two roles: first as the measure (miyar) of the commanded act, meaning the act is defined by this time (e.g., fasting in Ramadan), and second as the legal cause (sabab) for the obligation itself. The key ruling for this type is that no other act besides this obligation is legislated in that time. Consequently, if someone intends to fast with the absolute name (e.g., just 'fasting') even if they make an error in specifying the type (e.g., thinking it is a voluntary fast), it counts as the obligatory fast. However, there is an exception for travelers: according to Imam Abu Hanifah, if a traveler intends another wajib fast (e.g., a vow), his fast counts for that other obligation, not for Ramadan. There are two narrations if he intends nafl. For a sick person, since his concession is based on actual incapacity, the very act of fasting shows the condition for concession is absent, so his fast always counts for the obligatory (Ramadan). For a traveler, the concession is due to a presumed incapacity (travel itself is a cause), so fasting does not negate the condition for concession; hence, his intention is effective for another obligation. The commentary explains the reasoning behind these rulings.

Key Terms
النوع الثاني (al-naw' al-thānī): The second type of time-bound obligation where time is both the measure and the cause for the obligation; applies to fasting.
معيار (mi'yar): Measure; the standard by which the commanded act is defined and quantified; for fasting, the time determines its validity and quantity.
سبب (sabab): Legal cause; the factor that triggers the obligation. For fasting, the time itself is the cause for the obligation to fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the role of time in the second type of time-bound obligations?
A) Time is only a container for the act
B) Time is both the measure and the cause for the obligation
C) Time is only a condition for validity
D) Time is irrelevant to the obligation

Key Takeaway
Time in the second type serves as both measure and cause, making any intention of the absolute act sufficient for the obligation.

Exceptions for Travelers and Sick Persons in Fasting Obligation
Exceptions for travelers and sick persons in the second type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on a traveler who intends another wajib fast on a day of Ramadan, and distinguish it from the case of a sick person.

Core Idea
The traveler's concession allows his intention for another wajib, but the sick person's concession vanishes upon fasting, so his fast always counts for Ramadan.

The passage extends the discussion of the second type to cases where the obligated person has a legal concession (rukhsah). The ruling pivots on whether the concession is based on actual incapacity (marad) or presumed incapacity (safar). This leads to a difference within the Hanafi school regarding the traveler's intention, as well as a settled rule for the sick person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The text gives special rulings for two types of people: traveler (musafir) and sick (marid).
Note that the sick person is distinguished by actual incapacity, while the traveler's incapacity is presumed due to the journey.
2
Understand the traveler's exception
The exception says: 'except in the case of travelers who intend another obligatory [fast] according to Abu Hanifah.' This means if a traveler intends a different wajib fast (e.g., a vowed fast) on a day of Ramadan, that fast counts for the other wajib, not for Ramadan.
This is only for another wajib; if he intends nafl, there are two narrations.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the traveler
The traveler's concession is based on a presumed incapacity (travel itself is a cause). Since the concession remains despite fasting, the traveler can effectively 'divert' his fast to another obligation.
The text says: 'the concession extends by way of indication to his religious need.'
4
Analyze the sick person's ruling
For the sick person, the correct opinion (al-sahih) is that his fast always falls for the obligation (Ramadan), regardless of his intention. This is because his concession is based on actual incapacity, and by fasting, he shows he is capable, so the concession vanishes.
The text says: 'by the fast itself the absence of the condition for the concession becomes apparent.'
5
Compare the two
Contrast: The sick person cannot redirect his fast because his concession disappears upon fasting; the traveler can redirect because his concession remains.
This distinction is based on the nature of the incapacity: actual vs. presumed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالنّوع الثّانِئ مَاجُعِلَ الْوَقْتُ مِعْيَارَ اله وَسَبَبًا لِوُجُوْبِهِ وَهُوَ وَقْتُ الصَّوْمِ الا تَرى أَنَّهُ قَدِرَبِهِ وَأَضِيْفَ إِلَيْهِ وَمِنْ حُكْمِهِ أَنْ لَا يَبْقَى غَيْرُهُ مَشْرُوعًا فِيهِ فَيْصَابَ بِمُطْلَقِ الْاِسْمِ وَمَعَ الْخَطَاءِ فِي الْوَصْفِ إِلَّا فِي الْمُسَافِرِينَ يَنْوِيءُ وَاجِبًا أَخَرَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَلَوَنَوَى النَّفْلَ فَفِيهِ رِوَايَتَانِ وَأَمَّا الْمَرِيضُ فَالصَّحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ صَوْمُهُ عَنِ الْفَرْضِ بِكُلِ حَالٍ لِاَنَ رُخْصَتَهُ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِحَقِيْقَةِ الْعَجْزِ فَيَظْهَرُ بِنَفْسِ الصَّوْم فَوَاتُ شَرْطِ الرُّخْصَةِ فَيُلْحَقُ بِالصَّحِيحِ وَأَمَّا الْمُسَافِرُ فَيَسْتَوْجِبْ الرَّخْصَةَ بِعَجْزِ مُقَدَر لِقِيَام سَبَبِهِ وَهُوَ السَّفَرُ فَلَا يَظْهَرُ بِنَفْسِ الصَّوْمِ فَوَاتُ شَرْطِ الرُّخْصَةِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ التَّرَخُصُ فَيَتَعَدَّى حِينَئِذٍ بِطَرِيقِ التَّنْبِيْهِ إِلَى حَاجَتِهِ الدِّينِيَةِ

ترجمہ:۔ اور مقید بالوقت کی دوسری قسم وہ ہے جس میں وقت کو معیار بنایا جائے مامور بہ کے لئے اور سبب بنایا جائے اس کے وجوب کے لئے اور وہ روزہ کا وقت ہے کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ روزہ کو مقدر کیا گیا ہے وقت کے ساتھ اور روزہ کی اضافت کی گئی ہے وقت کی جانب ، اور اس قسم کے حکم میں سے یہ ہے کہ اس کے علاوہ وقت میں مشروع باقی نہیں رہے گا پس واجب کو درست قرار دیا جائے گا مطلق اسم صوم کے ساتھ اور وصف میں خطا کے ساتھ مگر مسافر کے حق میں کہ وہ نیت کرے دوسرے واجب کی امام ابو حنیفہ اللہ کے نزدیک ، اور اگر مسافر نے نفل روزے کی نیت کی تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ اور بہرحال بیمار کے بارے میں صحیح یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک اس کا روزہ ہر حال میں فرض کی طرف واقع ہو گا کیونکہ اس کی رخصت عجز کی حقیقت سے متعلق ہے پس روزہ کے ذریعہ رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے لہذا وہ صحیح کے حکم میں ملحق ہوگا اور بہرحال مسافر رخصت کا مستحق ہے ایک مقدر عجز کی وجہ سے اس لئے کہ اس کا سبب یعنی سفر قائم ہے پس روزہ کے ذریعہ رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا ظاہر نہیں ہوتا لہذا رخصت باطل نہیں ہوگی پس اس وقت وہ رخصت تعدی کرے گی تنبیہ کے طریقہ سے اس کی دینی حاجت کی طرف۔
And the second type is that in which time is made the measure for the commanded [act] and the cause for its obligation, and it is the time of fasting. Do you not see that it is measured by it and attributed to it. And from its ruling is that no other [act] remains valid in it, so it is attained with the absolute name [of fasting] and with error in description, except in the case of travelers who intend another obligatory [fast] according to Abu Hanifah. And if he intends voluntary, then there are two narrations. As for the sick person, the correct [opinion] with us is that his fast falls for the obligation in any case, because his concession is attached to the reality of incapacity, so by the fast itself the absence of the condition for the concession becomes apparent, so he is joined to the healthy. And as for the traveler, he deserves the concession due to a presumed incapacity because its cause, travel, remains. So by the fast itself, the absence of the condition for the concession does not become apparent, so the concession is not invalidated. Then at that time it extends by way of indication to his religious need. Translation: And the second type of time-bound [obligation] is that in which time is made the measure for the commanded [act] and the cause for its obligation, and that is the time of fasting. Do you not see that fasting is measured with time and attributed to time. And from the rulings of this type is that no other act remains valid in that time, so the obligation is considered valid with the absolute name of fasting and with error in description, except regarding the traveler that he intends another obligatory [fast] according to Imam Abu Hanifah. And if the traveler intends a voluntary fast, then there are two narrations. And as for the sick person, the correct opinion with us is that his fast falls for the obligation in any case, because his concession is attached to the reality of incapacity, so by the fast itself the absence of the condition for the concession becomes apparent, so he is joined to the ruling of the healthy. And as for the traveler, he deserves the concession due to a presumed incapacity because its cause, travel, remains. So by the fast itself, the absence of the condition for the concession does not become apparent, so the concession is not invalidated. So at that time, the concession extends by way of indication to his religious need.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage defines the second type of time-bound obligations in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Here, time serves two roles: first as the measure (miyar) of the commanded act, meaning the act is defined by this time (e.g., fasting in Ramadan), and second as the legal cause (sabab) for the obligation itself. The key ruling for this type is that no other act besides this obligation is legislated in that time. Consequently, if someone intends to fast with the absolute name (e.g., just 'fasting') even if they make an error in specifying the type (e.g., thinking it is a voluntary fast), it counts as the obligatory fast. However, there is an exception for travelers: according to Imam Abu Hanifah, if a traveler intends another wajib fast (e.g., a vow), his fast counts for that other obligation, not for Ramadan. There are two narrations if he intends nafl. For a sick person, since his concession is based on actual incapacity, the very act of fasting shows the condition for concession is absent, so his fast always counts for the obligatory (Ramadan). For a traveler, the concession is due to a presumed incapacity (travel itself is a cause), so fasting does not negate the condition for concession; hence, his intention is effective for another obligation. The commentary explains the reasoning behind these rulings.

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsah): A legal concession that modifies the original ruling due to an excuse (travel, illness).
عجز حقيقي (‘ajz haqiqi): Actual incapacity; the person is genuinely unable to perform the act (e.g., severe illness).
عجز مقدر (‘ajz muqaddar): Presumed incapacity; a legal presumption of difficulty due to a situation (e.g., travel) even if the person is actually able.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the sick person's fast always fall for the obligation (Ramadan) according to the text?
A) Because the sick person must always fast
B) Because his concession is based on actual incapacity, and by fasting he shows he is capable, so the concession vanishes
C) Because the sick person never has a concession
D) Because the sick person cannot intend another wajib

Key Takeaway
The traveler's concession remains effective, allowing redirection of the fast; the sick person's concession vanishes, forcing the fast to count for Ramadan.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Second Type of Time-Bound Command: Time as Measure and Cause
Defining the second type of time-bound command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the second type of time-bound command, distinguish it from the first type (time as a vessel), and apply the ruling that any intention of fasting in Ramadan results in the Ramadan fast for the healthy resident.

Core Idea
When time is a measure and cause, the commanded act is uniquely fixed to that time, overriding any mistaken intention.

In this passage, the commentator explains a key distinction in Hanafi usul: some commands are tied to a specific time as a measure and cause, not just as a container. The example is the fast of Ramadan. Understanding this distinction helps you see why Ramadan fasts automatically override other intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of time-bound commands
Recall the first type where time is a vessel (zarf) for the act, like prayer times. Here, time is a measure (mi'yar) and cause (sabab) for the obligation.
The first type was covered earlier in Al-Husami.
2
Understand the meaning of 'measure' (mi'yar)
Time as a measure means the commanded act expands or contracts with time. Fasting is proportional to the length of the day. The attribution 'sawmu Ramadān' shows causation: the month causes the obligation.
Idafa (attribution) in Arabic implies causality in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply the general rule for a healthy resident
In this type, no other act of the same kind can be intended in that time. If a healthy resident intends a fast in Ramadan, even if he mistakenly says 'qada' or 'nafl', the Ramadan fast is valid and the other intention is void.
4
Distinguish the exception: traveler and sick
The passage mentions an exception for the traveler and sick. This lesson focuses on the general rule; the exception will be covered separately.

Source Text

وَالنّوع الثّانِئ مَاجُعِلَ الْوَقْتُ مِعْيَارَ [؟] وَسَبَبًا لِوُجُوْبِهِ وَهُوَ وَقْتُ الصَّوْمِ الا تَرى أَنَّهُ قَدِرَبِهِ وَأَضِيْفَ إِلَيْهِ وَمِنْ حُكْمِهِ أَنْ لَا يَبْقَى غَيْرُهُ مَشْرُوعًا فِيهِ فَيْصَابَ [؟] بِمُطْلَقِ الْاِسْمِ وَمَعَ الْخَطَاءِ فِي الْوَصْفِ إِلَّا فِي الْمُسَافِرِيَنْوِئُ [؟] وَاجِبًا أَخَرَ عِنْدَ ابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَلَوْنَوَى النَّفْلَ فَفِيهِ رِوَايَتَانِ وَأَمَّا الْمَرِيضُ فَالصَّحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ صَوْمُهُ عَنِ الْفَرْضِ بِكُلِ حَالٍ لِاَنَ رُخْصَتَهُ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِحَقِيْقَةِ الْعَجْزِ فَيَظْهَرُ بِنَفْسِ الصَّوْم فَوَاتُ شَرْطِ الرُّخْصَةِ فَيُلْحَقُ بِالصَّحِيحِ وَأَمَّا الْمُسَافِرُ فَيَسْتَوْجِبْ [؟] الرَّخْصَةَ بِعَجْزِ مُقَدَر [؟] لِقِيَام سَبَبِهِ وَهُوَ السَّفَرُ فَلَا يَظْهَرُ بِنَفْسِ الصَّوْمِ فَوَاتُ شَرْطِ الرُّخْصَةِ فَلَا يَبْطُلُ التَّرَخُصُ [؟] فَيَتَعَدَّى حِينَئِذٍ بِطَرِيقِ التَّنْبِيْهِ إِلَى حَاجَتِهِ الدِّينِيَةِ

ترجمہ:۔ اور مقید بالوقت کی دوسری قسم وہ ہے جس میں وقت کو معیار بنایا جائے مامور بہ کے لئے اور سبب بنایا جائے اس کے وجوب کے لئے اور وہ روزہ کا وقت ہے کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ روزہ کو مقدر کیا گیا ہے وقت کے ساتھ اور روزہ کی اضافت کی گئی ہے وقت کی جانب ، اور اس قسم کے حکم میں سے یہ ہے کہ اس کے علاوہ وقت میں مشروع باقی نہیں رہے گا پس واجب کو درست قرار دیا جائے گا مطلق اسم صوم کے ساتھ اور وصف میں خطا کے ساتھ مگر مسافر کے حق میں کہ وہ نیت کرے دوسرے واجب کی امام ابو حنیفہ اللہ کے نزدیک ، اور اگر مسافر نے نفل روزے کی نیت کی تو اس میں دوروایتیں ہیں، اور بہر حال مریض پس صحیح قول ہمارے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ واقع ہوگا اس کا روزہ فرض سے ہر حال میں ، اس لئے کہ مریض کی رخصت متعلق ہے حقیقت عجز کے ساتھ پس ظاہر ہو جائے گا نفس روزہ سے رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا، پس مریض کو لاحق کیا جائے گا تندرست کے ساتھ ، اور بہر حال مسافر پس وہ مستحق ہوتا ہے رخصت کا عجز تقدیری کے ساتھ ، عجز کے سبب کے قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ سفر ہے، تو نہیں ظاہر ہوگا نفس روزہ سے رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا ، لہذا رخصت باطل نہیں ہوگی ، پس یہ رخصت متعدی ہوگی دلالت کے طریقہ پر اس کی حاجت دینیہ کی طرف۔

تشریح:- مصنف سے مامور بہ مقید بالوقت کی دوسری قسم کو بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ جس میں وقت مامور بہ کے لئے معیار ہو، اور وجوب کے لئے سبب ہو، پہلی قسم میں وقت ظرف تھا، اور یہاں معیار ہے، معیار ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے که مامور بہ پورے وقت کو گھیرے ہوئے ہو، اس طریقہ پر کہ وقت کے گھٹنے بڑھنے سے مامور بہ بھی گھٹے بڑھے، جیسے روزے کا وقت روزے کے لئے معیار ہے، روزہ وقت (دن) کے ساتھ اس طرح مقدر ہے کہ دن کے گھٹنے بڑھنے سے روزہ بھی گھٹتا بڑھتا ہے، اور روزہ کی اضافت صوم کی طرف کر کے کہتے ہیں ”صومُ رَمَضَانَ ، یہ اضافت سبیت کی دلیل ہے، اضافت کی صورت میں مضاف الیہ مضاف کا سبب ہوتا ہے۔ اس نوع ثانی کا حکم یہ ہے کہ چونکہ اس میں وقت معیار ہوتا ہے، تو وقت کے ساتھ جو مامور بہ ہے اس کے علاوہ کسی وقت میں دوسرے فعل کی گنجائش ہی نہیں ہے، یعنی رمضان میں غیر رمضان کے روزے کی گنجائش ہی نہیں ہے بلکہ رمضان کا مہینہ صوم رمضان کے لئے متعین ہو گیا تو اب اگر کوئی مطلق صوم کی نیت کرے جیسے دل یا زبان سے کہے کہ میں نے روزہ کی نیت کی ، تو رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا، نیت سے متعین کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، اسی طرح خطافی الوصف کے ساتھ نیت کی تو بھی رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا ، جیسے رمضان میں نفل روزے کی نیت کی ، یا قضاء، یا کفارہ یا نذر کے روزے کی نیت کی تو بھی رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا، جو نیت کی ہے وہ روزہ نہ ہوگا ، کیونکہ رمضان کا مہینہ صوم رمضان کے لئے معیار ہونے کی وجہ سے متعین ہے، لہذا اس نے غلطی سے جو وصف بیان کیا یعنی قضاء کفارہ وغیرہ یہ باطل ہو جائے گا، تندرست، مقیم کے لئے تو یہی حکم ہے، البتہ مریض و مسافر کے لئے کچھ تفصیل ہے۔ الا فى المسافر - مسافر کے بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ علی نے فرمایا کہ اگر وہ رمضان میں دوسرے واجب کی نیت کرتا ہے، تو وہ دوسرا واجب ادا ہوگا ، اور اگر نفل کی نیت کرتا ہے تو امام صاحب سے دور وایتیں ہیں ،مگر اصح قول یہی ہے کہ رمضان ہی کا روزہ ادا ہو گا۔ اور مریض کے بارے میں اگر چہ کئی اقوال ہیں، بعض احناف کہتے ہیں کہ مریض کا حکم بھی بعینہ مسافر کا حکم
And the second type is that in which time is made a measure for the commanded act and a cause for its obligation, and it is the time of fasting. Do you not see that it is measured by it and attributed to it? And from its ruling is that no other act remains valid in it, so it is validated with the absolute name and with error in description, except in the case of the traveler who intends another obligatory, according to Abu Hanifa; and if he intends supererogatory, there are two narrations. As for the sick person, the correct view with us is that his fast counts as the obligatory in every case because his license (rukhsa) is attached to the reality of incapacity, so the loss of the condition of license becomes apparent through the fast itself, so he is considered like the healthy. As for the traveler, he deserves the license due to a presumptive incapacity because its cause (travel) exists, so the loss of the condition of license does not become apparent through the fast itself, so the license is not invalidated, and then it extends by way of indication to his religious need.

Translation: The second type of time-bound command is that in which time is made a measure for the commanded act and a cause for its obligation, and that is the time of fasting. Do you not see that fasting is estimated by time and attributed to time, and among the rulings of this type is that nothing else remains valid in it except it, so the obligation is validated with the absolute name of fasting and with error in description, except in the case of the traveler that he intends another obligatory according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and if the traveler intends supererogatory fasting, then there are two narrations. As for the sick person, the correct view with us is that his fasting counts as the obligatory in every case, because the license for the sick is attached to the reality of incapacity, so the loss of the condition of license becomes apparent through the fasting itself, so the sick person is attached to the healthy. As for the traveler, he deserves the license due to presumptive incapacity because its cause (travel) exists, so the loss of the condition of license does not become apparent through the fasting itself, so the license is not invalidated, and then this license extends by way of indication to his religious need.

Commentary: The author (Mussanif) is explaining the second type of time-bound commanded act, in which time is a measure for the commanded act and a cause for its obligation. In the first type, time was a vessel (zarf), and here it is a measure (mi'yar). The meaning of being a measure is that the commanded act encompasses the entire time, such that as time decreases or increases, the commanded act decreases or increases, like the time of fasting is a measure for fasting. Fasting is estimated with time (the day) such that as the day decreases or increases, fasting decreases or increases. Attribution of fasting to time (sawmu Ramadān) is evidence of causation; in attribution, the thing attributed (mudaf ilayh) is the cause of the mudaf. The ruling of this second type is that since time is a measure, there is no room for any other act in that time besides the commanded act, i.e., in Ramadan there is no room for a non-Ramadan fast. Rather, the month of Ramadan is specified for the fast of Ramadan. So if someone intends the absolute fast (sawm mutlaq) – like saying with heart or tongue 'I intend fasting' – it will be the fast of Ramadan; there is no need to specify. Similarly, if he intends with an error in description, it will still be the Ramadan fast, e.g., if in Ramadan he intends a supererogatory fast, or a qada, kaffarah, or nadhr fast, it will still be the Ramadan fast; what he intended will not occur because the month of Ramadan is specified as a measure for the Ramadan fast, so the incorrect description (qada, kaffarah, etc.) becomes void. This ruling applies to the healthy, resident person. However, for the sick and traveler, there is some detail. Alā fil-musāfir: Regarding the traveler, Imam Abu Hanifa said that if he intends another wajib in Ramadan, that other wajib will be fulfilled; and if he intends nafl, there are two narrations from the Imam, but the strongest view is that it will be the Ramadan fast. Regarding the sick person, there are several opinions; some Hanafis say that the rule for the sick is exactly the same as for the traveler.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) on Al-Husami, explaining the second type of time-bound (muqayyad bi al-waqt) commanded acts. The author distinguishes between two types: the first (discussed earlier) where time is a vessel (zarf) for the act, like prayer times; the second, where time is a measure (mi'yar) and cause (sabab) for the obligation itself. The example given is the fast of Ramadan. The key principle: in the second type, the time (Ramadan) is so specific to the commanded act (fasting) that no other type of fast can be intended in that time. If someone intends an absolute fast (sawm mutlaq) or even mistakenly intends a qada, kaffarah, or nafl fast, it automatically becomes the Ramadan fast. This is because the time itself determines the obligation. The exception is the traveler: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a traveler intends another wajib fast (like qada), that wajib is fulfilled instead of the Ramadan fast, and if he intends nafl, there are two narrations (the stronger one is that it becomes Ramadan fast). The sick person's fast always counts as the obligatory fast (Ramadan) because the license (rukhsa) for the sick is based on actual incapacity, which disappears upon fasting, so they are like the healthy. The traveler's license is based on a presumptive incapacity (due to travel), so the license remains and can be applied through indication to other religious needs. The Urdu translation and commentary clarify these points by explaining the concept of 'measure' (mi'yar) and the attribution (idafa) as evidence of causation.

Key Terms
الوقت معيار (al-waqt mi'yar): Time as a measure (mi'yar) means the commanded act expands or contracts with the expanse or contraction of time, and the act is proportioned to the time.
السبب (al-sabab): Cause: the factor that brings about the obligation (wujub) of the act. Here, the time itself (Ramadan) is made the cause for the obligation of fasting.
الصوم (al-sawm): Fasting, the specific commanded act in this second type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a healthy resident in Ramadan says, 'I intend to fast a nafl fast'?
A) The nafl fast is valid.
B) The Ramadan fast is valid, and the nafl is not fulfilled.
C) No fast is valid because the intention is wrong.
D) The person must choose which fast to perform.

Key Takeaway
In the second type of time-bound command, time is both measure and cause, so the commanded act is uniquely fixed to that time, overriding mistaken intentions.

Exceptions for Traveler and Sick: The Rukhsa Analysis
Detailing the exceptions for traveler and sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the traveler's and sick person's fasts are treated differently in Ramadan, state Abu Hanifa's view on the traveler intending another wajib fast, and contrast the basis of rukhsa for each.

Core Idea
The traveler's license remains during Ramadan, allowing a different wajib fast; the sick person's license vanishes upon fasting.

The passage now turns to exceptions to the general rule. While a healthy resident's intention is overridden by the time, the traveler and sick person have a license (rukhsa) that modifies the ruling. Understanding the basis of their license—actual vs. presumptive incapacity—is key to predicting the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule and its exception
The general rule: any intention in Ramadan becomes the Ramadan fast. Exception: traveler and sick. The passage provides details specifically for the traveler and sick.
The exception is introduced with 'illa fi al-musafir'.
2
Analyze the sick person's case
The sick person's rukhsa (license not to fast) is based on actual incapacity. When he fasts, the incapacity disappears, so the license condition is lost. Thus, his fast counts as the obligatory Ramadan fast.
The text says the sick person is considered like the healthy.
3
Analyze the traveler's case
The traveler's rukhsa is based on presumptive incapacity (hardship of travel). The cause (safar) persists even while fasting, so the license remains. Thus, if a traveler intends another wajib fast (like qada), Abu Hanifa rules it counts as that wajib, not Ramadan.
This is the madhhab dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. other views.
4
Examine the nafl intention for traveler
If a traveler intends a nafl fast, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. The stronger view (as per the commentary) is that it becomes the Ramadan fast, like the general rule.

ترجمہ:۔ اور مقید بالوقت کی دوسری قسم وہ ہے جس میں وقت کو معیار بنایا جائے مامور بہ کے لئے اور سبب بنایا جائے اس کے وجوب کے لئے اور وہ روزہ کا وقت ہے کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ روزہ کو مقدر کیا گیا ہے وقت کے ساتھ اور روزہ کی اضافت کی گئی ہے وقت کی جانب ، اور اس قسم کے حکم میں سے یہ ہے کہ اس کے علاوہ وقت میں مشروع باقی نہیں رہے گا پس واجب کو درست قرار دیا جائے گا مطلق اسم صوم کے ساتھ اور وصف میں خطا کے ساتھ مگر مسافر کے حق میں کہ وہ نیت کرے دوسرے واجب کی امام ابو حنیفہ اللہ کے نزدیک ، اور اگر مسافر نے نفل روزے کی نیت کی تو اس میں دوروایتیں ہیں، اور بہر حال مریض پس صحیح قول ہمارے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ واقع ہوگا اس کا روزہ فرض سے ہر حال میں ، اس لئے کہ مریض کی رخصت متعلق ہے حقیقت عجز کے ساتھ پس ظاہر ہو جائے گا نفس روزہ سے رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا، پس مریض کو لاحق کیا جائے گا تندرست کے ساتھ ، اور بہر حال مسافر پس وہ مستحق ہوتا ہے رخصت کا عجز تقدیری کے ساتھ ، عجز کے سبب کے قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ سفر ہے، تو نہیں ظاہر ہوگا نفس روزہ سے رخصت کی شرط کا فوت ہونا ، لہذا رخصت باطل نہیں ہوگی ، پس یہ رخصت متعدی ہوگی دلالت کے طریقہ پر اس کی حاجت دینیہ کی طرف۔

تشریح:- مصنف سے مامور بہ مقید بالوقت کی دوسری قسم کو بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ جس میں وقت مامور بہ کے لئے معیار ہو، اور وجوب کے لئے سبب ہو، پہلی قسم میں وقت ظرف تھا، اور یہاں معیار ہے، معیار ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے که مامور بہ پورے وقت کو گھیرے ہوئے ہو، اس طریقہ پر کہ وقت کے گھٹنے بڑھنے سے مامور بہ بھی گھٹے بڑھے، جیسے روزے کا وقت روزے کے لئے معیار ہے، روزہ وقت (دن) کے ساتھ اس طرح مقدر ہے کہ دن کے گھٹنے بڑھنے سے روزہ بھی گھٹتا بڑھتا ہے، اور روزہ کی اضافت صوم کی طرف کر کے کہتے ہیں ”صومُ رَمَضَانَ ، یہ اضافت سبیت کی دلیل ہے، اضافت کی صورت میں مضاف الیہ مضاف کا سبب ہوتا ہے۔ اس نوع ثانی کا حکم یہ ہے کہ چونکہ اس میں وقت معیار ہوتا ہے، تو وقت کے ساتھ جو مامور بہ ہے اس کے علاوہ کسی وقت میں دوسرے فعل کی گنجائش ہی نہیں ہے، یعنی رمضان میں غیر رمضان کے روزے کی گنجائش ہی نہیں ہے بلکہ رمضان کا مہینہ صوم رمضان کے لئے متعین ہو گیا تو اب اگر کوئی مطلق صوم کی نیت کرے جیسے دل یا زبان سے کہے کہ میں نے روزہ کی نیت کی ، تو رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا، نیت سے متعین کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، اسی طرح خطافی الوصف کے ساتھ نیت کی تو بھی رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا ، جیسے رمضان میں نفل روزے کی نیت کی ، یا قضاء، یا کفارہ یا نذر کے روزے کی نیت کی تو بھی رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا، جو نیت کی ہے وہ روزہ نہ ہوگا ، کیونکہ رمضان کا مہینہ صوم رمضان کے لئے معیار ہونے کی وجہ سے متعین ہے، لہذا اس نے غلطی سے جو وصف بیان کیا یعنی قضاء کفارہ وغیرہ یہ باطل ہو جائے گا، تندرست، مقیم کے لئے تو یہی حکم ہے، البتہ مریض و مسافر کے لئے کچھ تفصیل ہے۔ الا فى المسافر - مسافر کے بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ علی نے فرمایا کہ اگر وہ رمضان میں دوسرے واجب کی نیت کرتا ہے، تو وہ دوسرا واجب ادا ہوگا ، اور اگر نفل کی نیت کرتا ہے تو امام صاحب سے دور وایتیں ہیں ،مگر اصح قول یہی ہے کہ رمضان ہی کا روزہ ادا ہو گا۔ اور مریض کے بارے میں اگر چہ کئی اقوال ہیں، بعض احناف کہتے ہیں کہ مریض کا حکم بھی بعینہ مسافر کا حکم
And the second type is that in which time is made a measure for the commanded act and a cause for its obligation, and it is the time of fasting. Do you not see that it is measured by it and attributed to it? And from its ruling is that no other act remains valid in it, so it is validated with the absolute name and with error in description, except in the case of the traveler who intends another obligatory, according to Abu Hanifa; and if he intends supererogatory, there are two narrations. As for the sick person, the correct view with us is that his fast counts as the obligatory in every case because his license (rukhsa) is attached to the reality of incapacity, so the loss of the condition of license becomes apparent through the fast itself, so he is considered like the healthy. As for the traveler, he deserves the license due to a presumptive incapacity because its cause (travel) exists, so the loss of the condition of license does not become apparent through the fast itself, so the license is not invalidated, and then it extends by way of indication to his religious need.

Translation: The second type of time-bound command is that in which time is made a measure for the commanded act and a cause for its obligation, and that is the time of fasting. Do you not see that fasting is estimated by time and attributed to time, and among the rulings of this type is that nothing else remains valid in it except it, so the obligation is validated with the absolute name of fasting and with error in description, except in the case of the traveler that he intends another obligatory according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and if the traveler intends supererogatory fasting, then there are two narrations. As for the sick person, the correct view with us is that his fasting counts as the obligatory in every case, because the license for the sick is attached to the reality of incapacity, so the loss of the condition of license becomes apparent through the fasting itself, so the sick person is attached to the healthy. As for the traveler, he deserves the license due to presumptive incapacity because its cause (travel) exists, so the loss of the condition of license does not become apparent through the fasting itself, so the license is not invalidated, and then this license extends by way of indication to his religious need.

Commentary: The author (Mussanif) is explaining the second type of time-bound commanded act, in which time is a measure for the commanded act and a cause for its obligation. In the first type, time was a vessel (zarf), and here it is a measure (mi'yar). The meaning of being a measure is that the commanded act encompasses the entire time, such that as time decreases or increases, the commanded act decreases or increases, like the time of fasting is a measure for fasting. Fasting is estimated with time (the day) such that as the day decreases or increases, fasting decreases or increases. Attribution of fasting to time (sawmu Ramadān) is evidence of causation; in attribution, the thing attributed (mudaf ilayh) is the cause of the mudaf. The ruling of this second type is that since time is a measure, there is no room for any other act in that time besides the commanded act, i.e., in Ramadan there is no room for a non-Ramadan fast. Rather, the month of Ramadan is specified for the fast of Ramadan. So if someone intends the absolute fast (sawm mutlaq) – like saying with heart or tongue 'I intend fasting' – it will be the fast of Ramadan; there is no need to specify. Similarly, if he intends with an error in description, it will still be the Ramadan fast, e.g., if in Ramadan he intends a supererogatory fast, or a qada, kaffarah, or nadhr fast, it will still be the Ramadan fast; what he intended will not occur because the month of Ramadan is specified as a measure for the Ramadan fast, so the incorrect description (qada, kaffarah, etc.) becomes void. This ruling applies to the healthy, resident person. However, for the sick and traveler, there is some detail. Alā fil-musāfir: Regarding the traveler, Imam Abu Hanifa said that if he intends another wajib in Ramadan, that other wajib will be fulfilled; and if he intends nafl, there are two narrations from the Imam, but the strongest view is that it will be the Ramadan fast. Regarding the sick person, there are several opinions; some Hanafis say that the rule for the sick is exactly the same as for the traveler.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) on Al-Husami, explaining the second type of time-bound (muqayyad bi al-waqt) commanded acts. The author distinguishes between two types: the first (discussed earlier) where time is a vessel (zarf) for the act, like prayer times; the second, where time is a measure (mi'yar) and cause (sabab) for the obligation itself. The example given is the fast of Ramadan. The key principle: in the second type, the time (Ramadan) is so specific to the commanded act (fasting) that no other type of fast can be intended in that time. If someone intends an absolute fast (sawm mutlaq) or even mistakenly intends a qada, kaffarah, or nafl fast, it automatically becomes the Ramadan fast. This is because the time itself determines the obligation. The exception is the traveler: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a traveler intends another wajib fast (like qada), that wajib is fulfilled instead of the Ramadan fast, and if he intends nafl, there are two narrations (the stronger one is that it becomes Ramadan fast). The sick person's fast always counts as the obligatory fast (Ramadan) because the license (rukhsa) for the sick is based on actual incapacity, which disappears upon fasting, so they are like the healthy. The traveler's license is based on a presumptive incapacity (due to travel), so the license remains and can be applied through indication to other religious needs. The Urdu translation and commentary clarify these points by explaining the concept of 'measure' (mi'yar) and the attribution (idafa) as evidence of causation.

Key Terms
الرخصة (al-rukhsa): License: a concession granted by the Lawgiver allowing a deviation from the original ruling due to an excuse. Here, the traveler and sick person have rukhsa to not fast.
المسافر (al-musafir): Traveler: one who undertakes a journey of three days or more (according to Hanafi fiqh) and is entitled to the license (rukhsa) of not fasting and shortening prayers.
عجز حقيقي (ajz haqiqi): Actual incapacity: the inability to perform the act due to genuine illness or weakness.
عجز تقديري (ajz taqdiri): Presumptive incapacity: the assumed inability due to travel, even if the person is physically able to fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the sick person's fast always count as the Ramadan fast, according to the passage?
A) Because the sick person has a stronger intention.
B) Because the sick person's license is based on actual incapacity, which disappears upon fasting.
C) Because the sick person is not considered a traveler.
D) Because the sick person must always make up the fast later.

Key Takeaway
The traveler's license is based on presumptive incapacity and persists during fasting, allowing a different wajib intention; the sick's license is based on actual incapacity and disappears, making the fast count as Ramadan.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Dispute on Hajj Timing: Fawr vs Tarakhkhi
Explains the dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on whether Hajj is immediate or delayed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding whether Hajj is obligatory immediately (fawr) or with delay (tarakhkhi), identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf), and apply the concept of dalalat al-hal to derive the ruling from absolute intention.

Core Idea
The dispute on Hajj timing only affects sin, not validity: both imams agree that later performance is ada, not qada.

This passage from the sharh of al-Husami presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the obligation of Hajj must be performed in the first available year or can be delayed. The discussion hinges on the nature of time—whether life is a measure (miyar) offering one chance, or a container (zarf) offering multiple opportunities. The analysis also addresses the effect on nafil Hajj and the use of dalalat al-hal to specify intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and the two positions
State the question: after Hajj becomes obligatory, must it be performed in the first year (fawr) or can it be delayed (tarakhkhi)? Identify Imam Muhammad's view (tarakhkhi) and Imam Abu Yusuf's view (fawr).
2
Analyze the reasoning: miyar vs zarf
Understand how each imam views the nature of time in the obligated person's life. Imam Muhammad considers life a container (zarf) with multiple opportunities; Imam Abu Yusuf considers it a measure (miyar) with a single opportunity, leading to precaution.
The ambiguity arises because it is uncertain whether the person will survive subsequent years.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: both imams agree that Hajj performed later is ada, not qada. The only difference is sin: according to Abu Yusuf, delaying the first year incurs sin (and testimony rejection) until performed; according to Muhammad, sin only occurs at death without performance.
The text explicitly says the dispute only affects sin, not validity of nafil or other matters.
4
Extend to nafil Hajj
Explain why the dispute does not affect the validity of nafil Hajj: the time (life) has capacity for both fard and nafil. Even if one delays the fard, nafil performed is valid. Imam Shafi'i's opposing view is noted: he considers nafil invalid when fard is outstanding.
Both Hanafi imams agree on this point; the dispute is only about sin.
5
Apply dalalat al-hal to absolute intention
Understand the answer to the objection: if one makes an absolute intention for Hajj (without specifying fard or nafil), the fard is fulfilled because the context (dalalat al-hal) indicates the intent to fulfill the obligation. This distinguishes Hajj from prayer, where absolute intention does not specify fard.
The passage uses the example of prayer to contrast: in prayer, the time has capacity for both, but there is no contextual indication (like an outstanding obligation) to specify fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور دوسرا طریقہ یہ کہ حج زندگی میں ایک مرتبہ فرض ہے، اور اس کا وقت اشھر حج ہے نہ کہ سارے مہینے ، پس یہ شخص حج فرض ہونے کے بعد اسی سال حج کا زمانہ گذر جانے کے بعد مر گیا، اس نے دوسرا، تیسر اسال نہ پایا تو گویا اس کی زندگی میں ایک ہی حج کی گنجائش تھی اس لحاظ سے وقت معیار کے مشابہ ہو گیا ، اور اگر مکلف حج فرض ہونے کے بعد کچھ سال زندہ رہا اور پہلے سال حج ادا نہیں کر سکا تو دوسرے تیسرے یا چوتھے سال میں بھی ادا کر سکتا ہے تو گویا اس کی زندگی میں ایک سے زائد حج کی گنجائش ہے تو اس لحاظ سے زندگی کا وقت ظرف کے مشابہ ہو گیا، مگر چونکہ حج فرض ہونے کے سال کے بعد اس کا زندہ رہنا یا نہ رہنا کچھ متعین نہیں ہے، اس لئے مکلف کی زندگی کو حج کے لئے معیار اور ظرف کہنا مشتبہ ہو گیا، یقینی طور پر ظرف بھی نہیں کہہ سکتے ، اور نہ معیار کہہ سکتے ہیں ، مصنف اللہ نے پہلے اشتباہ کو بوقت مشکل توسعه سے بیان کیا ہے اور دوسرے اشتباہ کو فانه فرض العمر" سے بیان کیا ہے۔ بہر حال حج کا وقت جب مشتبہ ہے اور وقت میں توسع اور تنگی دونوں پہلو ہیں، تو امام محمد اسی نے توسع کا پہلو اختیار کیا اور فرمایا کہ پہلے سال اشھر حج میں ادا ئیگی واجب نہیں ہے، بلکہ دوسرے تیسرے سال بھی اور اسی طرح آگے تک ادا کر سکتا ہے لیکن شرط ہے کہ فوت نہ ہو، زندگی میں ادا ہو جانا چاہیے ، اور امام ابو یوسف نے نے وقت کی تنگی کا اعتبار کیا اور فرمایا کہ احتیاط کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ پہلے سال کے اشہر حج میں ادا واجب ہے تا کہ حج فوت نہ ہو جائے ، تو امام محمد کے نزدیک حج علی التراخی واجب ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اللہ کے نزدیک علی الفور واجب ہے۔ وظهر ذلک: - صاحبین کے درمیان اختلاف کا ثمرہ صرف گناہ میں ظاہر ہوگا اور کسی چیز میں نہیں یعنی اگر پہلے سال ادا نہ کیا تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک گنہگار ہوگا ، فاسق اور مردود الشہادۃ ہوگا پھر جب دوسرے یا تیسرے سال ادا کر دیا تو گناہ ختم اور مردود الشہادۃ ہو نا ختم ہو جائے گا ، اور امام محمد عطاللہ کے نزدیک موت تک اگر ادا نہیں کر سکا تو گنہگار ہوگا، ورنہ تاخیر سے گنہگار نہ ہوگا، لیکن جب بھی ادا کرے گا بہر صورت ادا ہی ہوگا قضا نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب حسامی اے نے لا غیر پر تفریح کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ صاحبین کے اختلاف کا ثمر ہ صرف گناہ میں ظاہر ہوگا نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ میں ، اس لئے نفل کی مشروعیت علی حالہ باقی رہے گی یعنی اگر کسی پر حج فرض ہے اور وہ نفل حج کی نیت کرے تو بالا تفاق نفل حج صحیح ہو جائے گا نفلی حج کی نیت سے فریضہ حج ادا نہ ہوگا کیونکہ وقت یعنی مکلف کی زندگی میں جیسے ادائے فرض کی صلاحیت ہے ، ایسے ہی ادائے نفل کی بھی صلاحیت ہے ، تو جو نیت کرے گا وہ ادا ہوگا جیسے نماز کا وقت اس میں نفل کی بھی صلاحیت ہے اور فرض کی بھی ، پس اگر کسی نے فرض ادا نہ کی نفل ادا کی تو نفل ادا ہو جائے گی۔ اور رہا امام ابو یوسف علی کا پہلے سال کو حج فرض کے لئے متعین کرنا تو یہ تعیین فوت ہونے سے بچنے کے لئے احتیاط کی وجہ سے ہے، ورنہ یہ تعین صحت نفل کے سلسلہ میں اثر انداز نہیں ہے یعنی صحت نفل کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے البتہ امام شافعی سے نفل کی نیت کو لغو قرار دیتے ہیں جب کہ اس پر فرض باقی ہو، لہذا اگر نفل حج کی بھی نیت کرے گا تو فرض ہی ادا ہوگا۔ وجوازه عند الاطلاق :- ایک سوال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ جب وقت میں فرض اور نفل دونوں کی صلاحیت ہے تو اگر کوئی مطلق حج کی نیت کرے تو اس سے حج فرض ادا نہ ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ وقت میں فرض اور نفل دونوں کی صلاحیت ہے، جیسے کہ نماز کے وقت میں کوئی مطلق نماز کی نیت کرتا ہے تو فرض نماز ادا نہیں ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ وقت میں فرض اور نفل دونوں کی صلاحیت ہے ایسے ہی حج میں ہونا چاہیے، حالانکہ آپ کہتے ہیں کہ مطلق نیت سے حج فرض ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں فرض کی تعیین اگر چہ مکلف نے زبان سے نہیں کی ہے، مگر دلالت حال سے فرض کی تعیین ہوگئی ، کیونکہ جب مسلمان پر حج فرض ہوا اور وہ مطلق حج کی نیت کرے تو اس کا ظاہر حال یہ بتلاتا ہے کہ اس نے نفل کی نیت نہیں کی ہوگی بلکہ واجب حج کا ہی ارادہ کیا ہوگا ، پس دلالت حال سے فرض کی تعیین ہو گئی ، لہذا مطلق نیست سے فرض ادا ہو گا۔
The second method is that Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime, and its time is the months of Hajj, not all months. So this person became obligated for Hajj, then died after the time of Hajj passed that year, and he did not find a second or third year, so as if in his life there was only one opportunity for Hajj; from this perspective time became analogous to a measure. And if the obligated person lived some years after Hajj became obligatory and could not perform it the first year, he can perform it in the second, third, or fourth year, so as if in his life there is more than one opportunity for Hajj; from this perspective the time of life became analogous to a container. But because it is not determined whether he will survive after the year of obligation, calling the obligated person's life a measure or container for Hajj becomes ambiguous. We cannot definitively call it a container nor a measure. The author expressed the first ambiguity as 'بوقت مشکل توسعه' and the second ambiguity as 'فانه فرض العمر'. In any case, since the time of Hajj is ambiguous and has both expansion and contraction aspects, Imam Muhammad took the aspect of expansion and ruled that performance in the months of Hajj of the first year is not obligatory; rather he can perform it in the second, third, and so on, provided he does not die; it must be performed in his lifetime. Imam Abu Yusuf considered the aspect of contraction and ruled that precaution requires that performance is obligatory in the months of Hajj of the first year so that Hajj is not missed. So according to Imam Muhammad, Hajj is obligatory with delay (ala al-tarakhkhi), and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is obligatory immediately (ala al-fawr). The result: The fruit of the dispute between the two companions appears only in sin, not in anything else. That is, if one does not perform in the first year, according to Abu Yusuf he becomes sinful, a transgressor, and his testimony is rejected; then when he performs in the second or third year, the sin ends and the rejection of testimony ends. According to Imam Muhammad, if he cannot perform until death, he becomes sinful; otherwise delay does not make him sinful. But whenever he performs, in any case it will be ada, not qada. The author of al-Husami, commenting on 'لا غیر', said that the fruit of the dispute between the two companions appears only in sin, not otherwise. Therefore, the legitimacy of nafil remains as it is: if someone has Hajj obligatory and intends nafil Hajj, by consensus the nafil Hajj is valid; the obligatory Hajj is not performed by the intention of nafil. Because the time (i.e., the obligated person's life) has capacity for both performing the obligation and performing nafil. So whatever one intends will be performed, just as the time of prayer has capacity for both nafil and fard. So if someone does not perform fard but performs nafil, the nafil is performed. As for Imam Abu Yusuf's specification of the first year for Hajj, this specification is due to precaution to avoid missing it; otherwise, this specification does not affect the validity of nafil, i.e., it is not a preventer for the validity of nafil. However, Imam al-Shafi'i considers the intention of nafil invalid when there is an outstanding fard; so if one intends nafil Hajj, only the fard is performed. The permissibility of absolute intention (jawazuhu 'inda al-itlaq) is a response to a question: When the time has capacity for both fard and nafil, if someone intends absolute Hajj, the fard Hajj should not be performed because the time has capacity for both, like in prayer: if someone intends absolute prayer, the fard prayer is not performed because the time has capacity for both. This is what you say: with absolute intention, fard Hajj is performed. The answer: Here the specification of fard, even though not spoken verbally, is specified by the context (dalalat al-hal), because when a Muslim has Hajj obligatory and intends absolute Hajj, his apparent state indicates that he did not intend nafil but rather intended the obligatory Hajj. So specification of fard occurs by context, and thus from absolute intention the fard is performed.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in Hanafi usul regarding the timing of a wajib act — specifically whether Hajj, when it becomes obligatory, must be performed immediately (fawr) or can be delayed (tarakhkhi). The discussion begins by analyzing the nature of time in relation to the obligation. The author explains two possibilities: if the obligated person dies soon after Hajj becomes obligatory, then life served as a 'measure' (miyar) for a single Hajj; but if he lives several years, life is like a 'container' (zarf) that can accommodate multiple opportunities. Since it is unknown after the first year whether one will survive, both possibilities exist, leading to ambiguity. Imam Muhammad takes the expansive view: performance in the first year is not obligatory; one may delay as long as life remains, provided it is performed before death. Imam Abu Yusuf takes the restrictive view: precaution requires immediate performance in the first year to avoid missing the obligation. The practical result (thamara) of this ikhtilaf is only in terms of sin: Abu Yusuf holds that delaying without excuse incurs sin even if performed later; Muhammad holds that sin only occurs at death without performance. Importantly, the validity of nafil Hajj is unaffected by this dispute because the time has capacity for both fard and nafil. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if one makes an absolute intention (mutlaq niyyah) for Hajj without specifying fard or nafil, why does the fard become fulfilled? The answer is that the context (dalalat al-hal) indicates the intent to fulfill the obligation, since the person has an outstanding fard. This is a Hanafi position; the Shafi'i view is that absolute intention would not fulfill the fard because the time can accommodate both. The Hanafi response uses the concept of 'dalalat al-hal' to distinguish between the case of Hajj and the case of prayer (salat), where absolute intention does not automatically fulfill the fard.

Key Terms
معیار (miyar): Time as a measure: life allows only one opportunity for Hajj.
ظرف (zarf): Time as a container: life can accommodate multiple opportunities for Hajj.
علی الفور (ala al-fawr): Ruling that performance is obligatory immediately.
علی التراخی (ala al-tarakhkhi): Ruling that performance is obligatory with delay.
دلالت حال (dalalat al-hal): Contextual indication that specifies the intent from an absolute expression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if a person delays Hajj beyond the first year without excuse, what is the consequence?
A) The Hajj becomes qada.
B) He becomes sinful and his testimony is rejected until he performs it.
C) The nafil Hajj becomes invalid.
D) He is not sinful as long as he performs it before death.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accommodates two valid views on the timing of Hajj obligation; the practical difference is only sin, and the validity of nafil remains unaffected, with context (dalalat al-hal) specifying the intention.

Ada and Qada: Definitions and the Cause of Obligation
Defines ada and qada and discusses the ikhtilaf on the cause of qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada and qada in Hanafi usul and explain why the majority of mashayikh hold that qada is obligated by the same cause (khitab) as ada.

Core Idea
Ada is delivering the exact wajib in time; qada is dropping it by a substitute; both arise from the same divine command.

This lesson introduces two fundamental terms in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: ada and qada. Understanding them is essential for grasping how obligations persist beyond their appointed times. The passage also presents an internal Hanafi dispute: what exactly obligates qada — a specific textual command or the original divine address? The majority view, which we will analyze, has far-reaching implications for how qada extends to various acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Define Ada
Identify the definition of ada: delivering the very wajib (ayn al-wajib) by its cause (sabab) to its due recipient within the appointed time.
Focus on 'ayn al-wajib' – the exact act itself, not a substitute.
2
Define Qada
Identify the definition of qada: dropping the obligation (isqat al-wajib) by performing a substitute (mithl) from the mukallaf himself.
The substitute comes from the obligated person; it is his right (haqq) to use a substitute.
3
Recognize the Ikhtilaf
Note the disagreement among the mashayikh: some say qada requires a specific text (nas); the majority say it is by the same cause (khitab) that made ada wajib.
The majority's reasoning is based on the survival of the original wajib's basis (asl) and the ability to perform its equivalent.
4
Understand the Analogy (Qiyas)
The majority extends the principle from the cases where qada is textually established (prayer and fasting) to other obligations like specified vows, using qiyas.
This is a rational extension (ma'qul) based on the common illa: the obligation remains after the time passes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي حُكْمِ الْوَاجِبِ بِالْاَمْرِوَهُوَ نَوْعَانِ آدَاءً وَهُوَ تَسْلِيْمٌ عَيْنِ الْوَاجِبِ بِسَبَبِهِ إِلَى مُسْتَحِقِهِ وَقَضَاءً وَهُوَ اسْقَاطُ الْوَاجب بِمِثْلِ مِنْ عِنْدِهِ وَهُوَ حَقُهُ وَاخْتَلَفَ الْمَشَائِخَ فِي أَنَّ الْقَضَاءَ يَجِبْ بِنَضِ مَقْصُوْدِ أَمْ بِالسَّبَبِ الَّذِي يُوجِبُ الْأَدَاءَ قَالَ عَامَتُهُمْ بِأَنَّهُ يَجِبْ بِذلِكَ السَّبَبِ وَهُوَ الْخِطَاب لِأَنَّ بَقَاءَ اَصْلِ الْوَاجِبِ لِلْقَدْرَةِ عَلَى مِثْلٍ مِنْ عِنْدِهِ قُرْبَة وَسُقُوطَ فَضْلِ الْوَقْتِ لَا إِلَى مِثْلٍ وَضَمَانٍ لِلْعَجْزِ اَمْرٌ مَعْقُول فِى الْمَنْصُوصِ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ قَضَاءُ الصَّوْمِ وَالصَّلوةِ فَيَتَعَدّى إِلَى الْمَنْذُورَاتِ الْمُتَعَيَّنَةِ مِنَ الصَّلوةِ وَالصِّيَامِ وَالْإِعْتَكَافِ ترجمہ : ۔ یہ فصل ہے اس واجب کے حکم کے بیان میں جو امر سے واجب ہوا ہے اور اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں ،اداء اور وہ سپر دکرنا ہے بعینہ اس چیز کو جو واجب ہوئی ہے امر کے سبب سے اس کے مستحق کی طرف ، اور قضا اور وہ ساقط کرنا ہے واجب کا ایسے مثل کے ذریعہ جو مکلف کی جانب سے ہو اور وہ مثل مکلف کا حق ہے، اور اختلاف کیا ہے مشائخ نے اس بات میں کہ قضا واجب ہوتی ہے نص مقصود سے یا اس سبب سے جو ادا کو واجب کرتا ہے، عام مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ جوادا
Chapter on the ruling of the wajib by command, and it is of two types: Ada, which is the delivery of the very wajib by its cause to its due recipient; and Qada, which is the dropping of the wajib by a substitute from himself, and that substitute is his right. And the mashayikh differed regarding whether qada becomes obligatory by the intended text (nas) or by the cause that obligates ada. The majority of them said that it becomes obligatory by that cause, i.e., the address (khitab), because the survival of the origin of the wajib for the ability to produce a substitute from himself as an act of worship, and the dropping of the extra (superiority) of time not to a substitute, and a guarantee for incapacity, is a rational matter in what is explicitly mentioned (mansus 'alayh), and that is the qada of fasting and prayer. So it extends to the specified vows (manzurat) from prayer, fasting, and i'tikaf.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a definition and discussion of two key concepts in usul al-fiqh: ada and qada as applied to wajib that arises from a command (amr). Ada is defined as delivering the exact wajib (the same act) to its due recipient—that is, performing the act as commanded within its time. Qada is defined as dropping (removing) the liability of the wajib by performing its substitute (mithl) that comes from the obligated person himself, and that substitute is considered his due. The text then presents an ikhtilaf among the mashayikh (Hanafi scholars) about what obligates qada: is it a specific textual command (nas) regarding qada, or is it the same cause (sabab) that originally made ada wajib (i.e., the divine address/khitab)? The majority (aammatuhum) hold that qada is obligated by that same cause, because the original wajib remains in terms of liability, and when one gains the ability to perform its substitute (mithl), that substitute stands in for the original. The reason is that the specific time (of ada) is only a merit (fadl) that falls away when missed, but the underlying obligation does not. The passage states that this is rationally understood (ma'qul) in the matters explicitly addressed by nass—namely qada of fasts and prayers—and it extends by analogy to specific vows (manzurat mu'ayyanah) of prayer, fasting, and i'tikaf. The Urdu translation reiterates the definitions and confirms the majority view.

Key Terms
آداء (ada'): Performing the exact wajib act as commanded to the recipient (Allah) within its appointed time.
قضاء (qada'): Fulfilling the wajib by a substitute (mithl) performed by the obligated person after the time has passed.
الخطاب (al-khitab): The divine address (command) that made the act wajib in the first place.
النص المقصود (al-nas al-maqsud): A specific textual command (from Quran or Sunnah) that directly orders qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, what makes qada obligatory?
A) A separate textual command (nas) from the Quran or Sunnah.
B) The same divine address (khitab) that made ada wajib, because the obligation remains.
C) The requirement of the time itself.
D) The discretion of the imam.

Key Takeaway
Ada delivers the exact wajib; qada is a substitute for a missed wajib, and both are obligated by the same divine command according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Definitions of Ada and Qada and the Cause of Qada
Defining ada and qada and the dispute over qada's cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada and qada and state the Hanafi position on the cause of qada.

Core Idea
Qada is obligated by the same command as ada — the obligation persists until performed.

This passage introduces the key concepts of ada (performance) and qada (make-up) in Hanafi usul. It clarifies the technical definitions and then examines a debated issue: does make-up require a separate command, or does the original command suffice? Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping how obligations are maintained over time.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two types of wajib by command
The passage divides the wajib into two categories: ada (performance) and qada (make-up). Note the key difference: ada delivers the exact wajib within its time; qada drops the obligation by a similar act from oneself.
2
Understand the definitions technically
In ada, one delivers the very wajib (e.g., the specific prayer) to its rightful recipient (Allah). In qada, one drops the obligation by performing a similar act, and that act is considered the person's own right because it uses his own time.
The phrase 'from oneself' (min ʿindihī) distinguishes qada from ada.
3
Identify the dispute about qada's cause
The mashayikh disagreed: does qada become wajib by a new textual command (nas maqsūd) or by the same cause (sabab) that obligated ada? The sabab is the khitāb (divine address).
4
Follow the majority Hanafi argument
The majority (ʿāmmatuhum) said the same khitāb obligates qada. Their proof: the essence of the wajib remains due to ability to perform a similar act as worship, and the loss of time excellence is without compensation due to incapacity. This is rationally understood from textual examples like qada of fasting and prayer.
The argument uses both reason (ʿaql) and textual evidence (naṣṣ).
5
Extend the principle to vowed acts
Since the same khitāb applies, the obligation of qada extends to specified vowed acts (manẓūrāt) of prayer, fasting, and iʿtikāf, because they share the same nature.

لہذا مکلف کا اپنی طرف سے سپرد کرنا نہ ہوا۔ البتہ اگر وہ کل کی ظہر آج پڑھ رہا ہے، تو یہ جو وقت ظہر کے لئے دے رہا ہے یہ مکلف کا حق ہے، اس میں وہ آرام بھی کر سکتا ہے ، اور کوئی کام بھی کر سکتا ہے لیکن اس کبھی ادا اور قضا کو مجازاً ایک دوسرے کی جگہ استعمال کرتے ہیں ، فاذا قضيتم مناسككم اى اديتم - قضا بمعنى ادا ہے فاذ اقضيت الصلوة بمعنی ادیت اور نویت ان أُودَى ظہر الامس ،ای اقضی ادا بمعنی قضا ہے۔ واختلف المشائخ - مشائخ کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ کیا ادا جس سبب سے یعنی خطاب سے واجب ہوتی ہے اسی سے قضا بھی واجب ہوتی ہے یا قضا کے لئے نص جدید کی ضرورت ، یہاں سبب سے مراد امر ہے ،سبب
Chapter on the ruling of the wajib by command, and it is of two types: ada, which is the delivery of the very wajib by its cause to its rightful recipient; and qada, which is the dropping of the wajib by a similar [act] from oneself, and it is his right. The mashayikh disagreed whether qada is obligated by the intended text (nas) or by the cause that obligates ada. The majority said that it is obligated by that cause, which is the address (khitab), because the survival of the essence of the wajib due to ability to perform a similar act as an act of worship, and the falling away of the excellence of the time without a similar [act] and compensation due to incapacity, is a rational matter in what is textually specified, which is qada of fasting and prayer, so it extends to specified vowed acts of prayer, fasting and i'tikaf. Translation: This chapter is about the ruling of the wajib that becomes wajib by command, and it has two types: ada, which is to deliver the very thing that became wajib by the cause to its rightful recipient; and qada, which is to drop the wajib by means of a similar [act] from the responsible person, and that similar act is his right. The mashayikh differed as to whether qada is obligated by the intended text or by the cause that obligates ada. The common mashayikh said that qada is obligated by that same cause, which is the address (khitab), because the survival of the essence of the wajib as an act of worship due to ability to perform a similar act, and the falling away of the excellence of the time without a similar act and compensation due to incapacity, is a rational matter in what is textually specified, which is qada of prayer and fasting, so this obligation extends to specified vowed acts of prayer, fasting and i'tikaf. Explanation: The author says that the wajib established by command is of two types: (1) obligation of ada, (2) obligation of qada. Obligation of ada is: to deliver the very thing that became wajib in the dhimmah due to its cause to its rightful recipient. This definition includes time-bound wajib like prayer and fasting, and non-time-bound wajib like zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. 'Delivery' here means bringing into existence from non-existence, discharging one's dhimmah; otherwise ada is an act which is not delivered. Qada is: the responsible person dropping that which is wajib in his dhimmah by means of a similar [act] from himself, which is his right. The author used two expressions for mention: 'by a similar from himself' and 'it is his right': he gives a similar from himself and that similar is the person's right, because in ada what he delivers is not his right but Allah's right. For example, today's Zuhr and yesterday's Zuhr are both obligatory. The time he spends today for Zuhr is Allah's right because Allah specified that time for Zuhr, it is not the servant's right, so he did not deliver from himself. But if he is praying yesterday's Zuhr today, the time he gives is his right; he could rest or do other work, but he used this time for Zuhr and fulfilled the qada that was wajib, so he delivered the qada from himself, which was his own right. 'And it is his right' emphasizes 'from himself'; if they hadn't said 'from himself', the definition of ada would apply to qada as well, but when they said 'from himself', the difference between qada and ada became clear: in ada, the time spent is not from the servant; in qada, the time spent is from the servant. Benefit: Keep in mind that sometimes ada and qada are used metaphorically in place of each other: 'fā idhā qadaytum manāsikakum' i.e. adaytum; qada in the sense of ada; 'fā idhā qadaytu al-salāta' meaning adaytu; and 'nawaytu an u'addiya Zuhr al-ams' i.e. aqdiya; ada in the sense of qada. 'And the mashayikh differed' - the mashayikh differed over whether qada is obligated by the same cause, i.e., the address (khitab), that obligates ada, or requires a new text. Here 'cause' means the command.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a chapter (fasl) on the ruling of the wajib that becomes obligatory by command. It defines two categories: ada (performance) and qada (make-up). Ada is delivering the exact wajib (e.g., the specific prayer) to its rightful recipient (Allah) within its time. Qada is dropping the obligation by performing a similar act from one's own side, and that act is considered the person's own right because the time used is not divinely allocated. The Hanafi mashayikh disagreed: does qada become wajib by a new textual command (nas) or by the same original command (khitab)? The majority said by the same command, because when one is unable to perform in time, the obligation remains due to ability to do a similar act later, and the excellence of the time is lost without compensation. This is rationally understood from the textual examples of fasting and prayer, and it extends to vowed acts of the same nature. The commentary elaborates: in ada, one delivers what is Allah's right; in qada, one delivers from his own right (i.e., using his free time for worship). The passage also notes that ada and qada can be used metaphorically. The disagreement among mashayikh is over the cause: is it the same command or a new text? The text favors the majority view that it is the same command.

Key Terms
أداء (adā'): Delivery of the exact wajib by its cause to its rightful recipient (Allah) within its specified time.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Dropping the wajib by performing a similar act from oneself, which is considered the person's own right.
خطاب (khiṭāb): The divine address (command) that obligates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, what is the cause of the obligation of qada?
A) A new text (nas) specifically commanding qada.
B) The same cause (khitab) that obligates ada.
C) The intention of the worshipper.
D) The consensus of the community.

Key Takeaway
Ada delivers the exact wajib in its time; qada drops the same wajib by a similar act later, both obligated by the same divine command.

Pure Performance and Types of Ada in Hanafi Usul
Defines pure ada and classifies types: individual and lahiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish pure ada from deficient ada and ada resembling qada, and apply the definition to classify the acts of the munfarid, lahiq, and masbuq.

Core Idea
Pure performance is acting exactly as legislated; deficiency or resemblance does not change the category of ada.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the concept of ada (performance) is fundamental to understanding how acts of worship are classified. This passage by al-Husami breaks down pure ada (ada' mahd) and contrasts it with deficient forms, including the unique case of the lahiq. Mastering these distinctions is essential for correctly deriving rulings related to congregation, recitation, and the nature of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of pure ada
Locate the key phrase: 'what a person performs with its description as prescribed.' This means the act must be done exactly as legislated, including all recommended and obligatory features.
The example given is prayer in congregation.
2
Recognize the example of pure ada
Prayer in congregation fulfills all descriptions (jahr, following imam, etc.), making it pure ada. Understand that this is the ideal.
3
Contrast with deficient ada (individual prayer)
Individual prayer (munfarid) is still ada, but deficient because jahr (loud recitation) is dropped. Deficiency does not make it qada.
The passage asks: 'Do you not see that loud recitation is dropped from the individual?'
4
Analyze the lahiq's act
The lahiq joins the imam after the prayer has started and completes alone after the imam finishes. His act is ada resembling qada, because he committed to congregational ada from the start but lost it. The key is the initial intention.
The passage says: 'his obligatory status does not change by intending to join the congregation in this situation.'
5
Distinguish lahiq from masbuq
The masbuq (one who missed some rak'ahs) completes his prayer after the imam's salam, and his completion is clearly ada, not resembling qada. This contrast shows the nuance in the classification.
The passage ends with 'Unlike the masbuq, because he is performing in the completion of his prayer.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْآدَاء الْمَحْضُ مَا يُؤَدِيْهِ الْإِنْسَانُ بِوَصْفِهِ عَلَى مَاشُرِعَ مِثْلُ أَدَاءِ الصَّلُوةِ بِجَمَاعَةٍ وأَمَّا فِعْلُ الْفَرْدِ فَادَاءً فِيْهِ قُصُورٌ أَلَا تَرى أَنَّ الْجَهْرَ سَاقِطْ عَنِ الْمُنْفَرِدِ وَفِعْلُ اللَّاحِقِ بَعْدَ فَرَاغِ الْإِمَامِ اَدَاءً يَشْبَهُ الْقَضَاءَ بِاعْتَبَارِ أَنَّهُ الْتَزَمَ الْأَدَاءَ مَعَ الْأَمَامِ حِيْنَ تَحَرَّمَ مَعَهُ وَقَدْ فَاتَهُ ذَلِكَ حَقِيقَةً وَلِهَذَا لَا يَتَغَيَّرُ فَرْضُهُ بِنِيَّةِ الْآقَامَةِ فِى هَذهِ الْحَالَةِ كَمَا لَوْصَارَ قَضَاءً مَحْضًا بِالْفَوَاتِ ثُمَّ وَجِدَ الْمُغَيْرُ بِخِلَافِ الْمَسْبُوْقِ لِأَنَّهُ مُؤَدٍ فِي إِثْمَامِ صَلُوتِهِ ترجمہ: ۔ پھر اداء محض وہ ہے جس کو انسان اس وصف کے ساتھ ادا کرے جس وصف پر وہ مشروع ہوئی ہے جیسے نماز کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا، بہر حال منفرد کا فعل پس وہ ایسی ادا ہے جس میں قصور ہے، کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ جہر منفرد سے ساقط ہے، اور لاحق کا فعل امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ایسی ادا ہے جو قضا کے مشابہ ہے، اس اعتبار سے کہ اس نے امام کے ساتھ ادا کا التزام کیا ہے، جس وقت کہ اس نے امام کے ساتھ تحریمہ باندھا ہے، اور یہ ادا کا التزام )
Then pure performance is what a person performs with its description as prescribed, such as performing prayer in congregation. As for the act of an individual, it is a performance in which there is deficiency. Do you not see that loud recitation is dropped from the individual? The act of the one who joins (lahiq) after the imam has finished is a performance that resembles qada, considering that he committed to performing with the imam when he entered ihram with him, and that was lost to him in reality. For this reason, his obligatory status does not change by intending to join the congregation in this situation, just as if it had become pure qada due to missing and then the changer was found. Unlike the masbuq, because he is performing in the completion of his prayer.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage defines types of ada' (performance) in Hanafi fiqh. Pure ada (ada' mahd) is the ideal: performing an act exactly as legislated, e.g., praying in congregation with all its prescribed features. Individual prayer (munfarid) is also ada but deficient, as jahr (loud recitation) is dropped. The lahiq – a person who joins the imam after the prayer has started and then after the imam completes, he finishes alone – his act is ada but resembles qada because he committed to the congregation but lost the actual congregational performance. Nonetheless, it remains ada, not qada. This is contrasted with the masbuq (one who misses part of the prayer with the imam), whose completion is clearly ada. The passage emphasizes that the legal classification (fard) does not change despite the resemblance to qada.

Key Terms
الآداء المحض (al-ada' al-mahd): Pure performance: performing an act of worship exactly as legislated with all its recommended aspects.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who joins the imam after the imam has already begun the prayer but before the imam finishes; after the imam finishes, he completes his prayer alone, which is considered ada' resembling qada.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who misses one or more rak'ahs with the imam and completes them after the imam's salam; his act is considered ada (performance).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, a person who joins the imam after the prayer has started (but before the imam finishes) and then completes his prayer alone after the imam's salam is called a:
A) Munfarid
B) Masbuq
C) Lahiq
D) Qada

Key Takeaway
Pure performance is perfect adherence to the legislative description; deficiency or resemblance to qada does not change the fundamental category of ada.

Classification of Types of Ada in Prayer
Defining and classifying types of ada in prayer: complete, deficient, and resembling qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of ada (mahd, qasir, shabih bil qada) and explain the legal effect of niyyat al-iqama for the lahiq and masbuq.

Core Idea
Performance in prayer is classified by its completeness: ada mahd (congregational) is ideal, ada qasir (individual) is deficient, and ada shabih bil qada (lahiq's) resembles makeup.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text introduces a threefold classification of performance (ada) in prayer. It defines ada mahd as the perfect congregation, contrasts it with the deficient performance of a lone worshipper, and introduces the unique category of the lahiq's performance, which resembles qada (makeup) because the original commitment to pray with the imam is lost. Understanding these categories is essential for deriving rules about how intention and circumstances affect the prayer's obligation, especially for travelers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of ada
Find the definitions of ada mahd, ada qasir, and ada shabih bil qada in the text. Note their characteristics.
2
Understand the basis of classification
Why is ada mahd 'pure'? Why is individual prayer 'deficient'? What makes the lahiq's performance resemble qada?
3
Analyze the legal consequence for lahiq
Explain why the lahiq's intention to reside does not change the prayer length, and contrast with the masbuq.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a traveler who becomes a lahiq, determine whether his prayer length changes upon intending residence.

Source Text
