ثُمَّ الْآدَاء الْمَحْضُ مَا يُؤَدِيْهِ الْإِنْسَانُ بِوَصْفِهِ عَلَى مَاشُرِعَ مِثْلُ أَدَاءِ الصَّلُوةِ بِجَمَاعَةٍ وأَمَّا فِعْلُ الْفَرْدِ فَادَاءً فِيْهِ قُصُورٌ أَلَا تَرى أَنَّ الْجَهْرَ سَاقِطْ عَنِ الْمُنْفَرِدِ وَفِعْلُ اللَّاحِقِ بَعْدَ فَرَاغِ الْإِمَامِ اَدَاءً يَشْبَهُ الْقَضَاءَ بِاعْتَبَارِ أَنَّهُ الْتَزَمَ الْأَدَاءَ مَعَ الْأَمَامِ حِيْنَ تَحَرَّمَ مَعَهُ وَقَدْ فَاتَهُ ذَلِكَ حَقِيقَةً وَلِهَذَا لَا يَتَغَيَّرُ فَرْضُهُ بِنِيَّةِ الْآقَامَةِ فِى هَذهِ الْحَالَةِ كَمَا لَوْصَارَ قَضَاءً مَحْضًا بِالْفَوَاتِ ثُمَّ وَجِدَ الْمُغَيْرُ بِخِلَافِ الْمَسْبُوْقِ لِأَنَّهُ مُؤَدٍ فِي إِثْمَامِ صَلُوتِهِ
Then, pure performance (ada mahd) is that which a person performs with its description upon which it was prescribed, like performing prayer in congregation. As for the act of an individual, it is a performance in which there is deficiency. Do you not see that raising the voice (jahr) is dropped from the one praying alone? And the act of the lahiq (one who misses part of prayer) after the imam finishes is a performance resembling qada, considering that he committed to performance with the imam when he began with him, but that commitment was actually lost. For this reason, his obligatory duty does not change with the intention of residence (niyyat al-iqama) in this state, just as if it had become pure qada due to being missed, then the changer (mujayyir) were found [later], contrary to the masbuq (latecomer who catches part of prayer), because he is performing (muaddin) in completing his prayer.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is an usul definition and classification of types of ada (performance) in prayer. The author first defines ada mahd (pure/perfect performance) as performing an act in the exact manner it was prescribed, with congregation being the ideal for prayer. He then identifies two other types: (1) the performance of a lone worshipper (fi‘l al-fard) is deficient (qasir) because elements like jahr (loud recitation) are waived for him—this shows a lack of perfection, hence requiring sajdat al-sahw. (2) The action of a lahiq (one who missed part of prayer due to a minor disruption, like breaking wudu) after the imam finishes is called 'ada shabih bi'l-qada' (performance resembling qada). Resemblance to ada: it is performed within the prayer time; resemblance to qada: his commitment to pray entirely with the imam was not fulfilled. This classification has a legal effect: if a traveling lahiq intends residence while completing his prayer, his intention does not change the number of rak'at (i.e., he still prays two rak'at if he was traveling), because the changer (niyyat al-iqama) is attached to a period resembling qada, not to the original ada. This is unlike a masbuq (latecomer), who is still in the state of ada and thus his intention would affect the prayer.

Key Terms
اداء محض (ada mahd): Pure performance: performing an act exactly as prescribed in the Sharia, e.g., prayer in congregation.
اداء قاصر (ada qasir): Deficient performance: an act performed without its ideal attributes, e.g., prayer alone where jahr is dropped.
لاحق (lahiq): One who started prayer with the imam but had a minor disruption (like breaking wudu) and rejoins after the imam finishes.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the congregation after the imam has started, completing what he missed after the imam finishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the intention of residence (niyyat al-iqama) not change the prayer length for a lahiq (one who missed part of prayer due to minor disruption)?
A) Because the lahiq's prayer is considered pure ada and thus unaffected by external factors.
B) Because the lahiq's remaining prayer resembles qada, and the changer (niyyat al-iqama) is attached to qada, not ada.
C) Because the lahiq is not considered a musafir in this context.
D) Because the lahiq's prayer was completed in the original congregation.

Key Takeaway
The classification of ada into mahd, qasir, and shabih bil qada determines how external factors like intention affect prayer obligations, especially for the lahiq.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Types of Ada: Complete and Deficient Performance
Defining complete and deficient ada with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir) ada, and derive the ruling that praying alone is deficient based on the dropping of jahr.

Core Idea
Ada qasir omits an attribute of perfection; jahr dropping from munfarid proves deficiency.

In Hanafi usul, the performance of a ruling is classified into two types: complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). This classification affects reward and the need for compensation. In this lesson, we examine the definitions and the proof that individual prayer is deficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ada
The author divides ada into complete and deficient. Complete ada entails performing the act exactly as legislated with all its attributes, while deficient ada lacks some perfection attribute.
Example: prayer with congregation is complete; without is deficient.
2
Analyse the definition of ada kamil
Ada kamil is performing the ruling as it was legislated. For prayer, congregation is a legislated attribute, as Jibril led the Prophet in congregation. Thus, praying with jama'ah is complete ada.
3
Examine the proof for deficiency of munfarid
The text argues that jahr (loud recitation) is an attribute of perfection in jahri prayers. The munfarid omits jahr, which necessitates sujud al-sahw. Therefore, his ada is deficient.
The omission of a perfection attribute indicates deficiency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس سے حقیقتہ فوت ہو گیا، اور اسی وجہ سے اس کا فرض اقامت کی نیت سے متغیر نہیں ہوگا اس حالت میں ، جیسا کہ فرض قضاء محض ہو جائے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر مخیر پایا جائے برخلاف مسبوق کے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنی نماز کو پورا کرنے تک ادا کرنے والا ہے۔ تشریح : ۔ مصنف عالی ادا کی قسمیں بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ ادا کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) ادائے کامل (۲) ادائے قاصر ، اداء محض سے مراد اداء کامل ہے ، اداء کامل یہ ہے حکم جس طرح مشروع ہوا ہے اس کو اسی صفت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا جیسے نماز کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا، کیونکہ نماز جماعت کے ساتھ مشروع ہوئی ہے اسی لئے جب نماز مشروع ہوئی تو حضرت جبرئیل علیہ السلام نے شروع کے دو دن میں حضور [سنی اسلام؟] کو جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھائی ، بہر حال نماز کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا اداء کامل ہے، اور بغیر جماعت کے تنہا پڑھنا اداء قاصر ہے، اور اس کے اداء قاصر ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منفرد سے جہر ساقط ہو جاتا ہے حالانکہ جہری نماز میں جہر کرنا صفت کمال ہے، اس لئے اس کے چھوٹنے سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے ، پس صفت کمال یعنی جہر کا ساقط ہونا دلیل ہے اس کی کہ منفرد کی ادا اداء قاصر ہے۔ وفعل اللاحق - مصنف نے ادا کی تیسری قسم بیان کر رہے ہیں جس کو اداء شبیہ بالقضا کہتے ہیں ، جیسے فعل اللاحق کا فعل یعنی جس نے نماز امام کے ساتھ شروع کی، پھر درمیان میں حدث لاحق ہو گیا ، وہ وضو کر نے چلا گیا اور باقی نماز امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد پوری کر رہا ہے، تو لاحق کی یہ باقی نماز اداء مشابہ بالقضاء ہے ، چونکہ وہ وقت میں پڑھ رہا ہے، نماز کا وقت ابھی باقی ہے ، اس لئے یہ ادا کے مشابہ ہے، اور جس طرح اس نے التزام کیا تھا اس طرح وہ پوری نہ کر سکا، کیونکہ نماز شروع کرتے وقت اس نے اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تھا کہ پوری نماز امام کے ساتھ پڑھے گا اور یہ التزام اس سے حقیقۃ فوت ہو گیا، اس لئے یہ قضا کے مشابہ ہے۔ ولهذا لا يتغير : - لاحق کی نماز مشابہ بالقضا ہے، اس کا ثمرہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ یہ لاحق مسافر ہے اور اس نے مسافر امام کی اقتدا میں ظہر کی نماز شروع کی ، پھر اس کو حدث لاحق ہو گیا، اور وضو کر نے چلا گیا پھر باقی ماندہ نماز کو امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ادا کر رہا ہے، تو یہ لاحق کا فعل مشابہ بالقضاء ہے، لہذا اس وقت اگر وہ اقامت کی نیت کرتا ہے تو نیت اقامت سے اس کا فرض بدلے گا نہیں، کیونکہ مغیر (نیت اقامت ) ادا سے متصل نہیں ہے، بلکہ قضا سے متصل ہے، کیونکہ لاحق کی یہ نماز مشابہ بالقضا ہے، جیسے کسی کی نماز خالص قضا ہو جیسے مسافر نے ظہر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی اور عصر کے وقت میں وہ مقیم ہو جائے ، اقامت کی نیت کر کے، تو ظہر کی نماز وہ قصر ہی پڑھے گا کیونکہ اقامت کی نیت وقت کے بعد ہوئی ہے یعنی مغیر قضا سے متصل ہے ادا سے متصل نہیں ہے ، پس خالص قضا کی صورت میں موثر نہیں ہے، اسی طرح مشابہ بالقضاء میں بھی نیت موثر نہ ہوگی۔ البتہ اگر مسبوق جس کو کچھ نماز امام کے ساتھ ملی پھر باقی نماز وہ امام کے فراغت کے بعد ادا کر رہا ہے تو اگر مسافر ہے اور مسافر امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی اور بعد میں چھوٹی ہوئی نماز پوری کر رہا ہے ، اس وقت اگر اس نے اقامت کی نیت کر لی تو اس کا فرض بدل جائے گا اب یہ چار رکعت پوری کرے گا کیونکہ مسبوق کا فعل خالص ادا ہے اس لیے کہ وقت بھی باقی ہے اور مسبوق نے اس چھوٹی ہوئی نماز کو امام کے ساتھ پڑھنے کا التزام بھی نہیں کیا تھا کہ یہ قضا کے مشابہ ہو جائے ، پس مسبوق کی نماز ادا ہے اور مغیر (نیت اقامت ) ادا سے متصل ہوا، لہذا وہ فرض کو بدل دے گا۔
From this, in reality, it was missed, and for this reason his obligatory prayer will not change by the intention of residency in this situation, just as an obligatory prayer becomes pure qada due to missing it, then he is found to have a choice, contrary to the masbuq, because he is performing his prayer until completing it. Explanation: The author, may Allah elevate him, is explaining the types of ada: ada has two types: (1) complete ada, (2) deficient ada. By 'pure ada' he means complete ada. Complete ada is to perform a ruling as it was legislated, with its attributes, like praying prayer with congregation, because prayer was legislated with congregation. For this reason, when prayer was legislated, Jibril, peace be upon him, led the Prophet [؟] in prayer with congregation for the first two days. In any case, performing prayer with congregation is complete ada, and performing it alone without congregation is deficient ada. The proof for its being deficient ada is that from the one praying alone, the jahr (audible recitation) drops, even though in a prayer recited aloud, jahr is a attribute of perfection; thus, its omission necessitates the prostration of forgetfulness. So the dropping of the attribute of perfection, i.e., jahr, is proof that the ada of the one praying alone is deficient ada. As for the act of the lahiq: The author is mentioning a third type of ada called ada resembling qada, like the act of the lahiq—the one who started prayer with the imam, then had an hadath (impurity) in the middle, went to perform wudu, and completes the remainder of the prayer after the imam has finished. So this remaining prayer of the lahiq is ada resembling qada. Since he is praying within the time, the time of prayer is still remaining, so it resembles ada; and he could not complete it as he had committed, because at the start of prayer he had obligated upon himself to pray the entire prayer with the imam, and that commitment was effectively missed from him, so it resembles qada. And for this reason it does not change: The prayer of the lahiq resembles qada. He is explaining its consequence: That this lahiq is a traveler and started Dhuhr prayer in the congregation of a traveler imam, then had an hadath, went to perform wudu, then prays the remaining part after the imam finishes. So this act of the lahiq resembles qada. Therefore, if he intends residency at that time, the intention of residency will not change his obligatory prayer, because the modifier (intention of residency) is not connected to ada, but to qada, because this prayer of the lahiq resembles qada. Just as if someone's prayer is pure qada, like a traveler who did not pray Dhuhr and becomes a resident at the time of Asr, intending residency, he will pray Dhuhr shortened, because the intention of residency came after the time; i.e., the modifier is connected to qada, not to ada. So in the case of pure qada, it is ineffective, and similarly in the case of that which resembles qada, the intention will not be effective. However, if the masbuq—who caught some of the prayer with the imam then completes the rest after the imam finishes—if he is a traveler and prayed with a traveler imam and later completes the missed part, if he then intends residency, his obligatory prayer will change; now he will complete four rak'ahs. Because the act of the masbuq is pure ada, since the time is still remaining and the masbuq did not commit to pray the missed part with the imam such that it would resemble qada. So the prayer of the masbuq is ada, and the modifier (intention of residency) is connected to ada, hence it will change the obligatory prayer.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage from Al-Faiz-ul-Hijaz is a commentary on Al-Husami that defines the types of ada (performance). It begins by stating that ada has two types: complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). Complete ada is performing an act exactly as legislated with all its attributes, exemplified by praying with congregation (jama'ah) because prayer was originally legislated with congregation. The commentary notes that Jibril led the Prophet in congregation during the first two days of prayer obligation, establishing jama'ah as the sunnah. Deficient ada is performing the act without full attributes, such as praying alone without congregation. The proof given is that the attribute of jahr (loud recitation) drops from the munfarid (one praying alone), and its omission requires sujud al-sahw, indicating deficiency. Then the commentary introduces a third type: ada shabih bil-qada (ada resembling qada), which applies to the lahiq—one who began prayer with the imam, left due to hadath (impurity), performed wudu, and completes the remaining prayer after the imam finishes. This remaining prayer is considered ada because it is still within the time, but it resembles qada because his commitment to pray the entire prayer with the imam was missed. The passage then explains the practical ruling: if the lahiq is a traveler and intends residency during his remaining prayer, the intention does not change his obligation to pray shortened, because the intention of residency is connected to the qada-like part, not to the ada. This is contrasted with the masbuq (one who joined late but did not commit to stay with the imam throughout), whose remaining prayer is pure ada, so if he intends residency, his obligation changes and he prays four rak'ahs.

Key Terms
اداء کامل (ada kamil): Performing a ruling exactly as legislated with all its attributes, e.g., prayer with congregation.
اداء قاصر (ada qasir): Performing a ruling missing some attribute of perfection, e.g., prayer alone without congregation.
جہر (jahr): Audible recitation in prayer; considered an attribute of perfection for jahri prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what proves that individual prayer is deficient (ada qasir)?
A) The prayer becomes invalid without congregation.
B) The attribute of jahr drops from the munfarid, and its omission necessitates sujud al-sahw.
C) The Prophet always prayed with congregation.
D) The time for prayer is reduced.

Key Takeaway
Ada is classified into kamil (complete) and qasir (deficient); omission of a perfection attribute like jahr proves deficiency, not invalidity.

The Ruling of the Lahiq: Ada Shabih bil-Qada
Defining the lahiq's act as ada shabih bil-qada and its ruling compared to masbuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the lahiq and masbuq in terms of whether their remaining prayer is ada or shabih bil-qada, and apply the consequence for intention of residency.

Core Idea
The lahiq's prayer is ada shabih bil-qada, so intention of residency after leaving does not change his shortening; the masbuq's is pure ada, so it does change.

In Hanafi fiqh, a lahiq is one who starts prayer with the imam, leaves due to hadath, and completes after the imam. His remaining prayer is a hybrid: performed in time (ada) but with a broken commitment (qada). This unique classification has practical implications, especially regarding the effect of intending residency.

Guided Path
1
Define the lahiq and his scenario
The lahiq is a person who begins prayer with the imam, then becomes impure (hadath), performs wudu, and completes the rest after the imam finishes. His remaining prayer is called 'ada shabih bil-qada'.
Contrast with masbuq who joins late but does not break his prayer.
2
Classify the lahiq's remaining prayer
It is ada because it is performed within the time; it resembles qada because his commitment to pray the whole with the imam was missed. This duplicity makes it 'shabih bil-qada'.
3
Analyse the consequence for intention of residency
If a traveler lahiq intends residency while completing his remaining prayer, his obligation does not change to four rak'ahs because the intention of residency attaches to the qada-like part, not the ada. In contrast, a masbuq's missed part is pure ada, so intending residency changes his obligation.
The text compares it to pure qada: if a traveler misses Dhuhr and later intends residency, he still prays Dhuhr shortened.

Source Text

اس سے حقیقتہ فوت ہو گیا، اور اسی وجہ سے اس کا فرض اقامت کی نیت سے متغیر نہیں ہوگا اس حالت میں ، جیسا کہ فرض قضاء محض ہو جائے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر مخیر پایا جائے برخلاف مسبوق کے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنی نماز کو پورا کرنے تک ادا کرنے والا ہے۔ تشریح : ۔ مصنف عالی ادا کی قسمیں بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ ادا کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) ادائے کامل (۲) ادائے قاصر ، اداء محض سے مراد اداء کامل ہے ، اداء کامل یہ ہے حکم جس طرح مشروع ہوا ہے اس کو اسی صفت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا جیسے نماز کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا، کیونکہ نماز جماعت کے ساتھ مشروع ہوئی ہے اسی لئے جب نماز مشروع ہوئی تو حضرت جبرئیل علیہ السلام نے شروع کے دو دن میں حضور [سنی اسلام؟] کو جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھائی ، بہر حال نماز کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا اداء کامل ہے، اور بغیر جماعت کے تنہا پڑھنا اداء قاصر ہے، اور اس کے اداء قاصر ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منفرد سے جہر ساقط ہو جاتا ہے حالانکہ جہری نماز میں جہر کرنا صفت کمال ہے، اس لئے اس کے چھوٹنے سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے ، پس صفت کمال یعنی جہر کا ساقط ہونا دلیل ہے اس کی کہ منفرد کی ادا اداء قاصر ہے۔ وفعل اللاحق - مصنف نے ادا کی تیسری قسم بیان کر رہے ہیں جس کو اداء شبیہ بالقضا کہتے ہیں ، جیسے فعل اللاحق کا فعل یعنی جس نے نماز امام کے ساتھ شروع کی، پھر درمیان میں حدث لاحق ہو گیا ، وہ وضو کر نے چلا گیا اور باقی نماز امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد پوری کر رہا ہے، تو لاحق کی یہ باقی نماز اداء مشابہ بالقضاء ہے ، چونکہ وہ وقت میں پڑھ رہا ہے، نماز کا وقت ابھی باقی ہے ، اس لئے یہ ادا کے مشابہ ہے، اور جس طرح اس نے التزام کیا تھا اس طرح وہ پوری نہ کر سکا، کیونکہ نماز شروع کرتے وقت اس نے اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تھا کہ پوری نماز امام کے ساتھ پڑھے گا اور یہ التزام اس سے حقیقۃ فوت ہو گیا، اس لئے یہ قضا کے مشابہ ہے۔ ولهذا لا يتغير : - لاحق کی نماز مشابہ بالقضا ہے، اس کا ثمرہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ یہ لاحق مسافر ہے اور اس نے مسافر امام کی اقتدا میں ظہر کی نماز شروع کی ، پھر اس کو حدث لاحق ہو گیا، اور وضو کر نے چلا گیا پھر باقی ماندہ نماز کو امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ادا کر رہا ہے، تو یہ لاحق کا فعل مشابہ بالقضاء ہے، لہذا اس وقت اگر وہ اقامت کی نیت کرتا ہے تو نیت اقامت سے اس کا فرض بدلے گا نہیں، کیونکہ مغیر (نیت اقامت ) ادا سے متصل نہیں ہے، بلکہ قضا سے متصل ہے، کیونکہ لاحق کی یہ نماز مشابہ بالقضا ہے، جیسے کسی کی نماز خالص قضا ہو جیسے مسافر نے ظہر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی اور عصر کے وقت میں وہ مقیم ہو جائے ، اقامت کی نیت کر کے، تو ظہر کی نماز وہ قصر ہی پڑھے گا کیونکہ اقامت کی نیت وقت کے بعد ہوئی ہے یعنی مغیر قضا سے متصل ہے ادا سے متصل نہیں ہے ، پس خالص قضا کی صورت میں موثر نہیں ہے، اسی طرح مشابہ بالقضاء میں بھی نیت موثر نہ ہوگی۔ البتہ اگر مسبوق جس کو کچھ نماز امام کے ساتھ ملی پھر باقی نماز وہ امام کے فراغت کے بعد ادا کر رہا ہے تو اگر مسافر ہے اور مسافر امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی اور بعد میں چھوٹی ہوئی نماز پوری کر رہا ہے ، اس وقت اگر اس نے اقامت کی نیت کر لی تو اس کا فرض بدل جائے گا اب یہ چار رکعت پوری کرے گا کیونکہ مسبوق کا فعل خالص ادا ہے اس لیے کہ وقت بھی باقی ہے اور مسبوق نے اس چھوٹی ہوئی نماز کو امام کے ساتھ پڑھنے کا التزام بھی نہیں کیا تھا کہ یہ قضا کے مشابہ ہو جائے ، پس مسبوق کی نماز ادا ہے اور مغیر (نیت اقامت ) ادا سے متصل ہوا، لہذا وہ فرض کو بدل دے گا۔
From this, in reality, it was missed, and for this reason his obligatory prayer will not change by the intention of residency in this situation, just as an obligatory prayer becomes pure qada due to missing it, then he is found to have a choice, contrary to the masbuq, because he is performing his prayer until completing it. Explanation: The author, may Allah elevate him, is explaining the types of ada: ada has two types: (1) complete ada, (2) deficient ada. By 'pure ada' he means complete ada. Complete ada is to perform a ruling as it was legislated, with its attributes, like praying prayer with congregation, because prayer was legislated with congregation. For this reason, when prayer was legislated, Jibril, peace be upon him, led the Prophet [؟] in prayer with congregation for the first two days. In any case, performing prayer with congregation is complete ada, and performing it alone without congregation is deficient ada. The proof for its being deficient ada is that from the one praying alone, the jahr (audible recitation) drops, even though in a prayer recited aloud, jahr is a attribute of perfection; thus, its omission necessitates the prostration of forgetfulness. So the dropping of the attribute of perfection, i.e., jahr, is proof that the ada of the one praying alone is deficient ada. As for the act of the lahiq: The author is mentioning a third type of ada called ada resembling qada, like the act of the lahiq—the one who started prayer with the imam, then had an hadath (impurity) in the middle, went to perform wudu, and completes the remainder of the prayer after the imam has finished. So this remaining prayer of the lahiq is ada resembling qada. Since he is praying within the time, the time of prayer is still remaining, so it resembles ada; and he could not complete it as he had committed, because at the start of prayer he had obligated upon himself to pray the entire prayer with the imam, and that commitment was effectively missed from him, so it resembles qada. And for this reason it does not change: The prayer of the lahiq resembles qada. He is explaining its consequence: That this lahiq is a traveler and started Dhuhr prayer in the congregation of a traveler imam, then had an hadath, went to perform wudu, then prays the remaining part after the imam finishes. So this act of the lahiq resembles qada. Therefore, if he intends residency at that time, the intention of residency will not change his obligatory prayer, because the modifier (intention of residency) is not connected to ada, but to qada, because this prayer of the lahiq resembles qada. Just as if someone's prayer is pure qada, like a traveler who did not pray Dhuhr and becomes a resident at the time of Asr, intending residency, he will pray Dhuhr shortened, because the intention of residency came after the time; i.e., the modifier is connected to qada, not to ada. So in the case of pure qada, it is ineffective, and similarly in the case of that which resembles qada, the intention will not be effective. However, if the masbuq—who caught some of the prayer with the imam then completes the rest after the imam finishes—if he is a traveler and prayed with a traveler imam and later completes the missed part, if he then intends residency, his obligatory prayer will change; now he will complete four rak'ahs. Because the act of the masbuq is pure ada, since the time is still remaining and the masbuq did not commit to pray the missed part with the imam such that it would resemble qada. So the prayer of the masbuq is ada, and the modifier (intention of residency) is connected to ada, hence it will change the obligatory prayer.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage from Al-Faiz-ul-Hijaz is a commentary on Al-Husami that defines the types of ada (performance). It begins by stating that ada has two types: complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). Complete ada is performing an act exactly as legislated with all its attributes, exemplified by praying with congregation (jama'ah) because prayer was originally legislated with congregation. The commentary notes that Jibril led the Prophet in congregation during the first two days of prayer obligation, establishing jama'ah as the sunnah. Deficient ada is performing the act without full attributes, such as praying alone without congregation. The proof given is that the attribute of jahr (loud recitation) drops from the munfarid (one praying alone), and its omission requires sujud al-sahw, indicating deficiency. Then the commentary introduces a third type: ada shabih bil-qada (ada resembling qada), which applies to the lahiq—one who began prayer with the imam, left due to hadath (impurity), performed wudu, and completes the remaining prayer after the imam finishes. This remaining prayer is considered ada because it is still within the time, but it resembles qada because his commitment to pray the entire prayer with the imam was missed. The passage then explains the practical ruling: if the lahiq is a traveler and intends residency during his remaining prayer, the intention does not change his obligation to pray shortened, because the intention of residency is connected to the qada-like part, not to the ada. This is contrasted with the masbuq (one who joined late but did not commit to stay with the imam throughout), whose remaining prayer is pure ada, so if he intends residency, his obligation changes and he prays four rak'ahs.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): One who begins salah with the imam, then leaves due to hadath and completes after the imam finishes.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the congregation late and misses some rak'ahs with the imam, then completes them after the imam's salam.
اداء شبیہ بالقضاء (ada shabih bil-qada): Performance that is like qada: performed within the time but with a missed commitment, e.g., the lahiq's remaining prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler lahiq intends residency while completing his prayer after the imam finishes, why does his obligation remain shortened?
A) Because the intention of residency only affects future prayers.
B) Because his remaining prayer is ada shabih bil-qada, and the modifier connects to the qada part.
C) Because he is still traveling until he completes the prayer.
D) Because the imam's intention also matters.

Key Takeaway
The lahiq's remaining prayer is a unique hybrid (ada shabih bil-qada), which prevents the intention of residency from altering his shortening, unlike the masbuq whose missed part is pure ada.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Two Types of Qada: Rational and Non-Rational Compensation
Defining two categories of qada with examples and textual basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qada bi-mithl ma'qul and qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul, and apply the Hanafi principle that non-rational compensation is valid only when established by nass.

Core Idea
Qada can be by rational equivalent (like for like) or by non-rational equivalent, but the latter requires explicit textual proof.

After understanding the general concept of qada (making up missed obligations), we now dive into a critical distinction: some missed acts can be compensated by an act that is rationally similar, while others are compensated by an act that is not similar but is permitted by divine text. This lesson dissects both types and the evidentiary basis for accepting non-rational equivalents, such as fidya for fasting and hajj badal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qada
From the passage, extract the two categories: qada bi-mithl ma'qul (rational equivalence) and qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul (non-rational equivalence). Note that the first is based on rational similarity, while the second is based on textual command.
The passage explicitly states 'qada is of two types' and gives examples.
2
Recognize examples of rational qada
The passage mentions 'as we mentioned' referring to earlier examples like making up a fast with another fast or a prayer with the same prayer. Understand that in these cases, the substitute is rationally identical to the original.
3
Analyze non-rational qada and its proof
Focus on the examples of fidya for a decrepit old person (shaykh fani) and hajj badal. The passage states these are 'established by nass (text)'. Observe that the similarity between fasting and giving money, or between performing hajj and paying for someone else, is not rational, yet the shari'ah validates them.
The text (nass) overrides rational analogy (qiyas) in these cases.
4
Extend the principle to prayer
The author extends the ruling to prayer, arguing that since prayer is more important than fasting, fidya can be given for missed prayers as a precaution (ihtiyatan). Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Ziyadat confirms its validity with hope of acceptance.
This shows that the principle of non-rational compensation can be extended by analogy to other acts, but only when supported by the same rationale ('illa) of inability.

And qada is of two types: qada with a rational equivalent, as we mentioned, and qada with a non-rational equivalent, like the ransom (fidya) in the chapter of fasting for the decrepit old person, and having someone else perform Hajj with his wealth. Both are established by the text (nass). We do not understand rationally the similarity between fasting and ransom, nor between Hajj and expenditure. However, it is possible that it is caused by the cause of inability. And prayer is analogous to fasting, indeed it is more important than it, so we command him to give ransom for prayer as a precaution, and we hope for acceptance from Allah as a favor. And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said in al-Ziyadat: 'It suffices him, if Allah wills, just as when the heir gives it voluntarily for fasting.' Translation: qada is of two types: qada with rational equivalent, as we mentioned, and qada with non-rational equivalent, like the ransom in the chapter of fasting for the decrepit old person, and having someone else perform Hajj with his wealth. Both are established by the text, and the similarity between fasting and ransom is not rationally understood, nor between Hajj and expenditure. But the ruling of ransom carries the possibility that it may be caused by the cause of inability. Prayer is analogous to fasting, indeed it is more important, so we command him to give ransom for prayer as a precaution, and we hope for acceptance from Allah out of favor. Then Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said in al-Ziyadat: 'It will suffice him, if Allah wills, just as when the heir gives it voluntarily for fasting.' Explanation: The author, may Allah elevate him, after ada, now explains the division of qada. He says: qada is of two types: (1) pure qada, (2) qada resembling ada. Then pure qada has two types: (1) qada with rational equivalent, (2) qada with non-rational equivalent. The definition of qada with rational equivalent is that the similarity between the original ruling and the qada is rationally understood, e.g., making up a fast from Ramadan and making up a prayer as a performance prayer; between these the similarity is obvious. And qada with non-rational equivalent is that the similarity between the original ruling and the qada is not rationally understood, but the shari'ah has considered it equivalent, e.g., the ruling of ransom for fasting for the decrepit old person, and having Hajj performed on behalf of an incapacitated person with his wealth.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Husami discusses the division of qada (making up). It begins by stating that qada is of two types: qada with a rational equivalent (qada bi-mithl ma'qul) and qada with a non-rational equivalent (qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul). The first type is when the act of qada is exactly like the original act, e.g., making up a missed fast by fasting a similar day, or making up a missed prayer by praying the same prayer. This similarity is rationally understood. The second type is when the compensatory act is not similar in form but is established by a textual proof (nass), e.g., giving fidya (ransom) for fasting when one is a decrepit old person (shaykh fani) unable to fast, or having someone else perform Hajj with one's wealth when one is physically unable. The similarity between fasting and fidya is not rational, but the shari'ah considers it a valid compensation. The text then extends this to prayer: since prayer is more important than fasting, one may give fidya for missed prayers as a precaution, hoping for Allah's acceptance. It quotes Imam Muhammad from al-Ziyadat that this suffices, insha'Allah, just as when an heir voluntarily pays fidya for missed fasts of the deceased. The commentary further clarifies that qada itself can be pure (qada mahd) or resembling ada (qada shabih bil-ada), and pure qada is sub-divided into the two rational and non-rational types. The key principle is that the basis of qada is rational similarity, but in some cases the shari'ah establishes compensation without rational similarity due to textual evidence.

Key Terms
قضاء بمثل معقول (qada bi-mithl ma'qul): Making up an act with a rationally similar substitute, e.g., fasting for fasting.
قضاء بمثل غیر معقول (qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul): Compensation that is not rationally similar but established by nass, e.g., fidya for fasting.
فدیہ (fidya): Monetary ransom given in place of fasting or prayer for those permanently unable.
شیخ فانی (shaykh fani): A decrepit old person who cannot fast due to extreme age.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for accepting qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul, such as fidya for fasting?
A) Rational analogy (qiyas) between the original and the substitute.
B) Consensus of the companions (ijma').
C) Explicit textual proof (nass) from the Quran or Sunnah.
D) General necessity (darura) without specific text.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qada is not limited to rational equivalents; non-rational compensation is valid when explicitly supported by a clear text (nass).

Taklif Ma La Yutaq and Types of Power in Usul al-Fiqh
Usul definition of taklif ma la yutaq and types of power

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the three types of taklif ma la yutaq and distinguish between real power (qudra haqiqiyya) and conventional power (qudra muta'arifa) as the basis for obligation.

Core Idea
Not every impossible act is a burden; some impossibilities are validly obligated, and conventional power precedes the act.

This passage defines a core usul concept: whether Allah can obligate a person with something beyond their capacity (taklif ma la yutaq). The author categorizes three different types of 'impossible' acts and explains which can be obligated. He then introduces the crucial distinction between two kinds of power—real power (qudra haqiqiyya) and conventional power (qudra muta'arifa)—and argues that only conventional power serves as the basis for legal obligation. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly deriving rulings in situations where a person's ability is limited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of taklif ma la yutaq
First, extract the three categories of impossible acts: (1) intrinsically impossible (mumtani' li-dhatihi), (2) conventionally impossible (mumtani' li-ghayri), and (3) possible in essence but impossible due to divine knowledge/will (mumtani' bi'l-ghayr). Note the example given for each.
The third type is the most nuanced; it involves acts that are within human capacity but Allah knows they will not occur.
2
Determine permissibility and occurrence for each type
For each type, note the Hanafi position on whether obligating it is permissible (ja'iz) and whether it actually occurs (waqi'). For type 1: neither. For type 2: non-occurrence agreed, permissibility disputed. For type 3: both permissible and occurring (e.g., Abu Jahl's obligation to believe).
The Ash'ari view allows obligating types 1 and 2 rationally, but only type 2 is agreed not to occur.
3
Define the two types of power
Recognize that real power (qudra haqiqiyya) is Allah's tawfiq which accompanies the act, while conventional power (qudra muta'arifa) is the soundness of means and instruments and precedes the act. The key difference is timing relative to the act.
Conventional power is further divided into possible power (qudra mumakkana) and available power (qudra mayassara), though the passage cuts off here.
4
Justify why conventional power is the basis of obligation
The author gives two reasons: (a) if real power were the basis, disbelievers would not be obligated (since they lack tawfiq), but they are; (b) the power that is a condition must precede the act, but real power occurs simultaneously, while conventional power precedes.
This is a classic Hanafi argument distinguishing between the cause of the act (tawfiq) and the condition for obligation (means).

Source Text

تکلیف ہے اس کا فعل پر مقدم ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ یہ قدرت فعل کے لئے شرط ہوتی ہے اور شرط شئی شئی سے پہلے ہوتی ہے، اور قدرت حقیقیہ فعل پر مقدم نہیں ہوتی بلکہ فعل کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، البتہ قدرت متعارفہ فعل سے پہلے ہوتی ہے، لہذا یہی قدرت مدار تکلیف ہے۔ پھر قدرت متعارفہ بمعنی سلامتی اسباب و آلات کی دو قسمیں ہیں، (۱) قدرت ممکنہ (۲) قدرت میسرہ۔ قدرت ممکنہ وہ ادنی مقدار قدرت ہے جس سے بندہ فعل کو ادا کرنے پر قادر ہو جاتا ہے، جیسے مال زکوۃ کے لئے، اسی کا دوسرا نام مطلقہ اور قاصرہ بھی ہے، اور قدرت میسرہ وہ قدرت ہے جس سے فعل پر بندہ قادر بھی ہو جاتا ہے اور فعل
Explanation: Understand some things as an introduction: (1) Taklif ma la yutaq - i.e., making a slave obligated with something beyond his capacity - is it permissible or not? Then does it occur or not? There is some detail. Taklif ma la yutaq has three types: (1) Mumtani' li-dhatihi - intrinsically impossible, like the conjunction of opposites. (2) Mumtani' li-ghayrihi - an act intrinsically possible but its occurrence is usually impossible, like flying in the air or creating a body. (3) Third: an act which in itself is possible for the slave, but in Allah's knowledge that act will not occur from the slave, or Allah's will is that the act does not issue from the slave. If the slave does issue the act, then it would necessitate Allah's knowledge being wrong and His will being frustrated, which is impossible. And what is possible but necessitates an impossibility is called mumtani' bi'l-ghayr. So this act is possible in essence but impossible by virtue of something else. For the first type, the majority hold that obligating it is neither permissible nor does it occur; however, a group of Ash'aris hold that rationally obligating it is permissible but it does not occur. For the second type, non-occurrence is agreed upon, but there is dispute about permissibility: the Ash'aris say obligating it is permissible, because Allah is the true owner of servants and has all authority; there is no restriction on His disposal. The third type, which is possible in essence and impossible by virtue of something else, its obligating is permissible and it does occur, like the faith of Abu Jahl and Abu Lahab. In Allah's eternal knowledge it was determined that they would not believe, yet they are obligated with faith, because intrinsically believing was within their power, and obligation depends on the maintenance of power and free will; their free will is not nullified by Allah's eternal knowledge. (2) Then the power by which a slave is obligated is of two types: (1) Real power (qudra haqiqiyya) meaning Allah's tawfiq (divine facilitation). (2) Conventional power (qudra muta'arifa) meaning safety of means and instruments. Real power occurs with the act and is the cause of it; conventional power precedes the act. The basis of obligation is conventional power, not real power, because if real power were the basis, then a disbeliever would not be obligated, since he does not have tawfiq. Second reason: the power that is the basis of obligation must precede the act, because it is a condition, and a condition precedes the conditioned. Real power does not precede the act but occurs with it; conventional power precedes. So this is the basis. Then conventional power, meaning safety of means and instruments, is of two types: (1) Possible power (qudra mumakkana) and (2) Available power (qudura mayassara). Possible power is the minimum amount of power that enables the slave to perform the act, like wealth for zakat. Its other names are mutlaqa and qasira. Available power is that power by which the slave is able to perform the act and... (cut off).
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an introductory explanation (tashrih) on the topic of taklif ma la yutaq and the types of power in usul al-fiqh. The author first categorizes the obligation of the impossible into three types: intrinsically impossible (like contradictions), conventionally impossible (like flying), and that which is possible in essence but impossible due to divine knowledge/will (like the faith of Abu Jahl). He then discusses the permissibility and occurrence of each type, noting the Ash'ari view. Next, he distinguishes between real power (qudra haqiqiyya), which is Allah's facilitation and occurs with the act, and conventional power (qudra muta'arifa), which is the soundness of means and precedes the act. The basis of obligation is conventional power, not real power, because otherwise unbelievers would not be obligated. Conventional power is further divided into possible power (qudra mumakkana) and available power (qudura mayassara). The explanation uses Hanafi theological positions.

Key Terms
تکلیف مالا يطاق (taklif ma la yutaq): Obligating a person with something beyond his capacity.
ممتنع لذاتہ (mumtani' li-dhatihi): Intrinsically impossible, like the conjunction of opposites.
ممتنع لغیرہ (mumtani' li-ghayrihi): An act possible in essence but impossible due to external factors, like flying.
قدرت حقیقیہ (qudra haqiqiyya): Real power: Allah's tawfiq, which occurs with the act.
قدرت متعارفہ (qudra muta'arifa): Conventional power: safety of means and instruments, preceding the act.

A) Because real power is impossible to achieve
B) Because conventional power precedes the act, while real power occurs with it
C) Because conventional power is from Allah

Key Takeaway
Conventional power (safety of means and instruments) is the basis for obligation, not real power (divine facilitation), and this distinction allows obligation even when Allah knows the act will not occur.

Types of Taklif Ma La Yutaq and Their Rulings
Defining and categorizing the obligation of the impossible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of taklif ma la yutaq, state the Hanafi position on each, and explain why the third type is valid.

Core Idea
Obligation of the impossible is valid only when the act is intrinsically possible, even if divine knowledge precludes its occurrence.

The concept of taklif ma la yutaq (obligation of the impossible) raises fundamental questions about divine justice and human responsibility. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi classification of impossibility into three categories, distinguishing between intrinsic impossibility, normal impossibility, and impossibility by another. The third type—an act possible in itself but known by Allah not to occur—is accepted as a valid obligation, providing a key insight into how the Hanafi school balances divine foreknowledge with human capacity and choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Distinguish mumtani' li dhatihi (intrinsically impossible), mumtani' li ghayrihi (normally impossible), and the third type (possible in itself but known by Allah not to occur).
2
Determine permissibility for each
Note the Jumhur position: first type not permissible, second type non-occurring but debated, third type permissible and occurring.
Contrast with Ash'ari views.
3
Analyze the basis of the third type
Understand that obligation rests on the servant's power (qudra) and choice (ikhtiyar) at the time of action, not on divine foreknowledge.
4
Apply to the example of Abu Jahl
Classify Abu Jahl's obligation to believe as the third type: possible for him to believe, but Allah knew he would not. The obligation remains valid.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Explanation: Understand a few things as an introduction. (1) Taklif ma la yutaq: making a servant responsible for something beyond his capacity, is it permissible or not? Then does it occur or not? There is a little detail. Taklif ma la yutaq has three types: (1) Mumtani' li dhatihi, i.e., intrinsically impossible, like the conjunction of two opposites. (2) Mumtani' li ghayrihi, i.e., an act intrinsically possible but its occurrence is normally impossible, like flying in the air, creating a body. (3) Third: an act that is in itself possible for the servant, but Allah's knowledge is that this act will not occur from the servant, or Allah's will is that this act will not issue from the servant. Now if the act were to issue from the servant, then divine knowledge would be wrong and Allah's will would be frustrated, and this is impossible. And what is possible but necessitates an impossibility is called impossible by another (muhal bi'l-ghayr). Therefore this act is possible in itself and impossible by another. In the first type, the view of the majority is that obligating it is neither permissible nor does it occur. However, a group of the Ash'ariyyah hold that intellectually it is permissible to make one responsible for it, but it does not occur. In the second type, non-occurrence of obligation is unanimously agreed upon, but there is disagreement about permissibility. The Ash'ariyyah say that making one responsible for it is permissible, because Allah is the true owner of servants, He has every kind of authority; no action of Allah is [prevented]. The third type, which is possible in itself and impossible by another, obligating it is permissible and it does occur, like the faith of Abu Jahl and Abu Lahab. Regarding this, in Allah's eternal knowledge it was determined that they would not believe, yet they are obligated to believe, because believing is intrinsically within their power, and the basis of obligation is the continuation of power and choice. Their not believing being determined in Allah's eternal knowledge does not remove their choice.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the concept of taklif ma la yutaq (obligation of the impossible). The author begins by stating the issue: whether it is permissible for Allah to obligate a servant to do something beyond his capacity, and whether such an obligation can actually occur. He divides the impossible into three categories. The first is intrinsically impossible (mumtani' li dhatihi), like the conjunction of two opposites. The majority (Jumhur) hold that such an obligation is neither permissible nor does it occur. Some Ash'aris say it is intellectually permissible but does not occur. The second is that which is possible in itself but normally impossible due to external factors (mumtani' li ghayrihi), like flying. Here, non-occurrence is agreed upon, but the Ash'aris permit the obligation because Allah is the absolute owner. The third is that which is possible in itself but known by Allah not to occur (muhal bi'l-ghayr). This kind of obligation is permissible and actually occurs, as with Abu Jahl and Abu Lahab being obligated to believe despite Allah's eternal knowledge that they would not. The key point is that the basis of obligation is the existence of power and choice in the servant; divine knowledge does not negate that. Thus, this third type represents the concept of taklif ma la yutaq that is relevant in Hanafi usul: an obligation that is possible for the servant to perform but is accompanied by divine knowledge that it will not happen.

Key Terms
تکلیف مالا يطاق (taklif ma la yutaq): Obligation of that which is beyond one's capacity; classified into three types: intrinsically impossible, normally impossible, and possible in itself but known not to occur.
ممتنع لذاته (mumtani' li dhatihi): That which is impossible in itself, such as the conjunction of two opposites.
ممتنع لغیرہ (mumtani' li ghayrihi): That which is possible in itself but normally impossible due to external factors.
محال بالغیر (muhal bi'l-ghayr): Something possible in itself but which necessitates an impossibility; thus impossible by another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi classification of taklif ma la yutaq, which type is considered permissible and actually occurs?
A) Mumtani' li dhatihi
B) Mumtani' li ghayrihi
C) The third type: possible in itself but known in divine knowledge not to occur
D) None

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates the obligation of an act that is intrinsically possible for the servant, even if divine foreknowledge decrees it will not happen, because obligation rests on capacity and choice.

Kinds of Qudrah: Haqiqiyyah and Muta'arifah
Distinguishing two types of power relevant to obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qudrah haqiqiyyah and qudrah muta'arifah, and explain why qudrah muta'arifah is the basis of obligation in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Obligation is based on conventional power that precedes the act, not on divine facilitation that accompanies it.

In Hanafi usul, the concept of power (qudrah) is central to determining who is obligated. This passage clarifies a critical distinction: divine facilitation (tawfiq) is not the basis of obligation—rather, it is the soundness of means and instruments that precedes the act. By understanding this, you will grasp how the Hanafi school grounds taklif in accessible, measurable capacity, not in unseen grace.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qudrah
From the text, list qudrah haqiqiyyah (real power = divine facilitation) and qudrah muta'arifah (conventional power = soundness of means). Note their definitions and temporal relation to the act.
Focus on the fact that haqiqiyyah accompanies the act, while muta'arifah precedes it.
2
Analyze the argument against haqiqiyyah as basis
The text provides two proofs that haqiqiyyah cannot be the basis of taklif: (a) if it were, a disbeliever would not be obligated since he lacks tawfiq; (b) the basis must precede the act, but haqiqiyyah is concurrent.
These are rational (talil) proofs, not scriptural.
3
Confirm muta'arifah as the basis
Since muta'arifah precedes the act and is a condition for it, it satisfies the requirement for the basis of obligation. The text explicitly states 'مدار تکلیف قدرت متعارفہ ہے'.
Note that 'madar' here means the foundation or criterion.
4
Examine the two subtypes of muta'arifah
Qudrah muta'arifah is subdivided into qudrah mumkinah (minimal power to perform) and qudrah muyassarah (enhanced power that makes performance easy). The text gives zakat examples: having nisab is mumkinah; the passage of a year and productive wealth is muyassarah.
Only mumkinah is required for wujub al-ada'; muyassarah indicates ease but is not necessary for obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) پھر جس قدرت سے بندہ مکلف ہوتا ہے وہ دو طرح کی ہیں (۱) قدرت حقیقیہ جس سے مراد اللہ کی توفیق ہے، (۲) قدرت متعارفہ بمعنی اسباب و آلات کی سلامتی ، قدرت حقیقیہ بندے کے فعل کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے اور فعل کی علت ہوتی ہے اور قدرت متعارفہ فعل پر مقدم ہوتی ہے، مدار تکلیف قدرت متعارفہ ہے، قدرت حقیقیہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ قدرت حقیقیہ اگر مدار تکلیف ہوتی تو کافر مکلف نہ ہوتا، کیونکہ توفیق نہیں ملی تھی ، اگر توفیق ملتی تو وہ بھی ایمان لاتا، دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ جو قدرت مدار تکلیف ہے اس کا فعل پر مقدم ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ یہ قدرت فعل کے لئے شرط ہوتی ہے اور شرط شئی سے پہلے ہوتی ہے، اور قدرت حقیقیہ فعل پر مقدم نہیں ہوتی بلکہ فعل کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، البتہ قدرت متعارفہ فعل سے پہلے ہوتی ہے، لہذا یہی قدرت مدار تکلیف ہے۔ پھر قدرت متعارفہ بمعنی سلامتی اسباب و آلات کی دو قسمیں ہیں، (۱) قدرت ممکنه (۲) قدرت میسرہ - قدرت ممکنہ وہ ادنی مقدار قدرت ہے جس سے بندہ فعل کو ادا کرنے پر قادر ہو جاتا ہے، جیسے مال زکوۃ کے لئے ، اسی کا دوسرا نام مطلقہ اور قاصرہ بھی ہے، اور قدرت میسرہ وہ قدرت ہے جس سے فعل پر بندہ قادر بھی ہو جاتا ہے اور فعل کی ادائیگی آسان اور سہل بھی ہو جاتی ہے، یہ قدرت ممکنہ سے بڑھی ہوئی قدرت ہوتی ہے جیسے زکوۃ میں نصاب پر سال گذرنا اور مال نامی ہونا، یہ قدرت میسرہ ہے۔
(2) Then the power by which the servant is obligated is of two types: (1) qudrah haqiqiyyah (real power), by which is meant Allah's tawfiq (divine facilitation); (2) qudrah muta'arifah (conventional power), meaning soundness of means and instruments. Qudrah haqiqiyyah occurs with the servant's act and is the cause of the act, while qudrah muta'arifah precedes the act. The basis of obligation is qudrah muta'arifah, not qudrah haqiqiyyah, because if qudrah haqiqiyyah were the basis, then the disbeliever would not be obligated, since he was not granted tawfiq; if tawfiq had been granted, he would have believed. The second reason is that the power which is the basis of obligation must precede the act, because it is a condition for the act, and a condition precedes the conditioned. Qudrah haqiqiyyah does not precede the act but occurs with it, whereas qudrah muta'arifah precedes the act. Therefore, this is the power that is the basis of obligation. Then qudrah muta'arifah, meaning soundness of means and instruments, is of two types: (1) qudrah mumkinah (possible power) and (2) qudrah muyassarah (facilitated power). Qudrah mumkinah is the minimal amount of power by which the servant becomes capable of performing the act, like wealth for zakat. It is also called mutlaqah (absolute) or qasirah (limited). Qudrah muyassarah is the power by which the servant becomes capable of the act and the performance becomes easy and smooth; it is a greater power than qudrah mumkinah, like the passage of a year on the nisab and the wealth being growing (namia) in zakat. This is qudrah muyassarah.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage defines and elaborates on the concept of qudrah (power/capacity) as it relates to obligation in Hanafi usul. The author distinguishes between two fundamental types: qudrah haqiqiyyah, which is divine facilitation (tawfiq) that accompanies the act and is its cause; and qudrah muta'arifah, which is the soundness of means and instruments that precedes the act. The key argument is that the basis (madar) of taklif is qudrah muta'arifah, not qudrah haqiqiyyah. The proof is that if divine facilitation were required, a disbeliever could not be obligated, since he lacks it. Moreover, the condition for obligation must precede the act, but qudrah haqiqiyyah is concurrent with the act. Qudrah muta'arifah is further subdivided into qudrah mumkinah (the minimal power to perform) and qudrah muyassarah (an enhanced power making the act easy). In the Hanafi school, qudrah mumkinah is sufficient for the obligation of ada' (performance), while qudrah muyassarah is a higher degree but not required for mere obligation. Examples from zakat illustrate the distinction: having wealth above nisab constitutes qudrah mumkinah for zakat; the passage of a year and the wealth being productive constitute qudrah muyassarah.

Key Terms
قدرت حقیقیہ (qudrah haqiqiyyah): Real power: divine facilitation (tawfiq) that accompanies the act and is its cause.
قدرت متعارفہ (qudrah muta'arifah): Conventional power: soundness of means and instruments that precedes the act.
قدرت ممکنہ (qudrah mumkinah): Minimal power sufficient to perform the act, also called mutlaqah or qasirah.
قدرت میسرہ (qudrah muyassarah): Enhanced power that makes performance easy, e.g., having productive wealth for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul text, which type of power is the basis (madar) of taklif?
A) Qudrah haqiqiyyah
B) Qudrah muta'arifah
C) Qudrah mumkinah
D) Qudrah muyassarah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the basis of obligation is conventional power (qudrah muta'arifah) that precedes the act, not divine facilitation (qudrah haqiqiyyah) that accompanies it.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Condition of Qudrah for Ada' and Qada'
Explaining why qudrah is a condition for ada' but not for qada'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why qudrah mumkinah is a condition for wujub al-ada' but not for wujub al-qada' in Hanafi usul, and apply the concept of mutawahham al-wujud to determine when an obligation is triggered.

Core Idea
Qudrah is required for ada' but not for qada'; the obligation of qada' is the same obligation continuing.

This passage from al-Husami explains a foundational distinction in Hanafi usul: the role of power (qudrah) in the obligation to perform (ada') versus the obligation to make up (qada'). Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the principle that the Shari'ah does not burden a person with the impossible (taklif ma la yutaq), yet still ensures that missed obligations are not lightly set aside.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two obligations
Recognize that the Shari'ah imposes two types of obligation: wujub al-ada' (obligation to perform on time) and wujub al-qada' (obligation to make up after the time). These are not separate obligations; qada' is the continuation of the same original obligation.
The text emphasizes that wujub qada' is 'the same previous obligation' (nafs al-wujub al-sabiq).
2
Understand the condition for ada'
Qudrah mumkinah (minimal power) is a condition for wujub al-ada' to avoid taklif ma la yutaq (impossible burden). The Shari'ah does not oblige an act that is impossible for the individual at the time of performance.
For example, if a person has no time to pray at all, the obligation does not arise.
3
Grasp why qada' does not require qudrah
Since wujub al-qada' is the same obligation as wujub al-ada' (not a new one), imposing the condition of power again would lead to takrar al-wujub (repetition of the obligation) in a single wajib, which is invalid. Therefore, qudrah is not a condition for qada'.
This means even if a person becomes incapable after missing the time, qada' remains obligatory.
4
Apply the concept of mutawahham al-wujud
For the condition of qudrah in ada', it is sufficient that power be 'imagined to exist' (mutawahham al-wujud) at the time the obligation begins. Actual extended time is not necessary; even a moment's possibility triggers the obligation.
Example: If only enough time remains to say the takbirat al-tahrimah in Zuhr, Zuhr becomes obligatory. If time later extends, he performs; otherwise, he makes up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصنف نے وجوب اداء اور وجوب قضاء کے درمیان فرق بیان کیا ہے کہ شریعت نے قدرت ممکنہ کو وجوب ادا کے لئے شرط قرار دیا ہے، لیکن وجوب قضا کے لئے اس کو شرط نہیں قرار دیا ہے، اسی لئے اگر کوئی آدمی وقت میں ادا پر قادر ہو گیا مگر ادا نہیں کر سکا پھر وقت نکلنے کے بعد قدرت زائل ہو گئی تو بھی اس پر قضا واجب ہوگی ، اور قدرت ممکنہ ادا کے لئے شرط ہے اور قضا کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے، قدرت ممکنہ ادا کے لئے شرط اس لئے ہے کہ بندہ پر ادا واجب ہوا اور قدرت ممکنہ نہ ہو تو تکلیف مالا يطاق لازم آئے گی اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور قدرت ممکنہ کا قضا کے لئے شرط نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ سابق میں یہ بات گذر چکی کہ جو ادا کا سبب ہے وہی قضا کا سبب ہے، کیونکہ وجوب قضا وہی سابق وجوب کا بقاء ہے یہ کوئی دوسرا وجوب نہیں ہے، تو گویا دونوں ایک ہی واجب ہوئے ، اور وجوب اداء کے لئے قدرت ممکنہ کو شرط قرار دیا ہے، اب اگر وجوب قضا کے لئے بھی قدرت ممکنہ کو شرط قرار دیں تو واجب واحد میں وجوب کی تکرار لازم آئے گی ، کیونکہ شرط مکرر ہوئی یعنی قدرت ممکنہ تو جو مشروط ہے یعنی وجوب وہ بھی مکرر ہوگا، اور واجب واحد میں ، وجوب کی تکرار باطل ہے، معلوم ہوا کہ وجوب قضا کے لئے قدرت ممکنہ شرط نہیں ہے، لہذا وقت مل جائے تو قضا لازم ہوگی ورنہ فدیہ کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہوگا یا گناہ لازم ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آخر عمر میں فوت شدہ فرائض کی تلافی ضروری ہے اور یہ بات طے شدہ ہے کہ آخر عمر میں اس کی فوت شدہ تمام نمازوں اور روزوں کی ادائیگی پر وہ قادر نہیں ہے، تو نتیجہ وصیت یا اثم کی صورت میں ہوگا، غرض وجوب قضا کے لیے قدرت شرط نہیں ہے، کیوں کہ اس سے فعل مطلوب نہیں ہے۔ ہاں ! اگر مکلف سے فعل مطلوب ہو یعنی قضا کرانا مطلوب ہو تو اس صورت میں قدرت ممکنہ شرط ہے، کیونکہ بغیر قدرت کے مکلف سے فعل طلب کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔

والشرط كونه متوهم الوجود - مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اداء کے لئے جو قدرت ممکنہ کو شرط قرار دیا ہے، تو اس قدرت کا متحقق الوجود ہونا شرط نہیں ہے، بلکہ متوهم الوجود ہونا کافی ہے یعنی حقیقت میں وہ قدرت خارج میں پائی جائے یہ شرط نہیں ہے صرف توہم کافی ہے جیسے ظہر کے وقت میں مکلف کو اتنا وقت ملے کہ وہ چار رکعت پڑھ سکے، یہ قدرت کا تحقق ہے، یعنی حقیقی چار رکعت کی قدرت پائی گئی یہ ضروری نہیں ہے، بلکہ صرف وہم کے درجہ میں قدرت کا امکان ہو، اتنا کافی ہے جیسے ظہر کے وقت میں صرف اتنا وقت ملے کہ تحریمہ کہہ سکے تو ظہر واجب ہو جائے گی ، اب اگر وقت لمبا ہو گیا تو ادا کرے گا ورنہ قضا کرے گا اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قدرت ادا کے لئے شرط ہے، اور شرط مشروط پر مقدم ہوتی ہے، یعنی قدرت ادا سے پہلے ہوتی ہے، اب اگر قدرت کا متحقق الوجود ہونا شرط قرار
The author explained the difference between wujub al-ada' (obligation of performance) and wujub al-qada' (obligation of make-up). The Lawgiver has made qudrah mumkinah a condition for wujub al-ada', but did not make it a condition for wujub al-qada'. Therefore, if a person becomes capable of performance within the time but does not perform, then after the time passes, his power ceases, yet qada' is still obligatory upon him. Quwar mumkinah is a condition for ada' but not for qada'. Why is it a condition for ada'? Because if ada' becomes obligatory and qudrah mumkinah is not present, then that would entail taklif ma la yutaq, which is not permissible. Why is it not a condition for qada'? Because it has already been established that the cause of ada' is the same as the cause of qada', since wujub qada' is the continuation of the previous obligation, not a new obligation. So both are the same wajib. Now, if we make qudrah mumkinah a condition for wujub qada' as well, then in a single wajib, repetition of obligation (takrar al-wujub) would occur, because the condition would be repeated, and the conditioned (wujub) would also be repeated, and repetition of obligation in a single wajib is invalid. Hence, qudrah mumkinah is not a condition for wujub qada'. Therefore, if time remains, qada' is obligatory; otherwise, making a will for fidyah becomes obligatory, or sin becomes inevitable. The proof is that at the end of life, making up missed obligations is necessary, and it is established that at the end of life he is not capable of performing all missed prayers and fasts, so the result is either wasiyyah or ithm. In short, power is not a condition for wujub qada', because what is required is not the act itself. However, if the act is demanded from the mukallaf (i.e., performing qada' is demanded), then qudrah mumkinah is a condition, because demanding an act without power is not permissible. And the condition is that it be imagined to exist (mutawahham al-wujud) - the author stated that for the qudrah mumkinah which is made a condition for ada', it is not necessary that it actually exist in reality; rather, it is sufficient that it be imagined to exist. For example, in the time of Zuhr, the mukallaf gets enough time to say the takbirat al-tahrimah, then Zuhr becomes obligatory. If the time extended, he will perform; otherwise, he will make up. The proof is that power is a condition for ada', and a condition precedes the conditioned, meaning power comes before ada'. If power were required to actually exist as a condition,
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a rule-based exposition of the difference between the obligation to perform (wujub al-ada') and the obligation to make up (wujub al-qada') in relation to the condition of qudrah (power). The author states that the Shari'ah has made qudrah mumkinah (minimal power) a condition for the obligation of ada', but not for the obligation of qada'. The reasoning is twofold: First, if ada' were obligatory without power, it would be taklif ma la yutaq, which is impermissible. Second, the obligation of qada' is actually the same obligation as the original ada' (since it is a continuation), so if we required power again, it would cause repetition (takrar) of the obligation in a single wajib, which is invalid. Therefore, even if a person becomes incapable after the time, qada' remains obligatory. However, if the act of qada' itself is demanded (i.e., the person is required to physically perform it), then power is a condition, because demanding the impossible is not allowed. The passage also clarifies that for the condition of qudrah in ada', it is sufficient that power be 'imagined to exist' (mutawahham al-wujud), not necessarily that it actually occurs. This means that it is enough to have the mere possibility of power at the time of obligation, even if actualization does not occur. An example: if only time for takbirat al-tahrimah remains in Zuhr, Zuhr becomes obligatory; if later time expands, he performs; otherwise, he makes up. This shows that the condition is the mere possibility (tawahhum) of having sufficient time, not actual extended time.

Key Terms
وجوب اداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to perform an act within its prescribed time, conditioned on qudrah mumkinah.
وجوب قضا (wujub al-qada'): The obligation to make up a missed obligatory act; it is the continuation of the original obligation and does not require qudrah mumkinah as a condition.
قدرت ممکنہ (qudrah mumkinah): Minimal power to perform the act; necessary for wujub al-ada' but not for wujub al-qada'.
متوهم الوجود (mutawahham al-wujud): Imagined existence; it is sufficient that the power be potentially present in estimation, even if not actualized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul text, why is qudrah mumkinah not a condition for wujub al-qada'?
A) Because qada' is a new obligation requiring new power
B) Because requiring power for qada' would cause repetition of obligation in a single wajib
C) Because qada' is not obligatory at all
D) Because power is only needed for sunnah acts

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qudrah mumkinah is a condition for the obligation to perform (ada') to avoid impossibility, but not for the obligation to make up (qada'), because qada' is the same obligation continuing; the mere possibility of power (mutawahham al-wujud) is sufficient to trigger ada'.

Difference Between Obligation of Performance and Make-Up
Explaining qudrat mumkinah as condition for ada but not qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that qudrat mumkinah is a condition for wujub al-ada but not for wujub al-qada, and explain the rational proof for this distinction.

Core Idea
For a missed obligation, ability (qudrat) is not a condition for its make-up; otherwise, obligation would be repeated.

This commentary clarifies a key Hanafi usul distinction: potential ability (qudrat mumkinah) is required before an act becomes obligatory to perform on time, but it is not required for the obligation to make up a missed act. The author provides two rational arguments: (1) demanding an impossible act is an unbearable burden, and (2) making ability a condition for both performance and make-up would cause repetition of obligation in a single wajib, which is invalid.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that qudrat mumkinah is a condition for wujub al-ada but not for wujub al-qada.
This is the core ruling of this passage.
2
Analyze the first rational proof
Understand that without qudrat, demanding performance would be an unbearable burden (taklif ma la yutaq), which is impermissible.
This justifies the condition for ada.
3
Analyze the second rational proof
Recognize that wujub al-qada is the continuation of the original wujub, not a new obligation. If qudrat were a condition for both, the condition would be repeated, leading to repetition of obligation, which is invalid.
This justifies the absence of the condition for qada.
4
Identify the practical implication
If a person loses ability after the time expires, qada remains obligatory. If they regain ability later, they must make up; if not, they must either make a will for fidyah or incur sin.
5
Reflect on the logical structure
Note that the rational argument is based on the identity of the obligation: both ada and qada are the same wajib, so repeating the condition would entail repetition of the obligation.
This is a unique Hanafi usul reasoning.

Source Text

الفيضُ الحجازي
۱۲۰
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
کی ادائیگی آسان اور سہل بھی ہو جاتی ہے، یہ قدرت ممکنہ سے بڑھی ہوئی قدرت ہوتی ہے جیسے زکوۃ میں نصاب پر سال گذرنا اور مال نامی ہونا، یہ قدرت میسرہ ہے۔ مصنف ہے وجوب اداء اور وجوب قضاء کے درمیان فرق بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ شریعت نے قدرت ممکنہ کو وجوب ادا کے لئے شرط قرار دیا ہے، لیکن وجوب قضا کے لئے اس کو شرط نہیں قرار دیا ہے، اسی لئے اگر کوئی آدمی وقت میں ادا پر قادر ہو گیا مگر ادا نہیں کر سکا پھر وقت نکلنے کے بعد قدرت زائل ہو گئی تو بھی اس پر قضا واجب ہوگی ، اور قدرت ممکنہ ادا کے لئے شرط ہے اور قضا کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے، قدرت ممکنہ ادا کے لئے شرط اس لئے ہے کہ بندہ پر ادا واجب ہوا اور قدرت ممکنہ نہ ہو تو تکلیف مالا يطاق لازم آئے گی اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور قدرت ممکنہ کا قضا کے لئے شرط نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ سابق میں یہ بات گذر چکی کہ جو ادا کا سبب ہے وہی قضا کا سبب ہے، کیونکہ وجوب قضا وہی سابق وجوب کا بقاء ہے یہ کوئی دوسرا وجوب نہیں ہے، تو گویا دونوں ایک ہی واجب ہوئے ، اور وجوب اداء کے لئے قدرت ممکنہ کو شرط قرار دیا ہے، اب اگر وجوب قضا کے لئے بھی قدرت ممکنہ کو شرط قرار دیں تو واجب واحد میں وجوب کی تکرار لازم آئے گی ، کیونکہ شرط مکرر ہوئی یعنی قدرت ممکنہ تو جو مشروط ہے یعنی وجوب وہ بھی مکرر ہوگا، اور واجب واحد میں ، وجوب کی تکرار باطل ہے، معلوم ہوا کہ وجوب قضا کے لئے قدرت ممکنہ شرط نہیں ہے، لہذا وقت مل جائے تو قضا لازم ہوگی ورنہ فدیہ کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہوگا یا گناہ لازم ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آخر عمر میں فوت شدہ فرائض کی تلافی ضروری ہے اور یہ بات طے شدہ ہے کہ آخر عمر میں اس کی فوت شدہ تمام نمازوں اور روزوں کی ادائیگی پر وہ قادر نہیں ہے، تو نتیجہ وصیت یا اثم کی صورت میں ہوگا، غرض وجوب قضا کے لیے قدرت شرط نہیں ہے، کیوں کہ اس سے فعل مطلوب نہیں ہے۔ ہاں ! اگر مکلف سے فعل مطلوب ہو یعنی قضا کرانا مطلوب ہو تو اس صورت میں قدرت ممکنہ شرط ہے، کیونکہ بغیر قدرت کے مکلف سے فعل طلب کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
Al-Faiz al-Hijazi
120
Urdu commentary on Al-Muntakhab al-Husami
Payment becomes easy and simple; this ability is greater than qudrat mumkinah, like in zakat: the passing of a year on the nisab and the growth of wealth — this is qudrat muyassarah. The author is explaining the difference between obligation of performance and obligation of make-up: that the Shariah has made qudrat mumkinah a condition for the obligation of performance, but has not made it a condition for the obligation of make-up. Therefore, if a person becomes able to perform in time but does not perform, then after the time passes his ability ceases, still make-up is obligatory upon him. Qudrat mumkinah is a condition for performance and not for make-up. Qudrat mumkinah is a condition for performance because when performance is obligatory upon a servant and qudrat mumkinah is not present, then an unbearable burden would be necessary, and that is not permissible. And qudrat mumkinah not being a condition for make-up is because it has passed earlier that whatever is the cause of performance is the same cause of make-up, since the obligation of make-up is the continuation of the previous obligation; it is not a separate obligation. So both are effectively one wajib. And for the obligation of performance, qudrat mumkinah has been made a condition. Now if for the obligation of make-up we also make qudrat mumkinah a condition, then in a single wajib repetition of obligation would be necessary, because the condition is repeated, i.e., qudrat mumkinah, then that which is conditioned, i.e., obligation, would also be repeated. And in a single wajib, repetition of obligation is invalid. It is known that qudrat mumkinah is not a condition for the obligation of make-up. Therefore, if he gets time, make-up will be obligatory; otherwise, making a will for fidyah becomes obligatory, or sin becomes obligatory. Its proof is that at the end of life, compensation for missed obligations is necessary, and it is settled that at the end of life he is not able to perform all missed prayers and fasts. So the result is either will or sin. In short, for the obligation of make-up, qudrat is not a condition, because the action is not demanded from him. Yes! If the action is demanded from the mukallaf, i.e., the performance of make-up is demanded, then in that case qudrat mumkinah is a condition, because demanding an action from the mukallaf without ability is not permissible.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a rule from Al-Husami regarding the distinction between obligation of performance (wujub al-ada) and obligation of make-up (wujub al-qada). The commentator explains that qudrat mumkinah (potential ability) is a condition for the obligation of performance, but not for the obligation of make-up. The reason given is that if qudrat were also a condition for make-up, then in a single wajib (a missed obligation), the obligation would be repeated, which is invalid. Since the obligation of make-up is merely the continuation of the original obligation of performance, making the same condition again would entail repetition of the condition, and thus of the obligation. Furthermore, the commentator provides a proof: at the end of life, a person cannot make up all missed obligations, so qudrat cannot be a condition for make-up; otherwise, no one would be obliged to make up missed acts. However, if the action is actually demanded (i.e., the mukallaf is commanded to perform the make-up), then qudrat is a condition, as demanding the impossible is impermissible.

Key Terms
قدرت ممکنہ (qudrat mumkinah): Potential ability: the capacity to perform an act that is normally within human power, such as having enough time to perform a prayer.
وجوب اداء (wujub al-ada): Obligation to perform an act within its prescribed time.
وجوب قضاء (wujub al-qada): Obligation to make up a missed obligation after its time has elapsed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why is qudrat mumkinah not a condition for the obligation of make-up (wujub al-qada)?
A) Because make-up is not obligatory at all.
B) Because requiring it would lead to repetition of obligation in a single wajib.
C) Because qudrat is only a condition for performance.
D) Because make-up can only be done with qudrat muyassarah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qudrat mumkinah is a condition for the obligation to perform (ada) but not for the obligation to make up (qada), because qada is the continuation of the original obligation and repeating the condition would cause repetition of obligation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Presumed Ability as Condition for Obligation
Defining the condition of ability for obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that qudrat mutawahham al-wujud suffices for wujub al-ada and distinguish it from qudrat muyassarah.

Core Idea
For obligation, mere presumption of ability is sufficient; actual ability is not required.

This lesson unpacks a foundational Hanafi usul principle: what kind of ability (qudrat) is necessary for an obligation to be binding? The text explains that actual ability is not required; rather, the mere presumption that ability could exist (mutawahham al-wujud) is enough. This unlocks obligations even in extremely narrow time windows and transfers rulings when habitual capacity fails.

Guided Path
1
1. Grasp the definition of qudrat mutawahham al-wujud
Identify that the author defines this as ability whose existence is presumed (estimated) even if not actual. It is a mental anticipation of possibility, not a concrete reality.
Contrast with qudrat muhqaqqah (actual ability) which occurs simultaneously with performance.
2
2. Understand the rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
The proof uses the necessary precedence of condition over conditioned. Actual ability cannot precede performance, but presumed ability can. Hence, only presumed ability qualifies as a valid condition for obligation.
This is a qiyas from the general principle that a condition must precede its conditioned.
3
3. Work through the examples
Examine each example (end-of-time puberty, sky-touching oath, traveler without water) to see how the principle operates. In each case, the obligation arises because a possibility (extension of time, miracle, divine intervention) is conceivable, even if normally impossible.
The transfer to qada or tayammum occurs due to 'habitual incapacity', not because the obligation never existed.
4
4. Distinguish qudrat muyassarah from qudrat mumkinah
Note the final line: qudrat muyassarah is a higher degree that changes the description of the wajib to 'easy and simple'. This is a separate category for obligations that inherently require facilitation.
This distinction is key for understanding the scope of the principle.

Source Text

ساتھ ہوتا ہے، جب کہ شرط کا مشروط سے پہلے ہونا ضروری ہے، اور قدرت کا متوھم الوجود ہونا ادا پر مقدم ہوتا ہے، لہذا تو ھم قدرت کو شرط قرار دیں گے۔ اس پر تفریح پیش کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر آخری وقت میں جس میں صرف
