اصل فریضہ واجب ہو گیا ، اب اگر وقت کو اللہ نے ممتد کر دیا تو ادا کر لے لیکن ظاہری طور پر بندہ اس سے عاجز ہے کیونکہ صرف تحریمہ کے بقدر وقت میں فریضہ ادا نہیں کر سکتا، اور امتداد و غیرہ کا صرف امکان ہے، لہذا ظاہرا بندہ کے عجز کی وجہ سے نقل یعنی قضا واجب ہوگی، جیسے کسی نے آسمان چھونے کی قسم کھائی کہ اللہ کی قسم میں آسمان کو چھوڑ نگا تو قسم منعقد ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ آسمان کو چھو ناممکن ہے، محال نہیں ہے، چنانچہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور حضرت عیسیٰ علیہ السلام کے لئے بطور خرق عادت اس کا وقوع ہوا ، جن کے بارے میں قرآن میں خبر دی انا لمسنا السماء__ پس آسمان کو چھونے کی قدرت کا تو ھم ہے امکان ہے اس لئے قسم منعقد ہو جائے گی لیکن ظاہری طور پر بندہ اس کو چھونے سے عاجز ہے،لہذا فوراً حانث ہو جائے گا۔ مصنف اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تو ھم قدرت کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہی ہے جیسے کوئی آدمی سفر میں ہے اور اچانک اس پر نماز کا وقت داخل ہو گیا اور اس کے پاس پانی نہیں ہے، نہ آس پاس میں کہیں پانی ہے، تو اولا اس پر اصل یعنی وضو کا خطاب متوجہ ہوگا، کیونکہ پانی پر قدرت کا تو ھم موجود ہے جیسے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی انگلیوں سے پانی نکلا، حضرت علی بن ابی طالب نے زمین پر پاؤں مارا چشمہ جاری ہوا۔ لیکن چونکہ عادہ پانی پر قدرت سے عاجز ہے اس لئے اس فوری عجز کی وجہ سے حکم اصل (وضو) سے فرع (تیمم) کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گا ، اسی طرح آخر وقت میں بالغ اور مسلمان ہونے کا مسئلہ ہے۔ وَمِنَ الْأَدَاءِ مَالَا يَجِبُ اِلَّا بِقُدْرَةٍ مُيَسِرَةِ لِلْآدَاءِ وَهِيَ زَاعِدَةٌ عَلَى الْأُولَى بِدَرَجَةٍ وَفَرْقُ مَا بَيْنَهُمَا أَنَّ بِالثَّانِيَهِ يَتَغَيَرُ صِفَةُ الْوَاجِبِ فَيَصِيرُ سَمْحًا سَهْلًا
And the condition is that it be presumed to exist. The author (musannif) says regarding the condition of qudrat mumkinah for performance: that this ability actually existing is not a condition; rather, being presumed to exist is sufficient. That is, it is not a condition that this ability be actually found externally; mere presumption is enough. For example, at the time of Zuhr, if the mukallaf gets enough time to say the takbirat al-ihram, then Zuhr becomes obligatory. Now if the time becomes extended, he will perform; otherwise, he will make up. Its proof is that ability is a condition for performance, and the condition is prior to the conditioned; i.e., ability precedes performance. Now if we make actual existence of ability a condition, then actual existence of ability does not precede performance; rather, it occurs simultaneously with performance, whereas it is necessary for the condition to be prior to the conditioned. And the presumed ability does precede performance; therefore, we will make presumed ability the condition. He then elaborates: if at the last moment, when there is only enough time for takbirat al-ihram, a child reaches puberty or a disbeliever becomes Muslim, then prayer becomes obligatory upon them, because presumed ability is found, i.e., there is a possibility that the sun may stop and time may extend. This can happen; it is not impossible. Like in the case of Hadhrat Sulayman (AS), who, due to being occupied with reviewing horses, became heedless of Asr prayer until the sun set. He then started cutting the necks and legs of the horses as expiation for heedlessness, whereupon Allah returned the sun, and he performed Asr prayer. From this it is known that extension of time is possible. Therefore, the original obligation becomes obligatory. Now if Allah extends time, he will perform; but apparently the servant is incapable because he cannot perform the obligation in the time equal to takbirat al-ihram, and extension etc. is only a possibility. Therefore, apparently due to the servant's incapacity, transfer (to make-up) becomes obligatory. Like someone swears an oath to touch the sky, saying 'By Allah, I will touch the sky' — the oath will take effect, because touching the sky is mumkin (possible), not muhal (impossible). Indeed, for the Prophet (SAW) and Hadhrat Isa (AS) it occurred as a miracle. The Quran informs about them 'We have touched the sky'... So touching the sky has presumed ability; there is possibility. Therefore, the oath takes effect, but apparently the servant is incapable of touching it, so he immediately becomes a breaker of the oath. The author says that the example of presumed ability is exactly like a person who is on a journey and suddenly the time for prayer enters, and he has no water, nor is there water nearby. Initially, the original address (wudu) is directed to him, because the presumption of ability over water exists, just as water flowed from the fingers of the Prophet (SAW), and Hadhrat Ali (RA) struck the ground and a spring gushed forth. But since, by habit, he is incapable of ability over water, due to this immediate incapacity, the ruling transfers from the original (wudu) to the secondary (tayammum). Similarly is the issue of reaching puberty and becoming Muslim at the end of time. And from performance, there is that which is only obligatory with a facilitated ability for performance, and it is one degree above the first; and the difference between them is that with the second, the description of the wajib changes, becoming easy and simple.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage defines the Hanafi principle that for the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada), the condition of qudrat (ability) is not required to be actually existing; rather, it is sufficient that the ability be presumed to exist (mutawahham al-wujud). The commentator provides a rational proof: a condition must precede the conditioned. Actual ability does not precede performance; it occurs simultaneously. However, presumed ability does precede, because it is a mental anticipation of possibility. Therefore, presumed ability is the valid condition. He then illustrates with examples: if a boy reaches puberty or a disbeliever accepts Islam at the very end of a prayer time, with only enough time for takbirat al-ihram, the prayer becomes obligatory because there is a possibility that time might extend (as happened with Prophet Sulayman). Similarly, if someone swears to touch the sky, the oath is valid because touching the sky is possible (even if miraculous), so the oath takes effect but the person immediately becomes a breaker because normally it is impossible. Another example: a traveller without water: the obligation of wudu is initially addressed because water is presumably possible (miracles show it can be produced), but due to habitual incapacity, the ruling transfers to tayammum. The passage concludes with a distinction between qudrat mumkinah and qudrat muyassarah: the latter changes the nature of the wajib to something easy.

Key Terms
قدرت متوہم الوجود (qudrat mutawahham al-wujud): Ability whose existence is presumed (estimated) even if not actual; mere possibility suffices for obligation.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins prayer.
قدرت میسرہ (qudrat muyassarah): Facilitated ability that goes beyond mere potential ability; it eases performance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author hold that qudrat mutawahham al-wujud is sufficient for wujub al-ada?
A) Because the Quran explicitly says so.
B) Because actual ability never exists before performance.
C) Because a condition must precede the conditioned, and only presumed ability can precede performance.
D) Because the Shafi'i school also holds this view.

Key Takeaway
For a condition to be valid, it must precede the conditioned; thus, 'presumed ability' suffices for obligation, not actual ability.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Tawahhum al-Qudra: Hypothetical Capacity as a Condition for Obligation
Introducing hypothetical capacity with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tawahhum al-qudra to determine when an obligation becomes binding despite apparent incapacity.

Core Idea
Hypothetical capacity suffices to establish obligation; actual capacity is not required at the moment of obligation.

Can an obligation be imposed when you lack the actual ability to perform it? The Hanafi school introduces the concept of tawahhum al-qudra (hypothetical capacity), which considers the mere possibility of acquiring capacity as sufficient for the initial obligation. This lesson unpacks that principle through vivid examples from the usul text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle being introduced
The passage contrasts hypothetical capacity (tawahhum) with actual capacity and states that the former is considered a condition for obligation.
2
Analyze the first example: last moment of puberty or Islam
The text argues that a child reaching puberty or a disbeliever accepting Islam at the last moment of prayer time does not have actual capacity to pray, but the obligation still arises due to hypothetical capacity (possibility of time extension).
This shows that obligation does not require immediate actual capacity.
3
Examine the analogy with the oath to touch the sky
The passage compares it to swearing an oath to touch the sky. The oath is valid because touching the sky is possible in principle (miracle), even though the person cannot actually do it. Hypothetical capacity triggers legal consequences.
The example illustrates that impossibility does not negate obligation if it is not absolutely impossible.
4
Consider the travel-and-water scenario
A traveler without water is addressed with the obligation of wudu first because water could hypothetically be available (miracle), but due to actual incapacity, the ruling transfers to tayammum.
This demonstrates tawahhum al-qudra as a condition for the initial address.

دونوں کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ دوسری قدرت کی وجہ سے واجب کی صفت بدل جاتی ہے، پس واجب آسان اور سہل ہو جاتا ہے، پس شرط ہوگا اس قدرت کا دوام واجب کی بقاء کے لئے اس لئے کہ حق (واجب) جب واجب ہو گا کسی صفت کے ساتھ تو وہ واجب باقی نہیں رہے گا مگر اسی صفت کے ساتھ ، اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی نصاب کے ہلاک ہونے سے ، اور عشر ساقط ہو جائے گا پیداوار کے ہلاک ہونے سے، اور خراج ساقط ہو جائے گا جب کھیتی کو کوئی آفت ہلاک کر دے، اس لئے کہ شریعت نے ادا کو واجب کیا ہے کیسر کی صفت کے ساتھ ، کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا کہ شریعت نے زکوۃ کو خاص کیا ہے مال نامی اور حولی (جس پر سال گذرا ہو) کے ساتھ ، اور عشر کوحقیقی پیداوار کے ساتھ اور خراج کو زراعت پر قدرت اور اور پر کے ساتھ۔ تشریح:- مصنف ہے قدرت ممکنہ کو بیان کرنے کے بعد قدرت میسرہ کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ بعض ادا قدرت میسرہ سے واجب ہوتی ہیں ، اس میں قدرت ممکنہ کافی نہیں ہے، اور ان دونوں قدرتوں میں دو طرح سے فرق ہے (۱) مفہوم کے لحاظ سے فرق یہ ہے کہ قدرت ممکنہ میں ادنی مقدار کی قدرت ہوتی ہے جس سے بندہ فعل کے ادا کرنے پر قادر ہو جاتا ہے اور قدرت میشرہ میں فعل پر قدرت کے ساتھ آسانی اور سہولت بھی فراہم ہو جاتی ہے (۲) دوسرا فرق حکم کا ہے کہ قدرت میسرہ سے واجب کی ادائیگی میں یسر اور سہولت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے جو قدرت ممکنہ میں نہیں ہوتی ، پس واجب کی صفت بدل جاتی ہے اس میں آسانی اور سہولت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے۔ قدرت میسرہ عام طور پر عبادات مالیہ میں شرط ہے، عبادات بدینہ میں نہیں ہے، کیونکہ مال کی ادائیگی انسان پر زیادہ شاق ہوتی ہے اس لئے شریعت نے قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ ان کی ادار کھی ہے تا کہ سہولت ہو جائے۔ مصنف لیے فرماتے ہیں جو واجب قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ واجب ہوگا اس واجب کے بقاء کے لئے قدرت
They [the scholars] say that the actual existence of capacity (qudra) does not occur before performance, but rather concurrent with performance, while a condition must precede the conditioned. And the hypothetical existence of capacity precedes performance, so we consider hypothetical capacity as a condition. An example of this is: if at the last moment of the time, in which there is only room for the takbir [tahrima], a child reaches puberty or a disbeliever accepts Islam, then prayer becomes obligatory upon them, because hypothetical capacity exists—i.e., there is a possibility that the sun may stop and time may lengthen; this is possible, not impossible, as was done for Prophet Solomon... that due to preoccupation with inspecting horses he forgot the Asr prayer, then said: 'Love of wealth distracted me from the remembrance of Allah until I could not perform the [prayer] even until sunset' then he began to cut the necks and legs of the horses as expiation for the negligence, so Allah returned the sun, and he performed the Asr prayer. This shows that extension of time is possible. Hence the original obligation became due. Now if Allah extends the time, he will perform it, but outwardly he is incapable because in the time equal only to the takbir he cannot perform the obligation; extension is only a possibility. Therefore, due to his apparent incapacity, transfer (naql) i.e., qada becomes obligatory. Similarly, if someone swears: 'By Allah, I will touch the sky', the oath is valid because touching the sky is impossible but not absolutely impossible; it occurred for the Prophet and Isa as a miracle, as the Quran informs: 'We touched the sky' [???]. So hypothetical capacity for touching the sky exists, hence the oath is valid, but outwardly he is incapable, so he becomes a breaker of oath immediately. The author [mussannif] says that the example of hypothetical capacity is exactly like a man in travel when the time for prayer enters and he has no water, neither nearby; then first the original address of wudu is directed to him because hypothetical capacity for water exists, as water came from the fingers of the Prophet and 'Ali struck the earth causing a spring to flow. But since customarily he is incapable of water, due to this immediate incapacity the ruling transfers from the original (wudu) to the substitute (tayammum). Similarly is the issue of reaching puberty and accepting Islam at the last time. And from the acts of performance (ada) is that which is not obligatory except with a capacity that facilitates performance, and this capacity is one degree above the first [possible capacity]. The difference between them is that by the second, the attribute of the obligatory changes, becoming easy and simple. Hence its continuity is required for the continuation of the obligation, because when a right becomes obligatory with a certain attribute, it remains obligatory only with that attribute. For this reason we say that zakat drops with the destruction of the nisab, and ushr with the destruction of the produce, and kharaj when a pestilence destroys the crop, because the law has made performance obligatory with the attribute of ease. Do you not see that it specified zakat with annual growing wealth, ushr with the actual produce, and kharaj with the ability to cultivate. Commentary: After explaining qudra mumkina, the author explains qudra muyassira. He says some acts of performance are obligatory with qudra muyassira; qudra mumkina is not sufficient in them. The difference between these two capacities is in two ways: (1) In meaning: qudra mumkina is the minimal capacity enabling the servant to perform the act, while qudra muyassira provides ease and facility along with capacity. (2) In ruling: qudra muyassira creates ease and facility in performance of the obligation, which is not present in qudra mumkina; thus the attribute of the obligation changes, acquiring ease and facility. Qudra muyassira is generally a condition in financial devotions, not in bodily devotions, because paying wealth is more onerous; therefore the law linked their performance with qudra muyassira for ease. The author says that an obligation that becomes obligatory with qudra muyassira, for its continuation the capacity must continue.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul text explaining the concept of qudra (capacity) in relation to obligations. It distinguishes three types: qudra mumkina (possible capacity), tawahhum al-qudra (hypothetical capacity), and qudra muyassira (facilitating capacity). The author first discusses hypothetical capacity, which is considered a condition for obligation even if actual capacity is not present at the moment, using examples of a child reaching puberty at the end of prayer time or a disbeliever embracing Islam. Then he moves to the definition of qudra muyassira, which is required for certain obligations like zakat, ushr, and kharaj. This capacity not only enables performance but also makes it easy; it is one degree above possible capacity. The key difference is that qudra muyassira changes the attribute of the obligation to 'easy', and its continuity is required for the obligation to remain. Therefore, if the nisab for zakat is destroyed, the obligation falls because the ease is lost. Similarly for ushr and kharaj. The author notes that qudra muyassira is specific to financial acts of worship due to their burden. The commentary follows the matn closely, explaining the two differences between the capacities and the requirement of continuity in qudra muyassira.

Key Terms
توهم القدرة (tawahhum al-qudra): Hypothetical capacity; the possibility of acquiring capacity through extraordinary means (e.g., extension of time or miracle). It is considered a condition for obligation in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of tawahhum al-qudra on the obligation of prayer for a child who reaches puberty at the very end of prayer time?
A) Prayer becomes obligatory immediately but must be performed with tayammum.
B) Prayer becomes obligatory, but because actual capacity is lacking, qada is required.
C) No obligation arises because the child cannot actually pray in that moment.
D) The child must wait until the next prayer time to fulfill the duty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, hypothetical capacity (tawahhum al-qudra) is sufficient to make an obligation binding, even if actual capacity is absent at the moment of obligation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Qudra Muyassira: The Facilitating Capacity in Financial Obligations
Defining qudra muyassira and its effect on financial obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qudra muyassira, distinguish it from qudra mumkina, and apply it to determine the continuity of obligations like zakat, ushr, and kharaj.

Core Idea
Qudra muyassira changes the attribute of an obligation to ease; its continuity is required for the obligation to remain.

Not all obligations are created equal: some require not just the ability to perform, but also a degree of ease. The Hanafi concept of qudra muyassira (facilitating capacity) applies to financial devotions, making them easy and conditional on continued capacity. This lesson unpacks its definition and consequences.

Guided Path
1
Define qudra muyassira in contrast to qudra mumkina
The passage states that qudra muyassira is one degree above qudra mumkina. Identify the two differences: (1) in meaning – qudra mumkina is minimal capacity, while qudra muyassira includes ease; (2) in ruling – qudra muyassira changes the attribute of the obligation to ease.
2
Recognize the scope: financial devotions only
The text specifies that qudra muyassira applies to financial acts like zakat, ushr, and kharaj, not to bodily acts like prayer or fasting. Understand the reason: financial obligations are more burdensome, so ease is legislated.
The condition of annual growth (ḥawl) for zakat is a sign of this capacity.
3
Understand the requirement of continuity
Because the obligation was attached to the attribute of ease, the capacity must persist for the obligation to remain. If the easy condition is lost (e.g., nisab destroyed), the obligation drops.
This is contrasted with qudra mumkina where the obligation does not drop upon loss of capacity.
4
Work through the examples: zakat, ushr, kharaj
The text gives three examples: destruction of nisab drops zakat; destruction of produce drops ushr; pestilence destroying crop drops kharaj. Identify how each illustrates loss of qudra muyassira.
The ease (yusr) is gone, so the obligation is no longer with its required attribute.

کو چھوڑ نگا تو قسم منعقد ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ آسمان کو چھو ناممکن ہے، محال نہیں ہے، چنانچہ حضور صلی الی یم اور حضرت عیسی اللہ کے السلام علیه کے لئے بطور خرق عادت اس کا وقوع ہوا ، جن کے بارے میں قرآن میں خبر دی انا لمسنا السماء__ پس آسمان کو چھونے کی قدرت کا تو ھم ہے امکان ہے اس لئے قسم منعقد ہو جائے گی لیکن ظاہری طور پر بندہ اس کو چھونے سے عاجز ہے،لہذا فوراً حانث ہو جائے گا۔ مصنف ا اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تو ھم قدرت کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہی ہے جیسے کوئی آدمی سفر میں ہے اور اچانک اس پر نماز کا وقت داخل ہو گیا اور اس کے پاس پانی نہیں ہے، نہ آس پاس میں کہیں پانی ہے، تو اولا اس پر اصل یعنی وضو کا خطاب متوجه ہوگا، کیونکہ پانی پر قدرت کا تو ھم موجود ہے جیسے حضور صلی نمی بینم کی انگلیوں سے پانی نکلا، حضرت علی بین اللہ نے زمین پر پاؤں مارا چشمہ جاری ہوا۔ لیکن چونکہ عادہ پانی پر قدرت سے عاجز ہے اس لئے اس فوری عجز کی وجہ سے حکم اصل (وضو) سے فرع ( تیم ) کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے گا ، اسی طرح آخر وقت میں بالغ اور مسلمان ہونے کا مسئلہ ہے۔ وَمِنَ الْأَدَاءِ مَالَا يَجِبُ اِلَّا بِقُدْرَةٍ مُيَسِرَةِ لِلْآدَاءِ وَهِيَ زَاعِدَةٌ عَلَى الْأُولَى بِدَرَجَةٍ وَفَرْقُ مَا بَيْنَهُمَا أَنَّ بِالثَّانِيَهِ يَتَغَيَرُ صِفَةُ الْوَاجِبِ فَيَصِيرُ سَمْحًا سَهْلًا فَيَشْتَرِطُ دَوَامْهَا لِبَقَاءِ الْوَاجِبِ لِاَنَّ الْحَقِّ مَتى وَجَبَ بِصِفَةٍ لَا يَبْقَى وَاجِبًا إلَّا بِتِلْكَ الصِّفِةِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا بِأَنَّهُ يَسْقُطُ الزَّكُوةُ بِهَلَاكِ النِّصَابِ وَالْعُشْرُ بِهَلَاكِ الْخَارِج وَالْخِرَاجُ إِذَا اصْطَلَمَ الزَّرْعَ آفَةٌ لِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ أَوْجَبَ الْآدَاءَ بِصِفَةِ الْيُسْرِ اَلَاتَرى أَنَّهُ خَصَّ الزَّكْوةَ بِالْمَالِ النَّامِي الْحَوْلِى وَالْعُشْرَ بِالْخَارِجِ حَقِيْقَةً وَالْخِرَاجَ بِالتَّمَكُنِ مِنَ الزَّرَاعَةِ ترجمہ :۔ اور ادا میں سے ایک ادارہ ہے جو نہیں واجب ہوتی ہے مگر ادا کو آسان کرنے والی قدرت کے ساتھ ، اور قدرت میسرہ پہلی (قدرت ممكنه ) پر بڑھی ہوئی ہے ایک درجہ، اور ان دونوں کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ دوسری قدرت کی وجہ سے واجب کی صفت بدل جاتی ہے، پس واجب آسان اور سہل ہو جاتا ہے، پس شرط ہوگا اس قدرت کا دوام واجب کی بقاء کے لئے اس لئے کہ حق (واجب) جب واجب ہو گا کسی صفت کے ساتھ تو وہ واجب باقی نہیں رہے گا مگر اسی صفت کے ساتھ ، اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی نصاب کے ہلاک ہونے سے ، اور عشر ساقط ہو جائے گا پیداوار کے ہلاک ہونے سے، اور خراج ساقط ہو جائے گا جب کھیتی کو کوئی آفت ہلاک کر دے، اس لئے کہ شریعت نے ادا کو واجب کیا ہے کیسر کی صفت کے ساتھ ، کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا کہ شریعت نے زکوۃ کو خاص کیا ہے مال نامی اور حولی (جس پر سال گذرا ہو) کے ساتھ ، اور عشر کوحقیقی پیداوار کے ساتھ اور خراج کو زراعت پر قدرت اور اور پر کے ساتھ۔ تشریح:- مصنف ہے قدرت ممکنہ کو بیان کرنے کے بعد قدرت میسرہ کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ بعض ادا قدرت میسرہ سے واجب ہوتی ہیں ، اس میں قدرت ممکنہ کافی نہیں ہے، اور ان دونوں قدرتوں میں دو طرح سے فرق ہے (۱) مفہوم کے لحاظ سے فرق یہ ہے کہ قدرت ممکنہ میں ادنی مقدار کی قدرت ہوتی ہے جس سے بندہ فعل کے ادا کرنے پر قادر ہو جاتا ہے اور قدرت میشرہ میں فعل پر قدرت کے ساتھ آسانی اور سہولت بھی فراہم ہو جاتی ہے (۲) دوسرا فرق حکم کا ہے کہ قدرت میسرہ سے واجب کی ادائیگی میں یسر اور سہولت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے جو قدرت ممکنہ میں نہیں ہوتی ، پس واجب کی صفت بدل جاتی ہے اس میں آسانی اور سہولت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے۔ قدرت میسرہ عام طور پر عبادات مالیہ میں شرط ہے، عبادات بدینہ میں نہیں ہے، کیونکہ مال کی ادائیگی انسان پر زیادہ شاق ہوتی ہے اس لئے شریعت نے قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ ان کی ادار کھی ہے تا کہ سہولت ہو جائے۔ مصنف لیے فرماتے ہیں جو واجب قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ واجب ہوگا اس واجب کے بقاء کے لئے قدرت
They [the scholars] say that the actual existence of capacity (qudra) does not occur before performance, but rather concurrent with performance, while a condition must precede the conditioned. And the hypothetical existence of capacity precedes performance, so we consider hypothetical capacity as a condition. An example of this is: if at the last moment of the time, in which there is only room for the takbir [tahrima], a child reaches puberty or a disbeliever accepts Islam, then prayer becomes obligatory upon them, because hypothetical capacity exists—i.e., there is a possibility that the sun may stop and time may lengthen; this is possible, not impossible, as was done for Prophet Solomon... that due to preoccupation with inspecting horses he forgot the Asr prayer, then said: 'Love of wealth distracted me from the remembrance of Allah until I could not perform the [prayer] even until sunset' then he began to cut the necks and legs of the horses as expiation for the negligence, so Allah returned the sun, and he performed the Asr prayer. This shows that extension of time is possible. Hence the original obligation became due. Now if Allah extends the time, he will perform it, but outwardly he is incapable because in the time equal only to the takbir he cannot perform the obligation; extension is only a possibility. Therefore, due to his apparent incapacity, transfer (naql) i.e., qada becomes obligatory. Similarly, if someone swears: 'By Allah, I will touch the sky', the oath is valid because touching the sky is impossible but not absolutely impossible; it occurred for the Prophet and Isa as a miracle, as the Quran informs: 'We touched the sky' [???]. So hypothetical capacity for touching the sky exists, hence the oath is valid, but outwardly he is incapable, so he becomes a breaker of oath immediately. The author [mussannif] says that the example of hypothetical capacity is exactly like a man in travel when the time for prayer enters and he has no water, neither nearby; then first the original address of wudu is directed to him because hypothetical capacity for water exists, as water came from the fingers of the Prophet and 'Ali struck the earth causing a spring to flow. But since customarily he is incapable of water, due to this immediate incapacity the ruling transfers from the original (wudu) to the substitute (tayammum). Similarly is the issue of reaching puberty and accepting Islam at the last time. And from the acts of performance (ada) is that which is not obligatory except with a capacity that facilitates performance, and this capacity is one degree above the first [possible capacity]. The difference between them is that by the second, the attribute of the obligatory changes, becoming easy and simple. Hence its continuity is required for the continuation of the obligation, because when a right becomes obligatory with a certain attribute, it remains obligatory only with that attribute. For this reason we say that zakat drops with the destruction of the nisab, and ushr with the destruction of the produce, and kharaj when a pestilence destroys the crop, because the law has made performance obligatory with the attribute of ease. Do you not see that it specified zakat with annual growing wealth, ushr with the actual produce, and kharaj with the ability to cultivate. Commentary: After explaining qudra mumkina, the author explains qudra muyassira. He says some acts of performance are obligatory with qudra muyassira; qudra mumkina is not sufficient in them. The difference between these two capacities is in two ways: (1) In meaning: qudra mumkina is the minimal capacity enabling the servant to perform the act, while qudra muyassira provides ease and facility along with capacity. (2) In ruling: qudra muyassira creates ease and facility in performance of the obligation, which is not present in qudra mumkina; thus the attribute of the obligation changes, acquiring ease and facility. Qudra muyassira is generally a condition in financial devotions, not in bodily devotions, because paying wealth is more onerous; therefore the law linked their performance with qudra muyassira for ease. The author says that an obligation that becomes obligatory with qudra muyassira, for its continuation the capacity must continue.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul text explaining the concept of qudra (capacity) in relation to obligations. It distinguishes three types: qudra mumkina (possible capacity), tawahhum al-qudra (hypothetical capacity), and qudra muyassira (facilitating capacity). The author first discusses hypothetical capacity, which is considered a condition for obligation even if actual capacity is not present at the moment, using examples of a child reaching puberty at the end of prayer time or a disbeliever embracing Islam. Then he moves to the definition of qudra muyassira, which is required for certain obligations like zakat, ushr, and kharaj. This capacity not only enables performance but also makes it easy; it is one degree above possible capacity. The key difference is that qudra muyassira changes the attribute of the obligation to 'easy', and its continuity is required for the obligation to remain. Therefore, if the nisab for zakat is destroyed, the obligation falls because the ease is lost. Similarly for ushr and kharaj. The author notes that qudra muyassira is specific to financial acts of worship due to their burden. The commentary follows the matn closely, explaining the two differences between the capacities and the requirement of continuity in qudra muyassira.

Key Terms
قدرة ميسرة (qudra muyassira): A capacity that facilitates performance, making the obligation easy; it is a condition for certain financial obligations.
قدرة ممكنة (qudra mumkina): The minimal possible capacity that enables one to perform the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school rule that zakat drops if the nisab is destroyed before payment?
A) Because zakat is voluntary and can be cancelled anytime.
B) Because the attribute of ease (yusr) in the obligation is lost along with the nisab.
C) Because the poor have no right until the zakat is actually given.
D) Because the nisab must remain intact for the full year after the obligation.

Key Takeaway
Qudra muyassira is a higher level of capacity required for financial obligations; its continuity is essential for the obligation to remain binding.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
9 min
Qudrat Muyassara: Definition and Condition of Continuity
Defines qudrat muyassara and its condition of continuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qudrat muyassara, state its condition of continuity, and apply it to determine when financial obligations (zakat, 'ushr, kharaj) drop in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Financial obligations tied to ease drop when the ease is lost.

This lesson presents a key Hanafi usul principle: qudrat muyassara (facilitated capability) is a condition for the survival of certain financial obligations. The author explains that when an obligation is obligated with the quality of ease (yusr), it remains obligated only as long as that ease persists. This principle has direct practical consequences for zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj, and distinguishes the Hanafi school from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of capability
Identify qudrat mumkina (possible capability) and qudrat muyassara (facilitated capability). Note that qudrat muyassara adds ease and is required for financial ibadat.
Qudrat mumkina is the mere ability to perform; qudrat muyassara includes facility.
2
Understand the condition of continuity
The passage states that qudrat muyassara must be continuous (dawam) for the obligation to survive. If it is lost, the obligation drops.
This is not a condition for initiation but for continuation.
3
Apply to the three examples
Trace how zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj are each obligated with ease, and how the loss of the facilitative factor (destruction of nisab, produce, or crop) causes the obligation to drop.
The examples illustrate the rule's application.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Note the disagreement: Shafi'is hold that once the obligation is established (e.g., after the year passes), it does not drop by destruction. The Hanafi rejoinder is that the obligation was tied to ease, so its loss extinguishes the obligation.
This is a thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) in rulings.
5
Identify the exception for transgression
The passage notes that if the owner deliberately destroys the wealth, the obligation does not drop, because transgression (ta'di) prevents the loss of the obligation.
This shows the condition is linked to legitimate loss, not owner's fault.

قلنا: - واجب کی بقاء کے لئے قدرت میسرہ کا دوام شرط ہے اس لئے احناف کہتے ہیں حولان حول کے بعد زکوۃ کی ادائیگی سے پہلے مال ہلاک ہو جائے تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی، اگر چہ امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک زکوۃ ساقط نہ ہوگی کیونکہ حولان حول کے بعد ادائیگی پر قدرت کی وجہ سے وجوب ثابت ہو چکا اب یہ مال ہلاک ہونے سے ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ ہمارے نزدیک زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی ، پورا مال اگر ہلاک ہو گیا ہے تو پوری زکوۃ ساقط اور بعض مال ہلاک ہوا ہے تو اس کے حصہ کے بقدر زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی ، اور اگر اس نے ہلاک کر دیا ہے تو ہمارے نزدیک بھی ساقط نہ ہوگی ، کیونکہ تعدی ہوئی تو بطور زجر کے وجوب باقی رہے گا۔ بہر حال مال ہلاک ہونے سے زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح پیداوار ہلاک ہو گئی تو عشر ساقط ہو جائے گا اسی طرح اگر آسمانی آفت سے کھیتی بر باد ہوگئی تو خراج ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ زکوۃ ، عشر، اور خراج یہ تینوں چیزیں شریعت نے یسر کے ساتھ واجب کی ہیں ، کیونکہ زکوۃ میں مالِ نامی ہونا اور حولان حول کو شرط قرار دیا جس سے یسر پیدا ہو گیا, جب کہ زکوۃ نفس مال پر بھی بغیر حولان حول اور مال نامی کے واجب ہو سکتی تھی ، اسی طرح عشر حقیقۂ پیداوار کے ساتھ واجب کیا گیا، اس سے لیسر اور سہولت ہوگئی جبکہ عشر نفس زراعت پر بھی واجب ہو سکتا تھا، چاہے حقیقہ پیداوار نہ ہو، اسی طرح خراج میں بارش اور آلات حرث کے ذریعہ زراعت کی قدرت کو شرط قرار دیا یہ یسر کی دلیل ہے ورنہ زمین کے رقبہ پر بھی خراج لگایا جاسکتا تھا۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ تینوں چیزوں میں قدرت میسرہ شرط ہے، اور واجب کے بقاء کے لئے قدرت میسرہ کا دوام شرط ہے لہذا جب قدرت فوت ہو گئی تو تینوں چیزوں میں وجوب ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
And it requires its continuity for the survival of the obligation, because a right, when it becomes obligatory with a quality, does not remain obligatory except with that quality. That is why we said that zakat drops due to destruction of nisab, and ‘ushr drops due to destruction of the produce, and kharaj drops when a pestilence destroys the crop, because the law made performance obligatory with the quality of ease. Do you not see that it specifically assigned zakat to growing, annual wealth, and ‘ushr to actual produce, and kharaj to ability to cultivate? Translation: Among the types of payment is one that is only obligatory with a power that facilitates payment, and facilitated power is one degree higher than the first (possible power). The difference between the two is that due to the second power, the quality of the obligation changes; the obligation becomes easy and convenient. So the continuity of this power is required for the survival of the obligation, because a right (obligation) when it becomes obligatory with some quality, it will not remain obligatory except with that quality. For this reason, we said that zakat drops due to destruction of the nisab, and ‘ushr drops due to destruction of the produce, and kharaj drops when a calamity destroys the crop, because the law obligated performance with the quality of ease. Do you not see that the law specifically assigned zakat to growing, annual wealth, and ‘ushr to actual produce, and kharaj to the power to cultivate and… Commentary: The author, after explaining qadara mumkina, is explaining qadara muyassara. He says that some payments become obligatory with qadara muyassara; qadara mumkina is not sufficient. The difference between these two capabilities is twofold: (1) in terms of meaning, qadara mumkina is the minimal ability that enables the servant to perform the act, while qadara muyassara provides ease and facility along with the ability; (2) in terms of ruling, qadara muyassara creates ease and facility in the performance of the obligation, which is not found in qadara mumkina. Thus the quality of the obligation changes; it acquires ease and facility. Qadara muyassara is generally required in financial acts of worship, not in physical acts, because the payment of wealth is more burdensome for a person, so the law obligated them with qadara muyassara to facilitate. The author says: an obligation that becomes obligatory with qadara muyassara, the continuity of qadara muyassara is a condition for its survival; if qadara muyassara does not remain, the obligation will also not remain, because the obligation was initially legislated with a quality, i.e., ease. It will remain only with that quality. So we said: the continuity of qadara muyassara is a condition for the survival of the obligation. Therefore, Hanafis say that if after the passage of a year, before paying zakat, the wealth is destroyed, zakat drops, even though, according to Imam Shafi‘i, zakat does not drop, because after the passage of a year, due to the ability to pay, the obligation is established and will not drop by destruction of the wealth. According to us, zakat drops; if all wealth is destroyed, all zakat drops; if some wealth is destroyed, zakat drops proportionally. But if the person himself destroys it, according to us it does not drop, because there is transgression, so the obligation remains as a deterrent. In any case, zakat drops from destruction of wealth. Similarly, if the produce is destroyed, ‘ushr drops; similarly, if a heavenly calamity destroys the crop, kharaj drops. Because zakat, ‘ushr, and kharaj — these three things are obligated by the law with ease. Because in zakat, the conditions of growing wealth and the passage of a year were stipulated, which created ease, whereas zakat could have been obligated on the wealth itself without the passage of a year and without growth. Similarly, ‘ushr was obligated with actual produce, creating ease, whereas ‘ushr could have been obligated on cultivation itself, whether there is actual produce or not. Similarly, in kharaj, the ability to cultivate via rain and tools was made a condition; this is evidence of ease, otherwise kharaj could have been imposed on the area of land. Summary: In all three, qadara muyassara is a condition, and the continuity of qadara muyassara is a condition for the survival of the obligation; therefore, when the capability is lost, the obligation drops in all three.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of qudrat muyassara (facilitated capability) as a condition for certain obligations. The author explains that some obligations, like zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj, are obligated with ease (yusr). For these obligations, the continuity of this facilitated capability is required for the obligation to remain. If the capability is lost (e.g., wealth destroyed after the year passes), the obligation drops. This is a Hanafi position, contrasted with Imam Shafi‘i's view that once the obligation is established, it does not drop. The passage also distinguishes between qudrat mumkina (possible capability) and qudrat muyassara, and provides detailed reasoning for the drop in zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj, including the case of transgression (ta'di). The lesson is a ruling type: a condition for the survival of an obligation.

Key Terms
قدرة ميسرة (qudrat muyassara): القدرة التي تيسر الأداء وتجعل الواجب سهلاً
قدرة ممكنة (qudrat mumkina): القدرة التي تمكن من الفعل دون يسره
يسر (yusr): السهولة التي وصف بها الواجب في الشريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the obligation of zakat if the nisab is destroyed after the passage of a year but before payment?
A) The obligation remains and must be paid from other wealth.
B) The obligation drops because the facilitated capability is lost.
C) The obligation drops only if the destruction was not caused by the owner.
D) The obligation drops only if the owner intended to avoid payment.

Key Takeaway
Qudrat muyassara is a condition for the survival of financial obligations in the Hanafi school; its loss causes the obligation to drop, except in cases of transgression.

Extending the Qudrat Muyassara Principle: Oath-Breaker's Kaffarah by Qiyas on Zakat
Expansion of the qudrat muyassara principle to kaffarah via qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas to extend the principle of qudrat muyassara from zakat to oath-breaking kaffarah, and identify the effective cause (illa).

Core Idea
When wealth is lost, the obligation shifts to an easier form — the same principle governs zakat and oath-breaking kaffarah.

This passage demonstrates how the Hanafi school uses qiyas to extend a well-established principle from one area of fiqh to another. The principle of qudrat muyassara (the obligation takes into account present ability) is first applied in zakat: if wealth is lost, zakat is no longer due. Here, the same reasoning is applied to oath-breaking expiation: if the person has no wealth, he may fast instead. The passage carefully explains the analogy and the condition that consumption of wealth is not considered transgression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases being compared
The original case (asl) is zakat when wealth is lost; the new case (far') is oath-breaker's kaffarah when wealth is lost. Recognize that both involve a financial obligation that is affected by loss of wealth.
The passage explicitly says 'fakana min qabil al-zakat' (it is of the same category as zakat).
2
Extract the illa (effective cause)
Determine the common attribute that justifies transferring the ruling. The passage points to 'present inability despite expectation of future capability' and the desire for ease (taysir). The illa is the principle of qudrat muyassara: the obligation is conditioned on present ability.
Both zakat and kaffarah are financial obligations obligated with ease (yusr).
3
Verify the illa's validity in both cases
Check that the illa is present in the asl (zakat: if nisab is lost, no obligation) and in the far' (kaffarah: if wealth is gone, transfer to fasting). Confirm no countervailing factor.
The passage equates lawful consumption (istihlak) with destruction (halak) because there is no transgression on others' rights.
4
Derive the ruling for the far'
Since the illa applies, the ruling of the asl (ease in obligation) is transferred to the far'. The oath-breaker may fast instead of paying with wealth.
The passage states 'kaffara bi al-sawm' (expiates by fasting).
5
Note the distinction: wealth is not 'ayn (specific)
In zakat, the nisab is specific; here any wealth acquired later continues capability. This nuance strengthens the analogy, showing flexibility.
The passage says 'al-mal hunna ghayr 'ayn' (wealth here is not specific).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا اِنَّ الْحَانِثَ فِي الْيَمِيْنِ اِذَاذَهَبَ مَالُهُ كَفَرَ بِالصَّوْمِ لِاَنَّ التَّخْبِيرَ فِي أَنْوَاعِ التَّكْفِيْرِ بِالْمَالِ وَالنَّقَلَ عَنْهُ إِلَى الصَّوْمِ لِلْعَجْزِ فِى الْحَالِ مَعَ تَوَهُم الْقُدْرَةِ فِيْمَا يَسْتَقْبِلُ تَيْسِيرًا لِلْآدَاءِ فَكَانَ مِنْ قَبيْلِ الزَّكْوةِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمَالَ فَهُنَا غَيْرُ عَيْنٍ فَأَيُّ مَالٍ أَصَابَهُ مِنْ بَعْدُ دَامَتْ بِهِ الْقُدْرَةُ وَلِهَذَا سَاوَى الْإِسْتِهْلَاكُ الْهَلَاكَ فَهُنَا لِإِنْعِدَامِ التَّعَدِى عَلَى مَحَل مَشْغُولٍ بِحَقَّ الْغَيْرِ ترجمہ :۔ اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ قسم میں حانث ہونے والا جب اس کا مال ختم ہو جائے تو وہ روزے سے کفارہ ادا کرے گا اس لئے کہ کفارہ کی اقسام میں پہلے مال سے تخبیر ہے، اور پھر اس سے روزے کی طرف انتقال عجز حال کی وجہ سے ہے، ساتھ ہی مستقبل میں قدرت کے گمان کی وجہ سے یہ آسانی ہے ادائیگی میں۔ پس یہ زکوۃ جیسا ہے مگر یہاں مال معین نہیں ہے، پس جو بھی مال اسے بعد میں ملے گا اس کے ذریعہ قدرت باقی رہے گی۔ اور اسی وجہ سے یہاں استہلاک (خرچ کرنا) ہلاک کے برابر ہے، کیونکہ کسی ایسی جگہ پر تعدی نہیں ہے جو دوسرے کے حق سے مشغول ہو۔
And for this reason we said that the one who breaks an oath, when his wealth is gone, he expiates by fasting, because the choice among the types of expiation is with wealth, and the transfer from it to fasting is due to present inability despite the expectation of future capability, to facilitate performance. So it is of the same category as zakat, except that the wealth here is not specific; so whatever wealth he obtains later, capability continues with it. And for this reason, consumption (using up) is equated with destruction here, because there is no transgression upon a place occupied by the right of another. Translation: And for this reason we said that the one who breaks an oath, when his wealth is gone, he will expiate by fasting, because among the types of expiation, the initial choice is with wealth, and then the transfer to fasting is due to present inability, along with the assumption of capability in the future; this is ease in performance. So it is like zakat, except that here the wealth is not specific; so whatever wealth he obtains later, capability continues with it. And for this reason, consumption (using up) is equivalent to destruction here, because there is no transgression upon something occupied by the right of another.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage extends the principle of qudrat muyassara to the case of an oath-breaker. If a person breaks an oath and cannot afford the kaffarah (which is normally freeing a slave, feeding, or clothing), he may fast due to lack of wealth. This is similar to zakat, where if wealth is lost, the obligation drops. However, here, if he later acquires wealth, his capacity returns, and the fasting is sufficient? Actually, the text says the continuity of capability with any wealth he obtains. The key point is that 'consumption' (using up wealth) is treated like 'destruction' because there is no transgression (ta'di) on a right of another. This means if he spent his wealth lawfully, he is excused and can fast. The passage shows the Hanafi application of the principle of ease (yusr) to expiation (kaffarah).

Key Terms
حانث (hanith): شخص حنث في يمينه، أي لم يف بما حلف عليه
كفارة (kaffarah): ما يجب تكفيراً للذنب أو الحنث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because using wealth wastefully is a sin.
B) Because there is no transgression on the rights of others involved.
C) Because both lead to the same result of poverty.
D) Because the wealth is not specific.

Key Takeaway
When wealth is lost, the Hanafi school uses qiyas based on the principle of ease to allow fasting as expiation for a broken oath.

Continuation of Capacity: Usul Principle for Financial Expiation
Explaining the condition of continuous capacity for the obligation of kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that the continuation of an obligation (baqa' al-wajib) requires the continuation of its condition (qudrat muyassarah) to determine whether a financial expiation obligation shifts to fasting when capacity is lost.

Core Idea
Obligation requires continuous capacity; if capacity ends, the obligation shifts—unless the wealth is unspecified.

In this passage from al-Husami, the author explains a key usul principle: a wajib that depends on a condition (like capacity) only continues as long as that condition persists. Using the example of kaffarah for breaking an oath, he shows how the obligation shifts from financial expiation to fasting when wealth is destroyed—because capacity is lost. But unlike zakat, where wealth is specified, in kaffarah the wealth is unspecified, so the obligation can return when new capacity arises. This nuanced discussion teaches us how Hanafi usul handles the relationship between conditions and the persistence of obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle: baqa' al-wajib requires baqa' al-shart
The passage states that for the continuation of an obligation (baqa' al-wajib), the continuation of available capacity (qudrat muyassarah) is a condition. This is a fundamental usul rule.
The shart here is capacity; if capacity ends, the wajib falls or shifts.
2
Apply to the case of kaffarah after oath violation
The author gives the example: if a person violates an oath (hanith), financial expiation becomes wajib. But if his wealth is destroyed before he fulfills it, the obligation shifts to fasting because capacity is lost. This illustrates the principle in action.
Note: the shift is to a lighter form of expiation (fasting) to ease the burden.
3
Analyze the proofs for the principle
Two proofs are given: (1) The Shari'ah gave a choice among three types of financial expiation, showing ease is intended. (2) The ruling is transferred from wealth to fasting due to immediate incapacity, even though future capacity is imagined. This confirms that the obligation depends on current capacity.
The second proof uses the case of an aged person (shaykh fani) where permanent incapacity is considered, contrasting temporary incapacity here.
4
Address the objection: comparison with zakat
An objection is raised: if financial expiation is like zakat, why does the obligation return when new wealth arrives? The response distinguishes: in zakat, wealth is specified (mu'ayyan); when it is destroyed, the obligation falls permanently. In expiation, wealth is unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyan); new wealth restores capacity, so the obligation returns.
This distinction is crucial: the nature of the property (specified vs unspecified) determines whether the obligation is tied to a particular asset or to the person's capacity.
5
Understand the consequence for istihlak vs halak
Because wealth in expiation is unspecified, there is no right of another person attached to it. Therefore, if the owner himself destroys the wealth (istihlak) or it is destroyed externally (halak), both are equivalent—the obligation falls. In zakat, since the poor have a right, willful destruction does not cancel the obligation; it remains a liability.
This highlights how the presence of another's right affects the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کفارہ ادا کرے گا ، اس لئے کہ کفارہ بالمال کی انواع میں اختیار دینا، اور کفارہ بالمال سے مستقبل میں تو ھم قدرت کے باوجود فی الحال عجز کی وجہ سے روزہ کی طرف انتقال، ادا کو آسان بنانے کے لئے ہے، تو کفارہ بالمال زکوۃ کے قبیل سے ہو گا، مگر یہ کہ یہاں مال غیر معین ہے تو جو مال بھی اس کو پہنچے گا اس کے ( حنث اور عجز کے ) بعد تو اس کے ذریعہ قدرت کا دوام ہو جائے گا، اور اسی لئے یہاں استہلاک ہلاک کے مساوی ہوگا تعدی کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسے حل پر جو مشغول ہے غیر کے حق کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح:- ماقبل میں بتایا کہ بقائے واجب کے لئے قدرت میسرہ کا بقاء شرط ہے، اگر قدرت میسرہ نہ رہے تو واجب ساقط ہو جائے گا، لہذا اگر کوئی شخص قسم میں حانث ہو جائے تو اس پر کفارہ بالمال واجب ہے یعنی غلام آزاد کرے یا دس مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلائے یا دس مسکینوں کو کپڑا پہنائے لیکن حانث ہونے کے بعد اس کا سارا مال ہلاک ہو گیا ، تو اب روزے سے کفارہ ادا کرے گا۔ کفارہ بالمال کے قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مالی کفارہ میں شریعت نے تین چیزوں میں اختیار دیا ہے، یہ دلیل ہے کہ کفارہ میں میسر اور سہولت ملحوظ ہے، کیونکہ اختیار ملنے سے آسانی پیدا ہوتی ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فوری عجز کی وجہ سے شریعت نے مال سے روزہ کی طرف حکم کومنتقل کر دیا حالانکہ آئندہ مال کے آنے کا امکان و توھم موجود ہے، تو با وجود توهم قدرت کے فوری عجز کی وجہ سے مال سے روزہ کی طرف حکم کو منتقل کرنا یہ مکلف پر آسانی کرنے کے لئے ہے، ورنہ شیخ فانی کے حق میں اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا ہے، بلکہ اس میں روزہ سے فدیہ کی طرف حکم کو منتقل کرنے میں دائمی عجز کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے، یعنی شیخ فانی ابھی روزے سے عاجز ہے، مگر شریعت نے اس فوری عجز کا اعتبار نہیں کیا، بلکہ دائمی عجز کا اعتبار ہے کہ اس کا یہ عجز دائمی ہو ، اور یہ معلوم ہو گا موت پر لہذا اس وقت وہ فدیہ دے سکتا ہے۔ اور یہاں فوری عجز کا اعتبار ہے، یہ دلیل ہے کہ کفارہ مالی قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ واجب ہوا ہے، لہذا اس کی مثال زکوۃ جیسی ہو گئی ، جیسے زکوۃ میں بقاء واجب کے لئے قدرت شرط ہے ایسے ہی مالی کفارہ میں بھی شرط ہے۔ الا ان المال ههنا - ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا کہ کفارہ مالی زکوۃ کے قبیل سے ہے، اسی لئے مال کے ہلاک ہونے سے کفارہ مالی ساقط ہو جاتا ہے، اور حکم روزے کی طرف منتقل ہو جاتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ میں مال کے ہلاک ہونے سے زکوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، تو پھر دوسرا مال آنے سے کفارہ مالی کا وجوب لوٹ کر نہیں آنا چاہیے جیسے زکوۃ میں وجوب لوٹ کر نہیں آتا، اگر زکوۃ کا مال ہلاک ہو گیا پھر بعد میں اس کے پاس مال آیا تو اس پر سابق زکوۃ نہ واجب ہوگی، بلکہ اس مال پر جب سال گزرے گا تو زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، حالانکہ آپ کہتے ہیں کہ حانث کے پاس جب دوسرا امال آجائے گا تو دوبارہ کفارہ مالی واجب ہوگا تو کفارہ مالی زکوۃ کے قبیل سے کہاں ہوا؟ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ کفارہ مالی زکوۃ کے قبیل سے ہے، قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ واجب ہونے میں البتہ دونوں میں تھوڑا فرق ہے، وہ یہ کہ زکوۃ میں مال معین ہوتا ہے، اور جب یہ مال ہلاک ہو گیا تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی ، اور دوسرا مال جب اس کے پاس آگیا تو یہ اس کے قائم مقام نہیں ہوگا، لہذا جب اس دوسرے مال پر سال گذرے گا تو زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، وہ پہلا واجب تو ساقط ہی ہو گیا، اور کفارہ مالی میں معین مال کے ساتھ کفار متعلق نہیں ہوتا ہے بلکہ مطلق مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے، لہذا جب دوسرا مال آجائے گا تو قدرت ثابت ہو جائے گی لہذا دوبارہ کفارہ مالی واجب ہوگا۔ اسی فرق کی وجہ سے کہ کفارہ مالی میں مال غیر معین ہوتا ہے مال کا ہلاک ہونا اور ہلاک کرنا دونوں برابر ہیں یعنی جس طرح مال کے ہلاک ہونے سے کفارہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور کفارہ کا حکم روزہ کی طرف لوٹ جاتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی مال کے ہلاک کرنے سے بھی کفارہ ساقط اور حکم روزے کی طرف لوٹ جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ زکوۃ میں ایسا نہیں ہے، زکوۃ میں مال ہلاک ہونے سے تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے مگر ہلاک کرنے سے زکوۃ ساقط نہیں ہوتی بلکہ زجر او جوب باقی رہتا ہے، کیونکہ زکوۃ میں مال معین ہوتا ہے تو اس کو ہلاک کرنا ایسے محل پر تعدی اور زیادتی کرنا ہے جو حل دوسرے کے یعنی فقیر کے حق کے ساتھ مشغول ہے، گویا اس نے ہلاک کر کے فقیر پر ظلم و تعدی کی ، اور کفارہ میں ایسے محل پر تعدی نہیں ہے جو دوسرے کے حق کے ساتھ مشغول ہو، کیونکہ اس میں مال غیر معین ہوتا ہے، کسی غیر کے حق کے ساتھ مشغول ہے ہی نہیں ، لہذا کفارہ میں ہلاک داستهلاک دونوں کا حکم یکساں ہے۔
He will perform expiation, because giving choice in the types of financial expiation, and transferring the ruling from financial expiation to fasting due to temporary incapacity despite the existence of future potential capacity, is to make performance easy. So financial expiation will be of the category of zakat, except that here wealth is unspecified, so whatever wealth reaches him after (his violation and incapacity), through it his capacity will be prolonged. And for this reason, here consumption is equivalent to destruction due to the absence of transgression upon a locus that is occupied with another's right. Explanation: Previously it was stated that for the continuation of an obligation, the continuation of available capacity is a condition; if available capacity does not remain, the obligation will fall. So if a person violates an oath, then financial expiation is obligatory upon him, i.e., free a slave or feed ten poor or clothe ten poor. But after violation, all his wealth is destroyed. Then he will perform expiation by fasting, because financial expiation was obligatory with available capacity; therefore for the continuation of the obligation, continuation of capacity is a condition. When the wealth is destroyed, capacity does not remain, so now financial expiation will not be obligatory, and he will perform expiation by fasting. The proof that financial expiation is obligatory with available capacity is that the Shari'ah gave choice among three things in financial expiation. This is proof that ease and facility are considered in expiation, because choice produces ease. The second proof is that due to immediate incapacity, the Shari'ah transferred the ruling from wealth to fasting, even though the possibility and imagination of future wealth exists. So despite the imagination of capacity, transferring the ruling from wealth to fasting due to immediate incapacity is to make it easy for the obligated person. Otherwise, in the case of an aged person who is permanently weak, this is not considered; rather, in that case, in transferring the ruling from fasting to ransom, permanent incapacity is considered. That is, the aged person is currently unable to fast, but the Shari'ah did not consider this immediate incapacity; rather permanent incapacity is considered that his incapacity is permanent, and this will be known upon death, so at that time he can give ransom. And here immediate incapacity is considered. This is proof that financial expiation is obligatory with available capacity. Therefore its example became like zakat. Just as in zakat, for continuation of the obligation, capacity is a condition, similarly in financial expiation it is also a condition. 'Except that here wealth' - this is a response to an objection. The gist of the objection is: You said that financial expiation is of the category of zakat, therefore when wealth is destroyed, financial expiation falls, and the ruling transfers to fasting, just as in zakat when wealth is destroyed, zakat falls. So then when another wealth comes, the obligation of financial expiation should not return, as in zakat the obligation does not return. If zakat wealth is destroyed and later he gets wealth, the previous zakat is not obligatory; rather zakat will be obligatory on this wealth when a year passes. Yet you say that when another wealth comes to the violator, financial expiation becomes obligatory again. So how is financial expiation of the category of zakat? He is answering that financial expiation is of the category of zakat in terms of being obligatory with available capacity; however, there is a slight difference between them. That is, in zakat wealth is specified. When this wealth is destroyed, zakat will fall, and when another wealth comes, it will not take its place. So when a year passes on this second wealth, zakat will be obligatory; the first obligation has indeed fallen. In financial expiation, expiation is not attached to specified wealth but is attached to absolute wealth. So when another wealth comes, capacity is established, so financial expiation becomes obligatory again. Due to this difference, because in financial expiation wealth is unspecified, the destruction of wealth and making it perish are both equal; that is, just as by the destruction of wealth expiation falls and the ruling of expiation shifts to fasting, similarly by making wealth perish also expiation falls and the ruling shifts to fasting. While in zakat it is not so. In zakat, by destruction of wealth, zakat falls, but by making it perish, zakat does not fall; rather the obligation remains, because in zakat wealth is specified. So making it perish is transgression and excess upon a locus that is occupied with the right of another, i.e., the poor. It is as if by making it perish he has wronged and transgressed against the poor. In expiation, there is no transgression upon a locus occupied with another's right, because wealth is unspecified; it is not occupied with any other's right. Therefore in expiation, the ruling of destruction and consumption is equal.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and its proof concerning the condition of continuous capacity for the obligation of financial expiation (kaffarah bil-mal). The author begins by stating that if a person violates an oath and becomes liable for financial expiation, but then his wealth is destroyed, the obligation shifts to fasting because the condition of available capacity must continue for the obligation to remain. The proof is twofold: first, the Shari'ah gave a choice among three types of financial expiation, indicating that ease is intended; second, the ruling is transferred from wealth to fasting in case of immediate incapacity, even if future capacity is imagined. This shows that the obligation is contingent on available capacity. The author then analogizes it to zakat, where capacity is also a condition for continuity. An objection is raised: if it is like zakat, why does the obligation of expiation return when new wealth arrives, while zakat does not return? The response distinguishes: in zakat, wealth is specified (mu'ayyan), so when it is destroyed, the obligation falls permanently; new wealth is a new subject for zakat. In expiation, wealth is unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyan), so when new wealth comes, capacity is restored and the same expiation becomes obligatory again. Additionally, in zakat, actively destroying wealth (istikhlak) does not cancel the obligation because the wealth is occupied with the poor's right, making it a transgression. In expiation, there is no such right, so destruction and consumption are equivalent. This passage teaches a fundamental usul principle: the continuation of an obligation depends on the continuation of the condition that gave rise to it. It also refines the analogy by showing how a difference in the nature of the property (specified vs. unspecified) can produce different rulings.

Key Terms
قدرت میسرہ (qudrat muyassarah): Available capacity; the condition of having the financial means at the time of obligation and its continuation.
بقائے واجب (baqa' al-wajib): Continuation of an obligation; a principle that once an obligation is established, its continuation requires the continued existence of its condition.
استہلاک (istihlak): Consumption or destruction of property by the owner's own action, as opposed to destruction by external cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle explained in the passage, if a person liable for financial expiation for an oath violation has his wealth destroyed, and later acquires new wealth, what is the ruling?
A) The obligation of financial expiation is permanently cancelled.
B) The obligation shifts to fasting permanently.
C) The obligation returns as financial expiation because wealth is unspecified.
D) The obligation returns as financial expiation only if the new wealth is equal to the original amount.

Key Takeaway
The continuation of a wajib depends on the continuation of its condition; in kaffarah, capacity is the condition, and the obligation shifts if capacity is lost but returns when capacity is regained because wealth is unspecified.

Conditions of Obligation vs. Continuation: Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr
Distinguishing conditions of obligation from conditions of continuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions for initial obligation (shurut al-wujub) and conditions for continuation (shurut al-dawam) using the Hanafi examples of Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr, and apply this principle to other acts.

Core Idea
The condition that triggers an obligation may vanish, but the obligation remains.

This lesson examines a key usul principle: not all conditions for an act becoming obligatory remain necessary for its continuation. The text uses Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr as case studies to illustrate that financial ease (yusr) is a condition for the initial obligation but not for its persistence. Understanding this distinction prevents errors in determining when an obligation lapses and helps in the correct application of Hanafi rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two case studies
Locate the two acts discussed: Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr. Note the specific conditions mentioned for each at the time of obligation.
For Hajj: mumkinah min al-safar (ability to travel) and yusr (financial ease). For sadaqat al-fitr: qudrah (capacity) defined as ghina (sufficiency).
2
Extract the condition that is not required for continuation
The text states that having servants, helpers, and actual mounts is not a condition by consensus. Similarly, yusr is not required for the act to remain obligatory. Identify the reasoning: 'wa laysa dhalika bi-shartin bi al-ijma'.
The consensus (ijma) is that certain details of ability are not conditions at all, even initially, but the principle here is about conditions that are initially required but not for remaining.
3
Understand the reasoning for sadaqat al-fitr
The text says sadaqat al-fitr becomes obligatory even with only basic clothing (thiyab al-balah) because these are not productive (namiyah). Thus yusr is not a condition; rather, qudrah (being able to give without hardship) is the condition. This demonstrates that the condition for obligation is not necessarily persistent.
The key difference: yusr requires surplus wealth that grows, while qudrah is simply having enough to give without falling into need.
4
Generalize the usul principle
State the derived principle: 'The condition for the initial obligation of an act (shart al-wujub) is not necessarily a condition for its continuation (shart al-dawam).' Once the obligation becomes established, it remains even if the condition ceases.
This principle applies to various acts in Hanafi fiqh, e.g., zakat becomes due when nisab is reached; if nisab falls below, the obligation for that year's zakat still stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْحَج فَالشَّرْطُ فِيهِ الْمُمَكِنَةُ مِنَ السَّفَرِ الْمُعْتَادِ بِرَاحِلَةِ وَزَادٍ وَالْيُسْرلَايَقَعُ الَّا بِخَدَم وَأَعْوَانٍ وَمَرَاكِب وَلَيْسَ ذَلِكَ بِشَرْطِ بِالْإِجْمَاع - فَلِذَلِكَ لَمْ يَكُنْ شَرْطًا لِدَوَامِ الْوَاجِب وَكَذَلِكَ صَدَقَةُ الْفِطْرِ لَمْ تَجِبْ بِصِفَةِ الْيُسْرِ بَلْ بِشَرْطِ الْقُدْرَةِ وَهُوَ الْغِنَا لِيَصِيرَ الْمَوْصُوْفُ بِهِ أَهْلَا لِلْإِغْنَاءِ أَلَا تَرَىٰ أَنَّهُ يَجِبْ بِثِيَابِ الْبَلَةِ وَلَا يَقَعُ بهَا الْيُسْرُ لأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِنَامِيَةِ فَلَمْ يَكُن الْبَقَاء مُفْتَقِرًا إِلَى دَوَامِ شَرْطِ الْوُجُوبِ
As for Hajj, the condition in it is the ability to travel the normal journey with a mount and provisions, and ease. It is not realized except with servants, helpers, and mounts, and that is not a condition by consensus. Therefore it was not a condition for the continuation of the obligatory act. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr was not obligated with the quality of ease, but with the condition of capacity, which is sufficiency, so that the person described becomes worthy of giving. Do you not see that it becomes obligatory with clothes of need, and ease is not realized by them because they are not productive. So the continuation is not dependent on the continuation of the condition of obligation.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the obligation of Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr, specifically distinguishing between conditions for initial obligation and conditions for continuation. The author states that for Hajj, the condition is the ability to undertake the customary journey with a riding mount (raahilah), provisions (zaad), and financial ease (yusr). However, having servants, helpers, and actual mounts is not a condition by consensus. Consequently, these conditions are only for the initial obligation, not for its continuation. If a person becomes incapable of performing Hajj after it becomes obligatory, the obligation remains and must be performed later or by proxy if necessary. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr is obligated with the condition of capacity (qudrah), which is defined as sufficiency (ghina), not with the condition of ease (yusr). Evidence: It becomes obligatory even with basic clothing of need (thiyab al-balah) which do not provide financial ease because they are not productive (namiyah). Thus, the continuation of the obligation does not require the continuation of the condition of obligation. This illustrates a key usul principle: the conditions that make an act obligatory are not necessarily required for the act to remain obligatory once it is established.

Key Terms
ممکنة من السفر (mumkinah min al-safar): The ability to travel under normal circumstances; a condition for the obligation of Hajj.
یسر (yusr): Financial ease; having surplus wealth beyond basic needs.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The charity given at the end of Ramadan; obligatory on the condition of ghina (sufficiency).
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition for the initial obligation of an act; its presence triggers the obligation, but its later absence does not remove the obligation.
شرط الدوام (shart al-dawam): A condition required for the continuance of an obligation; Hanafi holds that for acts like Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr, no such condition exists for the obligations themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the condition of having a riding mount and provisions (raahilah wa zad) not a condition for the continuation of the obligation of Hajj?
A) Because it is impossible to always have a mount.
B) Because it is a condition for the initial obligation only, as established by consensus.
C) Because one can perform Hajj on foot.
D) Because it is only a recommended condition.

Key Takeaway
The condition for the initial obligation (shart al-wujub) does not need to persist for the obligation to remain (shart al-dawam), as illustrated by Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Specific vs Non-Specific Wealth: Zakat and Kaffarah
Explains the usul distinction between mu'ayyan and ghayr mu'ayyan wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between specific (mu'ayyan) and non-specific (ghayr mu'ayyan) wealth in Hanafi usul and apply this distinction to explain why zakat and kaffarah differ when wealth is destroyed.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, zakat attaches to specific wealth; destruction drops it. Kaffarah attaches to any wealth; destruction only suspends it.

This lesson explores a subtle but crucial distinction in Hanafi usul: the difference between specific wealth (maal mu'ayyan) and non-specific wealth (maal ghayr mu'ayyan). This distinction determines whether an obligation revives after new wealth is acquired following the destruction of the original wealth. The text uses zakat and monetary kaffarah (expiation for breaking an oath) as contrasting examples to illustrate the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of wealth
Recognize that 'maal mu'ayyan' refers to a specific, identifiable asset (e.g., a particular herd of camels or a specific sum of money), while 'maal ghayr mu'ayyan' refers to wealth in a general sense, not tied to a particular asset.
In zakat, the obligation is tied to the specific nisab wealth; in kaffarah, it is tied to the person's ability to pay from any wealth.
2
Understand the attachment of obligation
In zakat, the obligation (wujub) is attached directly to the specific wealth. In kaffarah, the obligation is attached to the person's financial capability (qudrat muyassara), not to any particular asset.
This difference explains why destruction of the specific wealth in zakat drops the obligation permanently, while in kaffarah, obligation can return with new wealth.
3
Analyze the effect of destruction (halak) vs causing destruction (ihlak)
For zakat: accidental destruction drops the obligation; intentional destruction does not drop the obligation because it is a transgression against the rights of the poor. For kaffarah: both accidental and intentional destruction drop the obligation and it reverts to fasting, because no third-party right is involved.
The key is whether the wealth is occupied with someone else's right (haqq al-ghayr). In zakat, the poor have a right in that specific wealth; in kaffarah, no one has a right until the obligation is fulfilled.
4
Apply the distinction to scenarios
Given a scenario, determine whether wealth is mu'ayyan or ghayr mu'ayyan, then predict the ruling when wealth is lost or destroyed. Example: Zakat on a specific herd vs. kaffarah for an oath.
Practice applying the rule: if the wealth is specific, destruction normally drops the obligation (unless intentional, then obligation remains as liability). If non-specific, destruction drops the obligation and it can be revived with new wealth.

کر نہیں آنا چاہیے جیسے زکوۃ میں وجوب لوٹ کر نہیں آتا، اگر زکوۃ کا مال ہلاک ہو گیا پھر بعد میں اس کے پاس مال آیا تو اس پر سابق زکوۃ نہ واجب ہوگی، بلکہ اس مال پر جب سال گزرے گا تو زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، حالانکہ آپ کہتے ہیں کہ حانث کے پاس جب دوسرا امال آجائے گا تو دوبارہ کفارہ مالی واجب ہوگا تو کفارہ مالی زکوۃ کے قبیل سے کہاں ہوا؟ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ کفارہ مالی زکوۃ کے قبیل سے ہے، قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ واجب ہونے میں البتہ دونوں میں تھوڑا فرق ہے، وہ یہ کہ زکوۃ میں مال معین ہوتا ہے، اور جب یہ مال ہلاک ہو گیا تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی ، اور دوسرا مال جب اس کے پاس آگیا تو یہ اس کے قائم مقام نہیں ہوگا، لہذا جب اس دوسرے مال پر سال گذرے گا تو زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، وہ پہلا واجب تو ساقط ہی ہو گیا، اور کفارہ مالی میں معین مال کے ساتھ کفار متعلق نہیں ہوتا ہے بلکہ مطلق مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے، لہذا جب دوسرا مال آجائے گا تو قدرت ثابت ہو جائے گی لہذا دوبارہ کفارہ مالی واجب ہوگا۔ اسی فرق کی وجہ سے کہ کفارہ مالی میں مال غیر معین ہوتا ہے مال کا ہلاک ہونا اور ہلاک کرنا دونوں برابر ہیں یعنی جس طرح مال کے ہلاک ہونے سے کفارہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور کفارہ کا حکم روزہ کی طرف لوٹ جاتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی مال کے ہلاک کرنے سے بھی کفارہ ساقط اور حکم روزے کی طرف لوٹ جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ زکوۃ میں ایسا نہیں ہے، زکوۃ میں مال ہلاک ہونے سے تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے مگر ہلاک کرنے سے زکوۃ ساقط نہیں ہوتی بلکہ زجر او جوب باقی رہتا ہے، کیونکہ زکوۃ میں مال معین ہوتا ہے تو اس کو ہلاک کرنا ایسے محل پر تعدی اور زیادتی کرنا ہے جو حل دوسرے کے یعنی فقیر کے حق کے ساتھ مشغول ہے، گویا اس نے ہلاک کر کے فقیر پر ظلم و تعدی کی ، اور کفارہ میں ایسے محل پر تعدی نہیں ہے جو دوسرے کے حق کے ساتھ مشغول ہو، کیونکہ اس میں مال غیر معین ہوتا ہے، کسی غیر کے حق کے ساتھ مشغول ہے ہی نہیں ، لہذا کفارہ میں ہلاک داستہلاک دونوں کا حکم یکساں ہے۔
Should not return like in zakat, obligation does not come back. If zakat wealth is destroyed, then later wealth comes to him, the previous zakat is not obligatory, rather zakat will be obligatory when a year passes on this wealth, even though you say that when another wealth comes to the oath-breaker, then monetary expiation becomes obligatory again. So how is monetary expiation from the genus of zakat? They are answering that monetary expiation is from the genus of zakat, with power of ease in being obligatory. However, there is a slight difference between the two: in zakat, wealth is specific (mu'ayyan), and when this wealth is destroyed, zakat is dropped, and when another wealth comes to him, it does not take its place. Therefore, when a year passes on this other wealth, zakat will be obligatory; the first obligation is already dropped. In monetary expiation, the expiation is not attached to specific wealth but to absolute wealth. Hence, when another wealth comes, power is established, so monetary expiation becomes obligatory again. Due to this difference that in monetary expiation wealth is non-specific (ghayr mu'ayyan), destruction of wealth and causing destruction are equal. That is, just as by the destruction of wealth the expiation is dropped and the ruling of expiation reverts to fasting, similarly by causing destruction of wealth, the expiation is dropped and the ruling reverts to fasting. While in zakat it is not so. In zakat, by destruction of wealth, zakat is dropped, but by causing destruction, zakat is not dropped; rather, the obligation remains as punishment, because in zakat wealth is specific, so destroying it is transgression and excess upon a locus that is occupied with the right of another, i.e., the poor. It is as if he oppressed and transgressed against the poor by destroying it. In expiation, there is no transgression upon a locus occupied with the right of another, because in it wealth is non-specific, it is not occupied with anyone's right. Therefore, in expiation, both destruction and causing destruction have the same ruling.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that explains a key distinction between zakat and monetary kaffarah (expiation). The issue arises from a potential objection: if zakat obligation returns when new wealth is acquired after loss, why doesn't the same apply to kaffarah for an oath? The commentator clarifies that both belong to the genus of obligations requiring power of ease, but they differ in the nature of wealth. In zakat, wealth is specific (mu'ayyan) to a particular asset; once that asset is destroyed, the obligation is dropped permanently, and new wealth starts a new cycle. In kaffarah, wealth is non-specific (ghayr mu'ayyan); the obligation is attached to any wealth the person possesses. Thus, if the wealth is destroyed (or he destroys it), the obligation falls, but when new wealth comes, the obligation revives because the condition of power is re-established. The commentator further explains that destrying zakat wealth is a transgression against the poor's right, so the obligation remains as liability, whereas in kaffarah, no one else's right is involved, so destruction (whether by accident or intentionally) has the same effect: the obligation reverts to fasting. This distinction is crucial for understanding how obligation relates to specific property rights.

Key Terms
مال معین (maal mu'ayyan): Wealth that is specific and identified, such that the obligation is attached to that particular asset.
مال غیر معین (maal ghayr mu'ayyan): Wealth that is not specific; the obligation is attached to the person's wealth in general, not to a particular asset.
قدرت میسرہ (qudrat muyassara): Power of ease: having wealth that is surplus and growing, beyond basic needs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the key reason that monetary kaffarah can become obligatory again after the loss of wealth, whereas zakat cannot?
A) Because kaffarah is a type of worship, while zakat is a financial right.
B) Because in kaffarah, wealth is non-specific (ghayr mu'ayyan), so the obligation revives with new wealth; in zakat, wealth is specific, so the obligation drops permanently.
C) Because kaffarah is more severe than zakat.
D) Because the poor have no right in kaffarah, but they have a right in zakat.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the distinction between specific and non-specific wealth determines whether an obligation is permanently dropped or can revive with new wealth, affecting rulings across various financial obligations.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
