Power of Possibility vs Power of Ease in Hajj and Fitr
Explains qudra mumkina vs muyassara with ijma proof and cross-madhhab dispute on fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qudra mumkina and qudra muyassara and apply the Hanafi rule that hajj and fitr require qudra mumkina based on ijma.

Core Idea
Hajj and fitr require minimal ability, not productive wealth.

In this passage from Al-Husami, we explore a key usul distinction: the type of power (qudra) that conditions obligations like hajj and sadaqat al-fitr. The Hanafi school insists on 'possible power' (qudra mumkina) rather than 'power of ease' (qudra muyassara). Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines when obligations become binding and whether they persist after wealth is lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of power
Locate the terms qudra mumkina and qudra muyassara in the text. Qudra mumkina refers to minimal ability (e.g., mount and provisions for hajj; owning nisab for fitr). Qudra muyassara refers to having servants, helpers, or productive wealth.
The Arabic words are 'الممكنة' and 'اليسر'.
2
Find the ijma proof
The text states that requiring ease (servants etc.) is not a condition by consensus (وَلَيْسَ ذَلِكَ بِشَرْطِ بِالْإِجْمَاع). This ijma is a qat'i proof that only qudra mumkina is required for hajj.
Ijma is cited to settle the matter definitively.
3
Understand the implication for continuity
Because the condition is minimal, it does not need to persist. Once hajj becomes wajib, if wealth is lost, the obligation remains; the person sins if they do not perform it.
This contradicts the idea that the condition must continue.
4
Apply to sadaqat al-fitr
Similarly, fitr is obligated with qudra mumkina: owning nisab (ghina), even if the wealth is not productive (e.g., thiyab al-balla). The purpose is to make the poor rich (ighna'), so the giver must be wealthy enough to give without becoming needy.
Note the contrast with zakat, which requires productive wealth and annual cycle.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The text addresses an objection: if ghina (nisab) is the condition, that seems like qudra muyassara. The Hanafi response (though cut off) argues that nisab is a minimal threshold, unlike the Shafi'i condition of one day's surplus, which would lead to inconsistency.
This shows how usul principles shape concrete rulings.

ترجمہ: اور بہر حال حج پس اس میں قدرت ممکنہ شرط ہے یعنی وہ سفر جس کے لوگ عادی ہیں سواری اور توشہ کے ساتھ ، اور میسر واقع نہیں ہوتا ہے مگر بہت سے خادموں کے ساتھ اور بہت سے مددگاروں اور سواریوں کے ساتھ ، اور یہ بالا جماع شرط نہیں ہے، پس اسی وجہ سے یہ ( قدرت ممکنہ ) دوام واجب کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے، اور اسی طرح صدقہ فطر یسر کی صفت کے ساتھ واجب نہیں ہوا بلکہ قدرت (ممکنہ) کی شرط کے ساتھ اور وہ غنا (مالداری) ساتھ واجب ہے، یعنی ادنی قدرت حاصل ہو جائے ، سواری اور توشہ پر قدرت سے حج واجب ہو جائے گا، یہ قدرت ممکنہ ہے، ورنہ یسر تو اس میں یہ ہے کہ ساتھ میں خدام ہوں، مددگار ہوں ،سواریاں ہوں وغیرہ حالانکہ بالا گذرنا شرط نہیں، یہ قدرت ممکنہ ہے، جس سے ادنی قدرت حاصل ہو جاتی ہے ورنہ میسر تو اس میں مالِ نامی اور حولان حول سے ہوتا ہے، حالانکہ یہ شرط نہیں ہے، اگر کوئی عید کی رات میں صبح صادق سے پہلے نصاب کا مالک ہو گیا تو صدقہ فطر واجب ہو جائے گا۔ اور غنا کی شرط اس لئے لگائی گئی کہ صدقہ قطر کا مقصود فقیر کوئی کرنا ہے، اس کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ خود غنی ہو، لہذا غنا کی شرط لگادی۔ اگر کوئی سوال کرے کہ غنا ( یعنی ہو گیا اب وہ خالی ہاتھ ہو گیا ، دوسرے دن محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے مانگنے پر
As for hajj, the condition in it is the possible power (al-mumkina) from the customary journey with a mount and provisions. Ease (al-yusr) does not occur except with servants, helpers, and mounts, and that is not a condition by consensus. Therefore, it is not a condition for the continuity of the obligation. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr was not obligated with the attribute of ease, but with the condition of power, and it is wealth (al-ghina), so that the one described with it becomes fit for enriching (al-ighna'). Do you not see that it becomes obligatory with working clothes (thiyab al-balla), while ease does not occur through them, because they are not productive (namiya). Thus, the continuity is not in need of the continuance of the condition of obligation.
Translation: And as for hajj, the condition in it is possible power, meaning the journey people are accustomed to with mount and provisions. And ease does not occur except with many servants, many helpers, and many mounts, and this is not a condition by consensus. Hence, this (possible power) is not a condition for the continuity of the obligation. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr was not obligated with the attribute of ease but with the condition of power, and it is wealth, so that the person described with wealth becomes fit for enriching. Do you not see that sadaqat al-fitr becomes obligatory with working clothes, although ease does not occur through them, because working clothes are not productive? So the continuity of the obligation is not in need of the continuance of the condition of obligation.
Explanation: The author is further clarifying the difference between possible power and power of ease. He says that hajj is obligatory with possible power, i.e., minimal power is attained; power over mount and provisions makes hajj obligatory. This is possible power. Otherwise, ease in it is having servants, helpers, mounts etc., yet by consensus this is not a condition. It is understood that the obligation of hajj is not by power of ease but by possible power. Therefore, the continuance of power is not a condition for the continuation of the obligation. Hence, if after hajj becomes obligatory, the wealth is destroyed, hajj is not dropped, and if he cannot do it, he will be sinful. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr is also not by power of ease but by possible power. Therefore, in it, wealth (ghina) i.e., being wealthy and being owner of nisab is a condition; having productive wealth and passing of a year are not conditions. This is possible power by which minimal power is attained. Otherwise, ease in it is from productive wealth and passing of a year, yet these are not conditions. If someone becomes owner of nisab on the night of Eid before true dawn, sadaqat al-fitr will be obligatory. And the condition of wealth was placed because the purpose of sadaqat al-fitr is to enrich the poor; for that, it is necessary that he himself be wealthy, so the condition of wealth was placed. If someone asks: when wealth (i.e., being owner of nisab) is made a condition, this is power of ease, because possible power is being owner of more than one day's sustenance. If possible power is the condition in sadaqat al-fitr, then it should be obligatory on having more than one day's sustenance, and the condition of nisab should not be there, as is the ruling according to Imam Shafi'i. The answer is that if one means more than one day's sustenance, then inversion of the subject matter would occur: today it became obligatory on more than one day's sustenance, now he becomes empty-handed, then on the second day due to being needy, he will beg...
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the distinction between qudra mumkina (possible power) and qudra muyassara (power of ease) in the context of hajj and sadaqat al-fitr. The author (Al-Husami) states that the condition for hajj is possible power, i.e., having the means for a customary journey with mount and provisions. Ease (like having servants) is not required by consensus. Therefore, the obligation does not require the condition to persist; once hajj becomes wajib, if the wealth is lost, the obligation remains and the person sins if he doesn't perform it. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr is obligated with possible power, not ease. The condition is being wealthy (ghina) i.e., owning nisab, not necessarily having productive wealth or annual cycle. For example, it is obligatory with working clothes (thiyab al-balla) even though they are not productive, because they indicate a level of wealth sufficient for the purpose of enriching the poor. The commentator then addresses an objection: if the condition is ghina (nisab), that seems to be power of ease, not possible power. The answer (cut off) likely explains that nisab is a minimal standard of wealth that still qualifies as possible power, and that requiring only one day's surplus would lead to inconsistency where a person becomes needy the next day. The textual reference to Imam Shafi'i shows the madhhab difference: Shafi'is consider sadaqat al-fitr obligatory on anyone with more than one day's food, while Hanafis require nisab ownership.

Key Terms
قدرة ممكنة (qudra mumkina): Possible power: the minimum ability to perform an obligation, such as having the means for travel in hajj or owning nisab for fitr.
قدرة ميسرة (qudra muyassara): Power of ease: having surplus wealth that is productive (growth) and beyond basic needs.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan on behalf of each person, based on being owner of nisab.
ثياب البلة (thiyab al-balla): Working clothes or everyday clothes that are not productive but indicate a level of wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens to the obligation of hajj if after it becomes wajib, the person's wealth is destroyed?
A) The obligation is dropped.
B) The obligation remains; he is sinful if he does not perform it.
C) The obligation is transferred to another year.
D) He must perform it only if wealth returns.

Key Takeaway
Qudra mumkina suffices for hajj and fitr; once the obligation is established, it does not require the condition to persist.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced

Power Possible vs Power Facilitated in Obligation
Expansion on power types in obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define power possible (qudrat mumkinah) and power facilitated (qudrat maysarah), apply the Hanafi rule that only power possible is required for Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr, and explain the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i position on the condition for Sadaqat al-Fitr.

Core Idea
Obligation requires only minimal power; extra ease is not a condition and the obligation persists even if means vanish.

This passage from Al-Husami commentary clarifies a critical usul principle: for obligations like Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr, the shari'ah only demands 'power possible'—the minimal means to perform the act. 'Power facilitated,' involving luxury such as servants or productive wealth, is not required. This distinction has practical consequences: if means are lost after the obligation becomes due, the obligation does not lapse. The passage also addresses an objection from Imam al-Shafi'i regarding Sadaqat al-Fitr and defends the Hanafi condition of nisab (ghina) over mere daily provision.

Guided Path
1
Define the two terms
Identify 'qudrat mumkinah' (power possible) as minimal means (e.g., mount and provision for Hajj) and 'qudrat maysarah' (power facilitated) as ease with extra resources. Note that ijma excludes the latter as a condition.
Legal definition dissector in the toolbox helps formalise these.
2
Apply to Hajj
See how the rule is applied: Hajj becomes obligatory with minimal mount and provision. If wealth is lost after obligation, the obligation remains (the person is sinful if unable).
This shows the rule's effect on continuity of obligation.
3
Apply to Sadaqat al-Fitr
Observe that the condition is also power possible, defined as ghina (ownership of nisab), not mere daily provision. The text uses analogy (qiyas) with Hajj and rational argument to justify the nisab condition.
The objection from Shafi'i and the Hanafi response are key.
4
Distil the usul rule
Formulate the principle: For any obligation, the condition is only the ability to perform the essential act; the presence of ease or luxury is not required, and the loss of means after obligation does not cancel the duty.
This is a general usul rule derived from the passage.
5
Analyse the Shafi'i dispute
Study the madhhab dispute map: Hanafi requires nisab; Shafi'i requires only one day's provision. Follow the Hanafi rebuttal based on the consequence of the giver becoming needy (qabih).
The thamarah al-khilaf is that a person with one day's provision must pay fitr according to Shafi'i but not according to Hanafi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال حج پس اس میں قدرت ممکنہ شرط ہے یعنی وہ سفر جس کے لوگ عادی ہیں سواری اور توشہ کے ساتھ ، اور میسر واقع نہیں ہوتا ہے مگر بہت سے خادموں کے ساتھ اور بہت سے مددگاروں اور سواریوں کے ساتھ ، اور یہ بالاجماع شرط نہیں ہے، پس اسی وجہ سے یہ ( قدرت ممکنہ ) دوام واجب کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے، اور اسی طرح صدقہ فطر یسر کی صفت کے ساتھ واجب نہیں ہوا بلکہ قدرت (ممکنہ) کی شرط کے ساتھ اور وہ غنا (مالداری) ہے ،تا کہ ہو جائے وہ شخص جو غنا کے ساتھ موصوف ہے غنی کرنے کا اہل کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ صدقہ فطر واجب ہو جاتا ہے کام کاج کے کپڑوں سے، حالانکہ ان کے ذریعہ یسر واقع نہیں ہوتا ہے، اس لئے کہ کام کاج کے کپڑے نامی نہیں ہیں، پس نہیں ہو گا بقاءِ واجب محتاج ، وجوب کی شرط کے دوام کی طرف۔ شریح : ۔ مصنف ع الله قدرت ممکنہ اور قدرت میسرہ کے درمیان فرق کو مزید واضح کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ حج قدرت ممکنہ کے ساتھ واجب ہے، یعنی ادنی قدرت حاصل ہو جائے ، سواری اور توشہ پر قدرت سے حج واجب ہو جائے گا، یہ قدرت ممکنہ ہے، ورنہ یسر تو اس میں یہ ہے کہ ساتھ میں خدام ہوں، مددگار ہوں ،سواریاں ہوں وغیرہ حالانکہ بالاجماع یہ شرط نہیں ہے، معلوم ہوا کہ قدرت میسرہ سے حج کا وجوب نہیں ہے، بلکہ ممکنہ سے ہے، اسی لئے بقاء واجب کے لئے قدرت کا دوام شرط نہیں ہے، لہذا حج واجب ہو جانے کے بعد مال ہلاک ہو گیا تو حج ساقط نہ ہوگا ، اور نہ کر سکا تو گنہگار ہوگا۔ اسی طرح صدقۂ فطر بھی قدرت میسرہ کے ساتھ نہیں ہے، بلکہ قدرت ممکنہ کے ساتھ واجب ہے، اسی لئے اس میں غنا یعنی مالدار ہونا ، اور صاحب نصاب ہونا شرط ہے، مال نامی ہونا اور سال گذرنا شرط نہیں، یہ قدرت ممکنہ ہے، جس سے ادنی قدرت حاصل ہو جاتی ہے ورنہ میسر تو اس میں مالِ نامی اور حولان حول سے ہوتا ہے، حالانکہ یہ شرط نہیں ہے، اگر کوئی عید کی رات میں صبح صادق سے پہلے نصاب کا مالک ہو گیا تو صدقہ فطر واجب ہو جائے گا۔ اور غنا کی شرط اس لئے لگائی گئی کہ صدقہ فطر کا مقصود فقیر کوئی کرنا ہے، اس کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ خود غنی ہو، لہذا غنا کی شرط لگادی۔ اگر کوئی سوال کرے کہ غنا ( یعنی نصاب کا مالک ہونا ) جب شرط قرار دیا تو یہ قدرت میسرہ ہوئی اس لئے کہ قدرت ممکنہ تو یہ ہے کہ ایک دن سے زائد روزی کا مالک ہو، اگر صدقہ فطر میں قدرت ممکنہ شرط ہے تو ایک دن سے زائد روزی پر صدقہ فطر ہونا چاہیے، نصاب کی شرط نہ ہونا چاہیے ، جیسے امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ایک دن سے زائد روزی مراد لینے کی صورت میں قلب موضوع لازم آتا ہے، کہ آج تو ایک دن سے زائد روزی پر صدقہ واجب ہو گیا اب وہ خالی ہاتھ ہو گیا ، دوسرے دن محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے مانگنے پر مجبور ہوگا، کل اس فقیر سے وہ صدقہ کا سوال کرے گا اور یہ قبیح چیز ہے، کیونکہ اپنی حاجت کو دفع کرنا غیر کی حاجت دفع کرنے سے اولی ہے، لہذا غنا شرط قرار دیا تا کہ یہ محتاج نہ بنے۔ بہر حال صدقۂ فطر قدرت ممکنہ کے ساتھ واجب ہے، اسی لئے اگر کسی کے پاس استعمال کے کپڑے حاجت اصلیہ سے زائد ہوں، اس پر بھی صدقہ فطر واجب ہوتا ہے، حالانکہ کام کاج کے کپڑوں پر وجوب کو [؟] کیونکہ یہ نامی نہیں ہیں، معلوم ہوا کہ صدقہ فطر قدرت میسرہ سے نہیں بلکہ قدرت ممکنہ کے ساتھ واجب ہے، پس بقاء واجب کے لئے قدرت کا دوام شرط نہیں ہے لہذا عید کے دن مال ہلاک ہو گیا تو صدقۂ فطر ساقط نہ ہوگا۔
Translation: And in any case, Hajj has as a condition power possible, meaning the journey that people are accustomed to with mount and provision, and it is not facilitated except with many servants and many helpers and mounts, and this is by consensus not a condition. Therefore, for this reason, this (power possible) is not a condition for the continuation of the obligation. Similarly, Sadaqat al-Fitr is not obligatory with the attribute of ease but with the condition of power possible, and that is wealth (ghina), so that the person who is described with wealth becomes capable of enriching. Do you not see that Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory from clothes of profession, even though ease is not achieved through them? Because clothes of profession are not productive. So there will not be need of continuation of the obligation toward the continuation of the condition of obligation. Sharh: The author clarifies the difference between power possible and power facilitated. He says: Hajj is obligatory with power possible, meaning the minimal power is obtained. With power over mount and provision, Hajj becomes obligatory. This is power possible. Otherwise, ease in it includes having servants, helpers, mounts, etc., but by consensus this is not a condition. It is known that Hajj's obligation is not by power facilitated but by power possible. Therefore, continuity of power is not a condition for the continuation of the obligation. So if after Hajj becomes obligatory, wealth perishes, Hajj does not lapse, and if he cannot do it, he is sinful. Similarly, Sadaqat al-Fitr is not by power facilitated but by power possible. Therefore, in it, wealth (being wealthy) and being owner of nisab are conditions; having productive wealth and passage of a year are not conditions. This is power possible, by which minimal power is acquired. Otherwise, ease in it comes about from productive wealth and annual turnover, but these are not conditions. If someone on the night of Eid before true dawn becomes owner of nisab, Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory. The condition of ghina was placed because the purpose of Sadaqat al-Fitr is to enrich the poor; for that, it is necessary that he himself be wealthy, so the condition of ghina was placed. If someone asks: When ghina (ownership of nisab) is made a condition, that is power facilitated, because power possible is that one owns provision for more than a day. If Sadaqat al-Fitr requires power possible, then it should be obligatory on one who has provision for more than a day, and the condition of nisab should not be required, as is the ruling according to Imam Shafi'i. The answer is that if we mean provision for more than a day, it would necessitate inversion of the subject: today he becomes obliged on the basis of having more than a day's provision, then he becomes empty-handed, and on the second day due to need, he is forced to beg; he would then ask that poor person for charity, and that is a bad thing because repelling one's own need is more virtuous than repelling another's need. Therefore, ghina was made a condition so that he does not become needy. In any case, Sadaqat al-Fitr is obligatory with power possible. For this reason, if someone has clothes of use beyond basic need, Sadaqat al-Fitr is also obligatory on that, even though the obligation on clothes of profession is [؟] because they are not productive. It is known that Sadaqat al-Fitr is not by power facilitated but by power possible. So for the continuation of the obligation, continuity of power is not a condition. Therefore, if wealth perishes on the day of Eid, Sadaqat al-Fitr does not lapse.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rule that for the obligation of Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr, only 'power possible' (qudrat mumkinah) is required, not 'power facilitated' (qudrat maysarah). The author explains that power possible means having the minimal means for the act, such as mount and provision for Hajj, or owning the nisab for Sadaqat al-Fitr. Power facilitated, on the other hand, would involve luxury such as servants and multiple mounts, which is not required by consensus. The absence of a requirement for ease means that if the means are lost after the obligation is established, the obligation does not lapse; the person remains obliged and sinful if they fail to perform. The passage then addresses a potential objection: If Sadaqat al-Fitr requires only power possible (which could be provision for one day), why is ownership of nisab (a full year's savings) required? The answer is that using a one-day provision would lead to the person becoming needy themselves the next day, which contradicts the purpose of enriching the poor. Therefore, the condition of nisab ensures the giver remains self-sufficient. The passage concludes by affirming that power possible is sufficient, and any surplus beyond basic needs triggers the obligation, even if the items are not productive capital.

Key Terms
قدرت ممکنہ (qudrat mumkinah): Minimal power or capacity to perform an act, i.e., having the essential means without extra ease.
قدرت میسرہ (qudrat maysarah): Power that includes additional ease, such as servants, multiple mounts, or productive wealth.
غنا (ghina): Wealth that makes one not in need, specifically ownership of nisab beyond basic needs.
قلب موضوع (qalb mawdu'): Inversion of the subject; here, the scenario where the payer becomes the one needing charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if wealth is destroyed after Hajj becomes obligatory?
A) The obligation lapses because the person no longer has the means.
B) The obligation remains; the person is sinful if unable to perform it.
C) The person is excused and need not make up the Hajj.
D) The obligation is postponed until wealth is regained.

Key Takeaway
Power possible (qudrat mumkinah) is the only condition for obligation; once established, loss of means does not cancel the duty.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Categories of Goodness: Inherent vs. Acquired
Defines the two types of husn for al-ma'mur bih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any commanded act as good due to inherent meaning or due to external meaning, and identify the underlying meaning that makes it good.

Core Idea
Goodness of an act is either inherent (like ta'zim in salah) or acquired through a means (like zakah via the poor's need).

What makes a commanded act good? The Lawgiver commands acts because they embody some goodness. In this passage, the Hanafi usul tradition distinguishes between acts that are inherently good due to their very nature, and acts that become good because they serve a good purpose outside themselves. Grasping this distinction is key to understanding why acts like salah are always good (unless time/state is off) while acts like zakah derive their goodness from the benefit they bring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary categories
Find the two main types of husn: good due to a meaning in itself, and good due to a meaning in something else.
The text explicitly states 'al-ma'muru bihi naw'ani: hasanun li-ma'na fi 'aynihi, wa hasanun li-ma'na fi ghayrihi'.
2
Analyze the first category: inherent goodness
Inherent goodness is subdivided into: (a) where the meaning is in its very constitution (like salah, because its actions and words are for ta'zim), and (b) annexed through a means (like zakah, fasting, hajj). Notice that the first subcategory is directly good; the second is good because it incorporates good means.
Salah is good due to ta'zim which is intrinsically good. But even salah can become blameworthy at improper times.
3
Examine the annexed goodness
Acts like zakah become good because they involve enriching the poor, subduing the enemy, and glorifying rites. These means are created by Allah, so the act is good without needing a third meaning.
The means are 'close to the essence,' almost inseparable, so the act is still classified under inherent goodness, but as an annexed type.
4
Apply the classification to examples
Given a new commanded act (e.g., reciting the Quran, charity, pilgrimage), determine which category it falls into and why.
Consider: the act of reciting Quran has inherent goodness because its words are praise (ta'zim). Charity has annexed goodness because it helps the poor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي صِفَةِ الْحُسْنِ لِلْمَأْمُورِ بِهِ . اَلْمَأْمُورُ بِهِ نَوْعَانِ: حَسَنٌ لِمَعْنًى فِي عَيْنِهِ، وَحَسَنٌ لِمَعْنًى فِي غَيْرِهِ. وَالَّذِي حَسَنٌ لِمَعْنًى فِي عَيْنِهِ نَوْعَانِ: مَا كَانَ الْمَعْنَى فِي وَضْعِهِ، كَالصَّلَاةِ فَإِنَّهَا تُؤَدَّى بِأَفْعَالٍ وَأَقْوَالٍ وُضِعَتْ لِلتَّعْظِيمِ، وَالتَّعْظِيمُ حَسَنٌ فِي نَفْسِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي غَيْرِ حِينِهِ أَوْ حَالِهِ، وَمَا الْتَحَقَ بِوَاسِطَةٍ بِمَا كَانَ الْمَعْنَى فِي وَضْعِهِ، كَالزَّكَاةِ وَالصَّوْمِ وَالْحَجِّ، فَإِنَّ هَذِهِ الْأَفْعَالَ بِوَاسِطَةِ حَاجَةِ الْفَقِيرِ وَاشْتِهَاءِ النَّفْسِ وَشَرَفِ الْمَكَانِ تَضَمَّنَتْ إِغْنَاءَ عِبَادِ اللَّهِ وَقَهْرَ عَدُوِّهِ وَتَعْظِيمَ شَعَائِرِهِ، فَصَارَتْ حَسَنَةً مِنَ الْعَبْدِ لِلرَّبِّ عَزَّتْ قُدْرَتُهُ بِلَا ثَالِثِ مَعْنًى، لِكَوْنِ هَذِهِ الْوَسَائِطِ ثَابِتَةً بِخَلْقِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَمُضَافَةً إِلَيْهِ.
A section on the description of the goodness of the commanded act. The commanded act is of two types: good due to a meaning inherent in itself, and good due to a meaning in other than itself. That which is good due to a meaning inherent in itself is of two types: that in which the meaning is in its very constitution, like prayer, for it is performed with actions and words placed for glorification, and glorification is good in itself unless it occurs at an improper time or state; and that which is annexed through a means to that in which the meaning is in its very constitution, like zakah, fasting, and hajj, for these actions, through the means of the need of the poor, the desire of the soul, and the honor of the place, encompass enriching the servants of Allah, subduing His enemy, and glorifying His rites, so they become good from the servant towards the Lord, may His power be exalted, without a third meaning, because these means are established by Allah's creation and attributed to Him.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is an usul definition explaining the types of goodness (husn) in commanded acts (ma'mur bih). The author—following the Hanafi usul tradition—first divides the ma'mur bih into two primary categories: hasan li-ma'na fi 'aynihi (good due to a meaning in its own essence) and hasan li-ma'na fi ghayrihi (good due to a meaning outside itself). The former is then subdivided into two types: (1) that in which the meaning is embedded in its very constitution, such as salah, because its actions and words are inherently meant for glorification (ta'zim), and glorification is intrinsically good; (2) that which is attached to the first category via an intermediate means, such as zakah, sawm, and hajj. These actions become good because they incorporate external purposes (enriching the poor, subduing the enemy, glorifying rites) that are themselves good by divine creation. The commentary elaborates that this second type is annexed to the first because the means are close to the essence, almost inseparable. The passage also notes that even intrinsically good acts like salah can become blameworthy if performed at the wrong time (e.g., disliked times) or state (e.g., without purity). This categorization is foundational for understanding how acts derive their moral and legal value in Hanafi usul, distinguishing between acts good in themselves (like faith, which never falls) and those good due to external factors.

Key Terms
المأمور به (al-ma'mur bihi): The act commanded by the Lawgiver (Allah)
حسن لمعنى في عينه (hasan li-ma'na fi 'aynihi): Good due to a meaning inherent in its own essence
تعظيم (ta'zim): Glorification or magnifying of Allah, the intrinsic meaning that makes salah good in itself

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of an act that is 'good due to a meaning inherent in itself' (first subcategory)?
A) Zakah
B) Fasting
C) Salah
D) Hajj

Key Takeaway
The goodness of a commanded act is either inherent (because of its very purpose like ta'zim) or annexed through a good means, but both are types of inherent goodness in Hanafi usul.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Types of Goodness in Commanded Acts
Classification of commanded acts by goodness essence vs. external

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a commanded act as ḥasan li-ʿaynihi or ḥasan li-ghayrihi and identify its subtype and ruling.

Core Idea
Goodness in a commanded act is either intrinsic to its essence or derived from an external purpose, determining how its obligation stands.

This lesson examines how Hanafi usul classifies commanded acts based on the nature of their goodness (ḥusn). The author explains that every act Allah commands must have goodness, but that goodness may be intrinsic or come from an external purpose. Understanding this distinction is essential for deriving rulings on obligation and invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two primary categories
Identify whether the commanded act's goodness is in its own essence (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi) or due to something external (ḥasan li-ghayrihi).
If the act is good in itself, proceed to step 2; otherwise skip to step 3.
2
Subdivide ḥasan li-ʿaynihi
Determine if the intrinsic goodness is by essence (bi al-dhāt, e.g., salat) or through an intermediary so close that it is considered intrinsic (bi al-wāsiṭa, e.g., zakat, fasting, hajj).
The intermediary must be created by Allah and essentially non-existent in the analysis.
3
Subdivide ḥasan li-ghayrihi
Decide whether the good meaning is obtained after a purposeful action (type 1, e.g., wudu) or by the action itself (type 2, e.g., funeral prayer).
Type 1 acts are means to an end; type 2 acts directly fulfill the purpose.
4
Apply the respective ruling
For both subtypes of ḥasan li-ʿaynihi: obligation remains until performed or invalidated by a specific cause. For ḥasan li-ghayrihi: obligation is tied to the obligation of the external purpose; if the purpose falls, the act's obligation falls.
This ruling is a key difference between the two major categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
ہے۔ حسن بغیر کسی تیسرے معنی کے (یعنی بغیر کسی زائد واسطہ کے ) ان واسطوں کے ثابت ہونے کی وجہ سے اللہ تعالی کے خلق سے اور منسوب ہونے کی وجہ سے اللہ تعالی کی طرف۔
تشریح:- یہ فصل ہے مامور بہ کے حسن کی صفت کے بیان میں، آمر اللہ تعالی ہیں، اور نا ہی بھی اللہ تعالی ہیں، اور اللہ حکیم ہے، اس کی حکمت کا تقاضا ہے کہ وہ جس چیز کا بندوں کو امر کریں گے یقینا اس مامور بہ میں حسن ہوگا اور جس چیز سے نہی کریں گے اس منہی عنہ میں فتح ہوگا۔ مصنف الله مامور بہ کی حسن کے لحاظ سے تقسیم کر رہے ہیں، حسن کے لحاظ سے مامور بہ کی دوقسمیں ہیں، (۱) مامور به حسن لعینه (۲) مامور به حسن لغیرہ ،حسن لعینہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ حُسن مامور بہ کی ذات میں ہو ، حسن لغیرہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ مامور بہ میں حسن ذاتی نہ ہو غیر کی وجہ سے آیا ہو۔
پھر مامور بہ حسن لعینہ کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں، (۱) حسن لعینہ بالذات (۲) حسن لعینہ بالواسطہ۔ حسن لعینہ بالذات اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جس وصف اور معنی کی وجہ سے مامور بہ میں حسن پیدا ہوا ہے وہ وصف فی حد ذاتہ حسن ہو بغیر کسی واسطہ کے، اس کی وضع میں ہی حسن ہو۔
اور حسن لعینہ بالواسطہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جس وصف و معنی کی وجہ سے مامور بہ میں حسن پیدا ہوا ہے وہ معنی اپنی وضع میں حسن نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں حسن کسی واسطہ سے آیا ہے لیکن یہ واسطہ بھی کوئی بہت دور کی چیز نہیں ہے، بلکہ نہ ہونے کے درجہ میں ہے، اس لئے یہ قسم ثانی قسم اول کے ساتھ ہی ملحق ہے۔ قسم اول یعنی حسن لعینہ بالذات کی مثال جیسے نماز کیونکہ نماز میں جس معنی اور وصف کی وجہ سے حسن آیا ہے وہ معنی ایسا ہے کہ اس کی ذات و وضع میں ہی حسن ہے، اس لئے کہ نماز اقوال یعنی شنا تسبیح وغیرہ اور افعال یعنی رکوع ، سجدہ وغیرہ کا نام ہے، تو نماز میں ان افعال و اقوال سے حسن آیا ہے اور یہ افعال و اقوال ایسے ہیں کہ ان کی وضع میں حسن ہیں کیونکہ ان کا مقصد تعظیم باری تعالی ہے، اور تعظیم فی ذاتہ حسن ہے، لہذا نماز حسن لعینہ بالذات ہوئی، اسی قسم اول میں ایمان بھی داخل ہے، بلکہ ایمان تو قسم اول کا اعلی درجہ ہے، کیونکہ ایمان تو کسی بھی وقت سقوط کو قبول نہیں کرتا ہے، اور نماز تو بعض اوقات ساقط بھی ہو جاتی ہے، اسی لئے بعض حضرات نے اس قسم اول کی تقسیم کی ہے (۱) مالا یقبل السقوط مثل الايمان (۲) ما يقبل السقوط مثل الصلوة الاان يكون : - تعظيم فی ذاتہ حسن ہے مگر یہ کہ غیر حالت میں یا غیر وقت میں ہو، جیسے بجائے طہارت کے حالت جنابت میں ہو یا غیر وقت میں ہو جیسے اوقات مکروہ میں ہو تو حسن نہ ہوگی بلکہ قبیح اور مکروہ ہوگی۔ وما التحق بوابسطة : قسم اول بیان ہو گئی قسم ثانی وہ ہے جو واسطہ کی وجہ سے قسم اول کے ساتھ ملحق ہے، جیسے زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج ، زکوۃ میں بظاہر کوئی حسن نہیں ہے کیونکہ زکوۃ میں مال کو ضائع کرنا ہے ،مگر اس سے فقیر کی حاجت دفع ہوتی ہے، اور یہ اچھی چیز ہے تو اس کی وجہ سے زکوۃ میں حسن آیا، اور یہ واسطہ یعنی فقیر کی حاجت اللہ نے پیدا کی ہے، فقیر کا اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔
اسی طرح روزہ بظا ہر نفس کو بھوکا رکھنا ہے، اس میں کوئی حسن نہیں ہے، البتہ اس سے نفس امارہ مغلوب ہوتا ہے اس واسطہ سے حسن آیا ۔ اور یہ واسطہ یعنی نفس کی عداوت اللہ نے پیدا کی ہے، بندہ کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح حج بظاہر لمبا سفر کرنا ، اپنے آپ کو تھکانا، متفرق مقامات کو دیکھنا ہے جس میں کوئی خوبی نہیں ہے، البتہ حج میں مکان کے شرف یعنی بیت اللہ کے شرف کے سبب حسن آیا اور یہ واسطہ اللہ کے پیدا کرنے سے ہے بندہ کا اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ الغرض زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج میں حسن ایک واسطہ سے آیا ہے، اور تینوں جگہ وہ واسطہ اللہ کے پیدا کرنے سے ہوا ہے اور وہ واسطہ اللہ کی طرف ہی منسوب ہے، بندہ کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے تو گویا وہ واسطہ درمیان میں ہے ہی نہیں ، لہذا زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج بھی قسم اول یعنی حسن لعینہ بالذات کے ساتھ ملحق ہو گئے، اسی لئے مصنف نے نے کہا وما التحق بواسطة بما كان المعنی فی وضعہ اور دوسری قسم وہ ہے جو واسطہ کے ساتھ ملحق ہواسی ( پہلی قسم کے ساتھ جس کی ذات میں وہ معنی ہے۔
وَحُكْمُ هَذَيْنِ النَّوْعَيْنِ وَاحِدٌ وَهُوَانَ الْوُجُوْبَ مَتى ثَبَتَ لَا يَسْقُطُ إِلَّا بِفِعْلِ الْوَاجِب أَوْ بِاعْتِرَاضِ مَا يُسْقِطْهُ بِعَيْنِهِ وَالَّذِى حَسَنٌ لِمَعْنَّي فِي غَيْرِهِ نَوْعَانِ مَا يَحْصُلُ الْمَعْنَى بَعْدَهُ بِفِعْلٍ مَقْصُودٍ كَالْوَضُوْءِ وَالسَّعِى إِلَى الْجُمْعَةِ وَمَا يَحْصُلُ الْمَعْنَى بِفِعْلِ الْمَامُؤرِيهِ كَالصَّلوةِ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ وَالْجِهَادِ وَإِقَامَةِ الْحُدُودِ فَإِنَّ مَا فِيْهِ الْحُسْنُ مِنْ قَضَاءِ حَقَّ الْمُسْلِمِ وَكَبْتِ أَعْدَاءِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَالأَجْرِعَنِ الْمَعَاصِي يَحْصُلُ بِنَفْسِ الْفِعْلِ وَحُكْمَ هَذَيْنِ النَّوْعَيْنِ وَاحِدٌ أَيْضًا وَهُوَ بَقَاءَ الْوَاجِبِ بِوُجُوبِ الْغَيْرِ وَسْقُوْطُهُ بِسُقُوْطِ الْغَيْرِ ترجمہ : ۔ اور ان دونوں قسموں کا حکم ایک ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ واجب جب ثابت ہو جائے گا تو وہ ساقط نہ ہو گا مگر واجب کو ادا کرنے سے ، یا اس عارض کے پیش آنے سے جو بذات خود واجب کو ساقط کر دے، اور وہ مامور بہ جوحسن ہے ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے جو اس کے غیر میں ہے دو قسم پر ہے، (۱) ایک یہ کہ وہ معنی اس ( مامور بہ کو کرنے ) کے بعد فعل
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi: Explanation in Urdu of Al-Muntakhab Al-Husami. ... Goodness without any third meaning (i.e., without any extra intermediary) due to these intermediaries being established from the creation of Allah and being attributed to Allah. Elucidation: This is a section on describing the goodness of the commanded act. The commander is Allah, and the prohibition is also from Allah, and Allah is Wise. His wisdom requires that whatever He commands His servants indeed has goodness in that commanded act, and whatever He prohibits has evil in that prohibited act. The author is dividing the commanded act from the perspective of goodness. According to goodness, the commanded act is of two types: (1) commanded act good in itself (hasan li-aynihi) and (2) commanded act good due to something else (hasan li-ghayrihi). Hasan li-aynihi means that the goodness is in the essence of the commanded act. Hasan li-ghayrihi means that there is no intrinsic goodness in the commanded act; goodness came from something else. Then hasan li-aynihi is also of two types: (1) hasan li-aynihi bi-al-dhat (good in itself by essence) and (2) hasan li-aynihi bi-al-wasita (good in itself through an intermediary). Hasan bi-al-dhat means that the attribute or meaning by which goodness arises in the commanded act is in itself good without any intermediary; its very nature is good. And hasan bi-al-wasita means that the attribute or meaning by which goodness arises in the commanded act is not good in its nature, but goodness came to it through an intermediary, but this intermediary is not something very distant; rather it is at the level of non-existence, so this second type is attached to the first type. The example of the first type (hasan bi-al-dhat) is prayer (salat), because the meaning and attribute by which goodness comes to prayer is such that goodness is in its essence and nature, because prayer is a name for statements (like recitation, tasbih, etc.) and actions (like ruku, sujud, etc.), so goodness comes to prayer through these actions and statements, and these actions and statements are good in their nature because their purpose is to glorify the Most High, and glorification is good in itself. Hence prayer is hasan li-aynihi bi-al-dhat. Faith (iman) is also included in this first type; indeed faith is the highest degree of the first type, because faith never accepts invalidation, while prayer sometimes becomes invalidated. For this reason, some scholars have divided this first type into (1) what does not accept invalidation like iman, and (2) what accepts invalidation like salat, except that glorification is good in itself, but if it is in an improper state or time, such as in a state of major impurity instead of purification, or at improper times like disliked times, then it will not be good but rather ugly and disliked. 'And what is attached through an intermediary': The first type has been explained. The second type is that which is attached to the first type due to an intermediary, such as zakat, fasting, and hajj. Zakat outwardly has no goodness because it involves wasting wealth, but it fulfills the need of the poor, and that is good, so goodness comes to zakat through that. And this intermediary (the need of the poor) is created by Allah; the poor has no role in it. Similarly, fasting outwardly is starving oneself; there is no goodness in it, but it overcomes the commanding self (nafs ammara); through this intermediary goodness comes. And this intermediary (opposition to the self) is created by Allah; the servant has no role. Similarly, hajj outwardly is a long journey, exhausting oneself, seeing different places; there is no virtue in it, but in hajj, goodness comes due to the honor of the place (i.e., the honor of the House of Allah), and this intermediary is by Allah's creation; the servant has no role. In short, goodness in zakat, fasting, and hajj comes through an intermediary, and in all three cases that intermediary is created by Allah and attributed to Allah; the servant has no role, so that intermediary is as if it does not exist. Hence zakat, fasting, and hajj are also attached to the first type (hasan li-aynihi bi-al-dhat). Therefore the author said: 'And what is attached through an intermediary because the meaning is in its nature' and the second type is that which is attached through an intermediary to the first type whose essence has that meaning. 'And the ruling of these two types is one, and it is that when obligation is established, it does not fall except by performing the wajib or by the occurrence of something that removes it by itself. And that which is good due to a meaning in something else is of two types: (1) that in which the meaning is obtained after a purposeful action, like ablution and going to Friday prayer, and (2) that in which the meaning is obtained by the action of the commanded person, like prayer over the deceased, jihad, and establishment of hadd punishments; for that in which the goodness lies in fulfilling the right of a Muslim, subduing the enemies of Allah, and preventing sins is obtained by the action itself. And the ruling of these two types is also one, and it is that the wajib remains with the obligation of the other and falls with the falling of the other.' Translation: And the ruling of both these types is one, and that is that when the wajib is established, it will not be void except by performing the wajib or by the occurrence of that which by itself voids the wajib. And the commanded act that is good due to a meaning that is in something other than it is of two types: (1) one is that the meaning comes after the act, like wudu and going to Friday prayer, and (2) the other is that the meaning comes with the act of the commanded person, like prayer over the dead, jihad, and establishment of hadd punishments. So the goodness in these from fulfilling the right of a Muslim, subduing the enemies of Allah, and deterring from sins comes by the act itself. And the ruling of these two types is also one: the wajib remains with the obligation of the other and falls with the falling of the other.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the commanded act (ma'mur bih) from the perspective of its goodness (husn). The author begins by stating that Allah, being Wise, only commands what has goodness and prohibits what has evil. The commanded act is then divided into two primary categories: (1) that which is good in itself (hasan li-aynihi) and (2) that which is good due to something external (hasan li-ghayrihi). The first category is further subdivided into two: (a) good by essence (hasan bi-al-dhat), where the quality causing goodness is intrinsically good—the example given is salat, whose components (recitation, ruku, sujud) are all acts of glorification, which is good per se; (b) good through an intermediary (hasan bi-al-wasita), where the quality is not intrinsically good but becomes good through a close intermediary that is almost nonexistent, such as zakat, fasting, and hajj. In these acts, the apparent action (spending money, starving, traveling) is not inherently good, but the underlying purpose (relieving the poor, subduing the nafs, honoring the House of Allah) is good, and these purposes are created by Allah, not by the servant, so they are effectively considered as part of the goodness of the act itself. The author then states that both subcategories of hasan li-aynihi share the same ruling: the obligation remains until the act is performed or a specific invalidating cause occurs. Next, the passage turns to the second major category: the commanded act that is good due to a meaning in something else (hasan li-ghayrihi). This is divided into two types: (1) where the good meaning is obtained after a purposeful external act (e.g., wudu is a means to prayer, rushing to Friday prayer is a means to attend); (2) where the good meaning is obtained by the commanded act itself (e.g., funeral prayer fulfills the right of the deceased, jihad subdues enemies, hadd punishments deter sin). The ruling for both types is that the obligation of these acts remains as long as the external purpose remains obligatory; if that purpose falls, the act's obligation also falls. Throughout, the commentary clarifies the intricate distinctions in Hanafi usul regarding the nature of goodness in divine commands.

Key Terms
حسن لعينه (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi): The commanded act whose goodness is in its very essence, not dependent on anything else.
حسن لغيره (ḥasan li-ghayrihi): The commanded act that becomes good due to a meaning or purpose external to itself.
حسن لعينه بالذات (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi bi al-dhāt): Goodness is intrinsic to the act's essence, e.g., salat because its components are acts of glorification.
حسن لعينه بالواسطة (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi bi al-wāsiṭa): Goodness comes through an intermediary that is so close it is considered as intrinsic; e.g., zakat, fasting, hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a commanded act that is good in itself by essence (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi bi al-dhāt)?
A) Zakat
B) Fasting
C) Prayer (Salat)
D) Wudu

Key Takeaway
Commanded acts are classified by the source of their goodness: intrinsic (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi) or derived (ḥasan li-ghayrihi), and this classification determines how their obligation is maintained.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Two Main Categories of Obligatory Acts: Intrinsic Goodness vs. Derived Goodness
Classifies obligations by source of goodness and explains their rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the Hanafi classification of obligatory acts based on husn, and apply the ruling that obligations drop only by performance or a specific obstacle.

Core Idea
Intrinsic goodness and goodness through an intermediary both yield obligations that cannot drop except by performance or a specific obstacle.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, obligations are not all alike; the source of their goodness affects how they are ruled. This lesson unpacks the classification of wajib based on husn (goodness), distinguishing acts good in themselves from those good due to an intermediary or an external meaning. Understanding this helps you grasp why some obligations like wudu are contingent on others, while acts like iman are permanently binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary categories
The text distinguishes between acts that are good in themselves (husn li-aynihi, e.g., iman) and acts that are good due to a meaning in something else (husn li-ghayrihi). Note that the first category also includes acts whose goodness comes through an intermediary solely from Allah, effectively merging them.
The intermediary (wasta) must be from Allah alone for the act to join the first category.
2
Understand the role of the intermediary (wasta)
For acts like zakat, fasting, and hajj, the goodness arises from an intermediary created by Allah (e.g., the poor's need subduing the soul). Since the servant has no role, these are treated as intrinsically good. Identify the intermediary for each act as mentioned.
This is a key Hanafi nuance: acts are not intrinsically good if the intermediary involves human choice.
3
Analyze the two subtypes of husn li-ghayrihi
Husn li-ghayrihi has two types: (a) the good meaning is achieved by a separate intended act after the commanded act (e.g., wudu enables prayer, which is a separate act), and (b) the good meaning is achieved by the commanded act itself (e.g., janazah prayer fulfills the right of the Muslim directly).
In type (a), the obligation of the intermediary act remains until the main act is performed.
4
Apply the ruling for each category
For the first category (including acts joined by an intermediary), the ruling is: once established, the obligation does not drop except by performing the act or by a specific obstacle (e.g., menstruation for prayer). For the second category, the ruling is: the obligation remains as long as the other (the underlying good) remains obligatory, and drops when the other drops (e.g., wudu is obligatory only when prayer is obligatory).
This ruling is derived from the text's statement about the two types of husn li-ghayrihi.

ہے، جیسے زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج ، زکوۃ میں بظاہر کوئی حسن نہیں ہے کیونکہ زکوۃ میں مال کو ضائع کرنا ہے ،مگر اس سے فقیر کی حاجت دفع ہوتی ہے، اور یہ اچھی چیز ہے تو اس کی وجہ سے زکوۃ میں حسن آیا، اور یہ واسطہ یعنی فقیر کی حاجت اللہ نے پیدا کی ہے، فقیر کا اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔
اسی طرح روزہ بظا ہر نفس کو بھوکا رکھنا ہے، اس میں کوئی حسن نہیں ہے، البتہ اس سے نفس امارہ مغلوب ہوتا ہے اس واسطہ سے حسن آیا ۔ اور یہ واسطہ یعنی نفس کی عداوت اللہ نے پیدا کی ہے، بندہ کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح حج بظاہر لمبا سفر کرنا ، اپنے آپ کو تھکانا، متفرق مقامات کو دیکھنا ہے جس میں کوئی خوبی نہیں ہے، البتہ حج میں مکان کے شرف یعنی بیت اللہ کے شرف کے سبب حسن آیا اور یہ واسطہ اللہ کے پیدا کرنے سے ہے بندہ کا اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ الغرض زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج میں حسن ایک واسطہ سے آیا ہے، اور تینوں جگہ وہ واسطہ اللہ کے پیدا کرنے سے ہوا ہے اور وہ واسطہ اللہ کی طرف ہی منسوب ہے، بندہ کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے تو گویا وہ واسطہ درمیان میں ہے ہی نہیں ، لہذا زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج بھی قسم اول یعنی حسن لعینہ بالذات کے ساتھ ملحق ہو گئے، اسی لئے مصنف نے نے کہا وما التحق بواسطة بما كان المعنی فی وضعہ اور دوسری قسم وہ ہے جو واسطہ کے ساتھ ملحق ہواسی ( پہلی قسم کے ساتھ جس کی ذات میں وہ معنی ہے۔
وَحُكْمُ هَذَيْنِ النَّوْعَيْنِ وَاحِدٌ وَهُوَانَ الْوُجُوْبَ مَتى ثَبَتَ لَا يَسْقُطُ إِلَّا بِفِعْلِ الْوَاجِب أَوْ بِاعْتِرَاضِ مَا يُسْقِطْهُ بِعَيْنِهِ وَالَّذِى حَسَنٌ لِمَعْنِّي فِي غَيْرِهِ نَوْعَانِ مَا يَحُصُلُ الْمَعْنَى بَعْدَهُ بِفِعْلٍ مَقْصُودٍ كَالْوَضُوْءِ وَالسَّعِى إِلَى الْجُمْعَةِ وَمَا يَحْصُلُ الْمَعْنَى بِفِعْلِ الْمَامُؤرِيهِ كَالصَّلوةِ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ وَالْجِهَادِ وَإِقَامَةِ الْحُدُودِ فَإِنَّ مَا فِيْهِ الْحُسْنُ مِنْ قَضَاءِ حَقَّ الْمُسْلِمِ وَكَبْتِ أَعْدَاءِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَالأَجْرِعَنِ الْمَعَاصِي يَحْصُلُ بِنَفْسِ الْفِعْلِ وَحُكْمَ هَذَيْنِ النَّوْعَيْنِ وَاحِدٌ أَيْضًا وَهُوَ بَقَاءَ الْوَاجِبِ بِوُجُوبِ الْغَيْرِ وَسْقُوْطُهُ بِسُقُوْطِ الْغَيْرِ ترجمہ : ۔ اور ان دونوں قسموں کا حکم ایک ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ واجب جب ثابت ہو جائے گا تو وہ ساقط نہ ہو گا مگر واجب کو ادا کرنے سے ، یا اس عارض کے پیش آنے سے جو بذات خود واجب کو ساقط کر دے، اور وہ مامور بہ جوحسن ہے ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے جو اس کے غیر میں ہے دو قسم پر ہے، (۱) ایک یہ کہ وہ معنی اس ( مامور بہ کو کرنے ) کے بعد فعل مقصود سے حاصل ہو جیسے وضو اور سعی الی الجمعہ ، (۲) اور دوسری قسم وہ کہ وہ معنی حاصل ہو جائے مامور بہ کو کرنے سے جیسے میت پر نماز پڑھنا، اور جہاد اور حدود قائم کرنا پس بیشک وہ معنی جس میں حسن ہے یعنی مسلمان کا حق ادا کرنا ، اللہ کے دشمنوں کو ذلیل کرنا اور معاصی سے روکنا نفس فعل سے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے، اور ان دو قسموں کا حکم بھی ایک ہے اور وہ واجب کا باقی رہنا ہے غیر کے ثابت رہنے سے اور واجب کا ساقط ہونا ہے غیر کے سقوط سے۔ تشریح:- مصنف یہ پہلی دو قسموں کا حکم بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ حسن لعینہ اور جوحسن لعینہ کے ساتھ کسی واسطہ سے ملحق ہے، ان دونوں قسموں کا حکم یہ ہے کہ واجب جب ثابت ہو جائے گا تو یا تو اس کے ادا کرنے سے ساقط ہوگا یا کوئی ایسا عارض پیش آجائے جو بغیر کسی واسطہ کے بذات خود اس واجب کو ساقط کر دے جیسے حیض ونفاس، اس کے پیش آنے سے نماز ساقط ہو جائے گی ، یہ بذات خود بغیر کسی واسطہ کے نماز کو ساقط کر دیتا ہے، اور جنون مطبق یہ نماز روزہ ، حج اور زکوۃ سب کو ساقط کر دیتا ہے۔ والذى حسن المعنى - مصنف اللہ حسن لعینہ کو بیان کرنے کے بعد اب حسن لغیرہ کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، حسن لغیرہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ مامور بہ میں حسن ذاتی نہ ہو کسی غیر کی وجہ سے حسن آیا ہو، اس کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں، (۱) ایک وہ جس میں وہ غیر جس کی وجہ سے مامور بہ میں حسن آیا ہے، وہ مامور بہ کو ادا کرنے سے ادا نہ ہو بلکہ مامور بہ کو ادا کرنے کے بعد اس کو مستقل ادا کرنا پڑے جیسے وضو اور سعی الی الجمعہ، وضو میں ذاتی حسن نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ تو پانی ضائع کرنا ہے، البتہ نماز کا وسیلہ ہونے سے حسن آیا ہے، اور نماز جس کی وجہ سے وضو میں حُسن آیا ہے یہ وضو کے ادا کرنے سے ادا نہیں ہوتی ہے بلکہ وضو کے بعد مستقلاً ادا کرنا پڑتا ہے۔۔ اسی طرح سعی الی الجمعہ میں بذات خود کوئی حُسن نہیں ہے بلکہ نماز جمعہ کی وجہ سے حسن آیا ہے، اور نماز جمعہ سعی سے ادا نہیں ہوتی ہے بلکہ اس کو مستقلاً ادا کرنا پڑتا ہے۔ (۲) حسن لغیرہ کی دوسری قسم وہ ہے کہ جس میں وہ غیر جس کی وجہ سے مامور بہ میں حسن آیا ہے وہ مامور بہ کو ادا کرنے سے ادا ہو جائے اس کے لئے مستقلاً عمل نہ کرنا پڑے، جیسے میت پر نماز ، اس میں ذاتی محسن نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تو بت پرستی کے مشابہ ہے، مگر اس سے مسلمان کے حق کی ادائیگی ہوتی ہے ،اس کی وجہ سے حسن آیا ہے، اور ادائے حق مسلم صلوۃ علی المیت سے ادا ہو جاتا ہے ، اس کے لئے الگ سے کوئی عمل کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور جیسے جہاد اس میں ذاتی حسن نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ اس میں اللہ کے بندوں کو عذاب دینا اور شہروں کو اجاڑنا ہے، مگر اعلاء کلمتہ اللہ کی وجہ سے اس میں حسن آیا ہے، اور اعلاء کلمتہ اللہ نفس جہاد سے ادا ہوجاتا ہے، کوئی الگ عمل کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، اسی طرح حدود قائم کرنا، حد زنا، حد سرقہ وغیرہ اس میں فی نفسہ عذاب دینا ہے، کوئی خوبی نہیں ہے ، مگر اس سے گناہوں کی روک تھام ہو جاتی ہے، اس کی وجہ سے حسن آیا، اور گناہوں کی روک تھام حد قائم کرنے
like zakat, fasting and hajj; in zakat apparently there is no goodness because in zakat one is wasting wealth, but through it the need of the poor is fulfilled, and this is a good thing, so due to that goodness came into zakat, and this intermediary i.e. the need of the poor Allah created, the poor has no role in it. Similarly fasting apparently is keeping the soul hungry, there is no goodness in it, but through it the commanding soul is subdued, due to this intermediary goodness came. And this intermediary i.e. the enmity of the soul Allah created, the servant has no role. Similarly hajj apparently is making a long journey, tiring oneself, seeing various places, in which there is no virtue, but in hajj due to the honor of the place i.e. the honor of the House of Allah goodness came, and this intermediary is from Allah's creation, the servant has no role in it. In short, in zakat, fasting and hajj goodness came through an intermediary, and in all three places that intermediary came from Allah's creation and that intermediary is attributed to Allah, the servant has no role, so as if that intermediary does not exist, therefore zakat, fasting and hajj also joined the first category i.e. goodness in itself; therefore the author said: "And what joined by an intermediary is like what the meaning is in its placement." And the second type is that which joins by an intermediary to the first type which has that meaning in its essence. And the ruling of these two types is one, and it is: obligation when established does not drop except by performing the obligatory act or by the occurrence of something that drops it by itself. And that which is good due to a meaning in something else is of two types: (1) that the meaning occurs after it by a separate intended act, like ablution and walking to Friday prayer, and (2) that the meaning occurs by the act of the commanded person itself, like praying over the deceased and Jihad and establishing prescribed punishments; for the goodness in it of fulfilling the right of a Muslim, subduing the enemies of Allah Almighty, and preventing sins occurs by the act itself. And the ruling of these two types is also one, and it is: the obligation remains with the obligation of the other, and it drops with the dropping of the other. Translation: And the ruling of these two types is one, and it is that when obligation is established, it will not drop except by performing the wajib, or by the occurrence of an obstacle that drops the wajib by itself. And the commanded act that is good due to a meaning in something else is of two types: (1) one is that the meaning is obtained after it by a intended act like wudu and walking to jumu'ah, (2) and the second type is that the meaning is obtained by performing the commanded act like praying over the deceased, and jihad, and establishing hudud; so indeed that meaning in which there is goodness i.e. fulfilling the right of the Muslim, humiliating the enemies of Allah, and preventing sins is obtained by the act itself. And the ruling of these two types is also one, and it is: the obligation remains as long as the other remains and the obligation drops by the dropping of the other. Explanation: The author is stating the ruling of the first two types that the ruling of husn li-'aynihi and what joins with husn li-'aynihi through some intermediary is that when the obligation is established, then either it will drop by performing it or some obstacle occurs that without any intermediary by itself drops that obligation, like menstruation and postnatal bleeding, by their occurrence prayer drops, they by themselves without any intermediary drop prayer, and continuous insanity drops prayer, fasting, hajj and zakat all. And that which is good due to a meaning - the author after explaining husn li-'aynihi is now explaining husn li-ghayrihi; husn li-ghayrihi is called that the commanded act does not have intrinsic goodness, goodness came due to something else; it also has two types: (1) one is that the other due to which goodness came into the commanded act is not fulfilled by performing the commanded act, rather after performing the commanded act it must be performed separately, like wudu and walking to jumu'ah; wudu has no intrinsic goodness, rather it is wasting water, but it has goodness due to being a means to prayer; and prayer due to which goodness came into wudu is not fulfilled by performing wudu, rather after wudu it must be performed separately. Similarly walking to jumu'ah has no goodness in itself, rather goodness came due to Friday prayer, and Friday prayer is not fulfilled by walking, rather it must be performed separately. (2) The second type of husn li-ghayrihi is that the other due to which goodness came into the commanded act is fulfilled by performing the commanded act, no separate act is needed for it, like praying over the deceased; it has no intrinsic goodness, rather it resembles idol worship, but through it the right of the Muslim is fulfilled, due to that goodness came; and the fulfillment of the Muslim's right is achieved by salat al-mayyit, no separate act is needed. And like jihad, it has no intrinsic goodness, because in it there is punishing Allah's servants and destroying cities, but due to raising the word of Allah goodness came into it, and raising the word of Allah is achieved by jihad itself, no separate act is needed. Similarly establishing hudud, hadd for zina, hadd for theft etc., in itself it is punishing, no virtue, but through it prevention of sins occurs, due to that goodness came, and prevention of sins is by establishing hadd...
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Husami discusses the classification of obligatory acts (wajibat) based on the source of their goodness (husn). The author distinguishes between two primary categories: (1) Acts that are good in themselves (husn li-'aynihi), such as faith (iman), where the goodness is intrinsic. (2) Acts that are good due to an intermediary (wasta) created by Allah, but since the intermediary is entirely from Allah and the servant has no role, these acts are effectively treated as having intrinsic goodness and join the first category. Examples given are zakat, fasting, and hajj. The ruling for both these categories is the same: once an obligation is established, it does not drop except by performing the act or by the occurrence of a specific obstacle that nullifies the obligation, such as menstruation for prayer or continuous insanity for all obligations. The author then introduces a separate category: acts that are good due to a meaning in something else (husn li-ghayrihi). These are acts that have no intrinsic goodness but become good because they serve as means to a good end. This category is further subdivided into two types: (a) The good meaning is achieved only after performing a separate intended act, such as wudu (which is a means to prayer) or walking to Friday prayer (which is a means to the Friday prayer itself). In these cases, the obligation of wudu or walking remains even after the act, because the intended good (prayer) is not yet fulfilled. (b) The good meaning is achieved directly by the act itself, such as praying over the deceased (which fulfills the right of the Muslim), jihad (which raises the word of Allah), and establishing hudud (which prevents sins). Here, the good is realized immediately upon performing the act, so no separate act is needed. The ruling for these two subtypes is also the same: the obligation remains as long as the other (the good meaning) remains obligatory, and it drops when the other drops. For example, wudu is obligatory as long as prayer is obligatory; if prayer becomes non-obligatory (e.g., due to menstruation), wudu also drops. The passage emphasizes the nuanced Hanafi understanding of how obligations relate to their underlying purposes.

Key Terms
حسن لعینہ (ḥusn li-ʿaynihi): Goodness intrinsic to the act itself, such as faith (īmān), not dependent on anything else.
حسن لغیرہ (ḥusn li-ghayrihi): Goodness that comes to an act due to something else external to it, such as wuḍū’ being good because it enables prayer.
واسطہ (wāsiṭah): An intermediary created by Allah that brings goodness to an act, like the need of the poor for zakat or the subduing of the soul for fasting.
واجب (wājib): An obligatory act that is established and can only drop by performance or a specific obstacle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling for the first two categories (husn li-aynihi and acts joined by an intermediary)?
A) They drop only by performing the wajib
B) They drop either by performing the wajib or by an obstacle that specifically drops the obligation
C) They never drop and remain obligatory forever
D) They drop when the reason for obligation ceases

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of wajib based on husn reveals that obligations are either intrinsically good (or effectively so) and drop only by performance or obstacle, or derivatively good and contingent on the underlying good they serve.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Classification of Prohibited Acts (Nahy) in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the division of prohibited acts by inherent vs. incidental badness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a prohibited act as qabih li-aynihi or qabih li-ghayrihi, apply the corresponding ruling (invalid vs valid but sinful), and explain the Hanafi basis for this distinction.

Core Idea
An act prohibited in itself (qabih li-aynihi) is invalid; an act prohibited due to an external factor (qabih li-ghayrihi) remains valid but sinful.

Prohibition (nahy) in Islamic law does not always render an act invalid. The Hanafi school distinguishes between acts that are inherently bad and those that become bad due to an external factor. This classification determines whether the act is legally accepted or completely void. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying rulings to cases like prayer in a usurped place or sale during the Friday call.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of badness
Read the passage and note that acts prohibited by the Shari'ah are divided into 'qabih li-aynihi' (bad in itself) and 'qabih li-ghayrihi' (bad due to something else).
This mirrors the division of commands into husn (goodness).
2
Subdivide each category
Qabih li-aynihi includes natural badness (e.g., kufr) and legal badness due to lack of capacity/suitability (e.g., prayer of a person without wudu). Qabih li-ghayrihi includes cases where the external meaning overtakes the act collectively (jam'an) or attaches as a description (wasfan).
Examples: jam'an – sale during Friday call; wasfan – not fully elaborated but mentioned.
3
Determine the ruling for each category
For qabih li-aynihi, the ruling is that the act is 'ghayru mashru' aslan' (not legislated at all – invalid). For qabih li-ghayrihi, the act remains 'sahih mashru' ba'da al-nahi' (valid and legally accepted despite the prohibition).
This is a key Hanafi position: the prohibition does not invalidate the act's essential structure.
4
Apply to the examples given
Examine the examples: prayer without wudu (qabih li-aynihi) is invalid; sale during Friday call (qabih li-ghayrihi) is valid but sinful. Intercourse during menstruation is valid for legal effects (e.g., remarrying first husband, establishing ihsan).
Note the practical difference: validity for ihsan and marriage dissolution.
5
Contrast with other schools (optional extension)
Consider that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that prohibition necessarily invalidates the act. The Hanafi view relies on a nuanced understanding of the relationship between the prohibition (nahy) and the act's essential elements.
This is not in the passage but helps contextualize.

فَصْلٌ فِي النَّهْي وَهُوَ فِي صِفَةِ الْقُبْحِ يَنْقَسِمُ انْقِسَامَ الْأَمْرِ فِي صِفَةِ الْحُسْنِ مَا قَبُحَ لِعَيْنِهِ وَضْعًا كَالْكُفْرِ وَالْعَبْثِ وَمَا الْتَحَقَ بِهِ بِوَاسِطَةِ عَدَمِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ وَالْمَحَلِيَّةِ شَرْعًا كَصَلَاةِ الْمُحْدِثِ وَبَيْعِ الْحُرِّ وَالْمَضَامِينِ وَالْمَلَاقِيحِ وَحُكْمُ النَّهْيِ فِيهِمَا بَيَانُ أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعٍ أَصْلًا وَمَا قَبُحَ لِمَعْنًى فِي غَيْرِهِ وَهُوَ نَوْعَانِ مَا جَاوَزَهُ الْمَعْنَى جَمْعًا كَالْبَيْعِ وَقْتَ النِّدَاءِ وَالصَّلَاةِ فِي الْأَرْضِ الْمَغْصُوبَةِ وَالْوَطْءِ فِي حَالَةِ الْحَيْضِ وَحُكْمُهُ أَنَّهُ يَكُونُ صَحِيحًا مَشْرُوعًا بَعْدَ النَّهْيِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا إِنَّ وَطْأَهَا فِي حَالَةِ الْحَيْضِ يُحَلِّلُهَا لِلزَّوْجِ الْأَوَّلِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِهِ إِحْصَانُ الْوَاطِئِ وَمَا اتَّصَلَ بِهِ الْمَعْنَى وَصْفًا
A section on prohibition: it, in terms of the attribute of badness, divides like the division of command in terms of the attribute of goodness. That which is bad in itself by way of disposition, like disbelief and futility; and that which is attached to it due to the absence of legal capacity or suitability, like the prayer of one in a state of ritual impurity, and the sale of a free person, and the sale of 'madaamin' (the contents of a male's loin) and 'malaqeeh' (the fetuses in female camels). The ruling of prohibition in both is a statement that it is not legislated at all. And that which is bad due to a meaning in something else, and it is two types: (1) what the meaning overtakes collectively, like sale at the time of the call for Friday prayer, prayer in usurped land, and intercourse during menstruation; its ruling is that it is valid and legally accepted despite the prohibition, and for this we say that intercourse with her during menstruation makes her permissible for the first husband and establishes the chastity of the one who had intercourse. (2) and that to which the meaning attaches as a description.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Husami explains the Hanafi classification of prohibited acts (manhiyyaat). The author begins by stating that prohibition, like command, is divided according to the attribute of badness (qubh). Two main categories are distinguished: (a) that which is bad by itself (qabih li-aynihi) and (b) that which is bad due to an external meaning (qabih li-ghayrihi). The first is further subdivided into wad'i (natural/dispositional) and shar'i (legal). Natural badness is recognized by reason, e.g., kufr (disbelief) and abath (futile actions). Legal badness arises from the absence of legal capacity (ahliyya) or suitability (mahalliyya) as determined by Shari'ah, e.g., the prayer of a person without wudu (invalid due to absence of ritual purity), the sale of a free person (not a valid commodity), and the sale of madaamin and malaqeeh (uncertain items). These prohibited acts are completely invalid and not legislated. The second category (qabih li-ghayrihi) involves acts that are valid in themselves but become prohibited due to an external factor. This has two subtypes: (i) where the external factor is combined with the act, e.g., sale during the Friday call to prayer (sale valid but sinful), prayer in usurped land (prayer valid but usurpation sinful), and intercourse during menstruation (valid in that it dissolves the previous marriage or establishes ihsaans); (ii) where the external factor attaches as a description. The ruling for these acts is that they are valid despite the prohibition.

Key Terms
قَبِيحٌ لِعَيْنِهِ (qabīḥ li-ʿaynihī): An act that is bad in itself, either by nature (disposition) or by legal determination due to lack of capacity/suitability.
قَبِيحٌ لِغَيْرِهِ (qabīḥ li-ghayrihī): An act that is not inherently bad but becomes prohibited due to an external factor, either combined (jam'an) or as a description (wasfan).
مَضَامِين (maḍāmīn): The contents of a male's loin (semen) when sold as part of a future offspring; considered invalid due to uncertainty.
مَلَاقِيح (malāqīḥ): The fetuses in female camels when sold before birth; considered invalid due to absence of ascertainable commodities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of the prohibition in the case of 'qabih li-ghayrihi' acts?
A) The act is invalid and not legislated at all.
B) The act is valid and legally accepted despite the prohibition.
C) The act is invalid only if the external factor is described.
D) The act is valid only if the prohibition is not known.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul distinguishes between acts prohibited in themselves (invalid) and acts prohibited due to external factors (valid but sinful), a crucial difference for determining legal effects.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
15 min
Two Types of Qabih li-Ghayrihi: Mujawiran vs Wasfan
Classifies prohibited acts due to external cause into two subtypes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qabih li-ghayrihi mujawiran and wasfan, and apply the correct ruling to each type.

Core Idea
A prohibition due to an adjacent cause leaves the act valid; an inherent cause voids it.

Not all prohibitions have the same legal effect. In Hanafi usul, the key lies in whether the prohibited act's evil stems from itself (qabih li-dhatihi) or from an external factor (qabih li-ghayrihi). This lesson unpacks the latter category, showing how the nature of the external cause—whether adjacent or inherent—determines if the act remains valid or becomes void.

Guided Path
1
Understand qabih li-ghayrihi
Recognize that in this category, the act itself is not evil; the evil is introduced by an external factor (ghayr). The act would be permissible without that factor.
Contrast with qabih li-dhatihi where the act is inherently evil (e.g., kufr).
2
Distinguish adjacency vs inherent description
Two subtypes based on how the external factor relates to the act: mujawiran (adjacent – the factor can be present or absent independently) and wasfan (inherent – the factor is an inseparable attribute of the act).
Mujawiran: the external cause is like a companion; wasfan: it is an inseparable trait.
3
Identify examples of each subtype
From the passage, assign each example to its subtype: sale during Friday adhan, prayer in usurped land, and intercourse during menstruation are mujawiran; fasid sale and fasting on Eid are wasfan.
Confirm why each example fits: e.g., the disruption of Friday prayer is not an essential part of the sale.
4
State the ruling for each subtype
For mujawiran, the act remains valid (sahih) but is makruh due to the external evil. For wasfan, the act is invalid (fasid) because the evil is inseparable.
Consequences: for mujawiran, ownership transfers (sale), prayer is valid, ihsan is established; for wasfan, no benefit is recognized.
5
Extract the legal principle
Formulate: A prohibition due to a non-inherent attribute does not nullify the act; only a prohibition due to an inherent attribute does.
This principle is used in further istinbat.
